Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer
Explains the preferred order of rows in congregation and the ruling on filling gaps.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred order of rows in congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
The Hanafi row order is men, boys, khunathas, women — based on proximity to the imam reflecting maturity and understanding.

The arrangement of rows in congregational prayer is not arbitrary; it follows a specific order derived from the Prophet's guidance. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on who should stand where and why, supported by key hadiths. You will also learn the related rulings on filling gaps and aligning shoulders.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred row order
State the sequence: men (front row), then discerning boys, then khunathas (hermaphrodites), then women (back rows). This is the mufta bihi position.
The order is sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Find the hadith 'Let those of you who are mature and prudent be near me' (ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهى). Understand how it indicates priority by proximity.
The imperative form suggests strong recommendation.
3
Analyze the reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
Recognize that 'mature and prudent' refers to men with understanding and responsibility. Boys and khunathas are less mature, so they stand further. Women are last.
The hadith also implies that the imam's row is the most honorable.
4
Understand the inclusion of khunathas
Khunathas (ambiguous gender) are placed between boys and women because they are not fully male nor female in Hanafi fiqh.
This is a distinct Hanafi position; other madhhabs may not separately categorize them.
5
Apply the rules for filling gaps and aligning shoulders
The passage also instructs to stand close (tarassu), fill gaps, and align shoulders. If the first row has a gap, someone from the second row may move forward. The imam should stand in the middle of his row.
These rulings are based on multiple hadiths quoted in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصف الرجال: أي صف الرجال مقدم على صف الصبيان وهو مقدم على صف الخناثي، وهو مقدم على صف النساء؛ لقوله : "ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهى". [ تبيين الحقائق: ٣٥٠/١] وينبغي للقوم أن يتراصوا ويسدوا الخلل ويسووا بين مناكبهم في الصفوف، ولا بأس أن يأمرهم الإمام بذلك لقوله عليه: "سووا صفوفكم؛ فإن تسوية الصفوف من تمام الصلاة"، وقال علي: لتسون صفوفكم أو ليخالفن الله بين وجوهكم" وهو راجع إلى اختلاف القلوب، وينبغي للإمام أن يقف بإزاء الوسط فإن لم يفعل فقد أساء، وينبغي أن يكملوا الصف الأول حتى إذا وجد فرجة فيه دون الثاني له أن يخرق الثاني؛ إذ لا حرمة لهم لتقصيرهم حيث لم يسدوا الصف الأول ثم يكمل ما يليه، وهلم جرا ، قال : "أقيموا الصفوف وحاذوا بين المناكب وسدوا الخلل ولينوا بأيدي إخوانكم ولا تذروا فرجات الشيطان من وصل صفاً وصله الله ومن قطع صفا قطعه الله"، وقال: "خياركم ألينكم مناكب في الصلاة". (فتح) معه الصبيان ثم الخناثى ثم النساء، الخناثي جمع خنثى كحبالى جمع حبلى، أي بعد الصبيان. (ط) ثم النساء: [ أي بعدهم يصف النساء، بأن يأمرهم بذلك لقوله : "ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهى"، ويتفرع على هذا مسألة المحاذاة، فلذلك ذكرها بالفاء وقال: "فإن". (ع)]
And he arranges the men: that is, the row of men is preferred over the row of boys, and it is preferred over the row of hermaphrodites, and it is preferred over the row of women; because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Let those of you who are mature and prudent be near me.' [Tabyin al-Haqaiq 1/350] And it is fitting for the people to stand close together, fill the gaps, and align their shoulders in the rows, and there is no harm if the imam instructs them to do so due to his statement: 'Straighten your rows, for straightening the rows is part of the perfection of prayer.' And 'Ali said: 'Straighten your rows or Allah will cause discord among your hearts' – this refers to difference of hearts. And it is fitting for the imam to stand opposite the middle; if he does not, he has done wrong. And they should complete the first row; if there is a gap in it but not in the second, he may break through the second (to fill the first) because they have no sanctity due to their negligence in not filling the first row. Then he completes the row next to it, and so on. He said: 'Establish the rows, align your shoulders, fill the gaps, be gentle with the hands of your brothers, and do not leave gaps for the devil. Whoever joins a row Allah will join him, and whoever cuts a row Allah will cut him off.' And he said: 'The best of you are those who are softest in their shoulders in prayer.' (Fath) With him (the imam) are the boys, then the hermaphrodites, then the women. 'Al-Khanathi' is plural of 'khuntha' (hermaphrodite) like habala from hubli (pregnant), i.e., after the boys. (T) Then the women: i.e., after them, the women are arranged, by instructing them to do so due to his statement: 'Let those of you who are mature and prudent be near me.' And from this branches the issue of alignment, so he mentioned it with the particle 'fa' and said 'fa-in' (then if). ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage provides guidance on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer. The primary order is: men first, then boys (discerning children), then hermaphrodites, then women. This is based on the hadith 'Let those of you who are mature and prudent be near me,' which implies proximity to the imam corresponds to religiosity and understanding. The passage then details rules for filling rows: worshippers should stand closely together, align shoulders, and fill any gaps. The imam may instruct them to do so because straightening rows is part of prayer perfection. The imam should stand in the middle of his row. If the first row has a gap, it is permissible for someone in the second row to move forward to fill it, because the second row's people are negligent by not filling the first. The passage concludes with several hadiths emphasizing the importance of row alignment and the virtue of being soft in shoulders (meaning flexibility in accommodating others). It then reiterates the order of rows with boys and hermaphrodites, and ends by noting that the issue of a woman's alignment (muhadhat) branches from this, which will be discussed next.

Key Terms
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite who has both male and female organs, ambiguous gender. Placed after boys and before women.
تراصوا (tarassu): To stand close together in rows, shoulder to shoulder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the recommended position for the imam in his row?
A) At the right end
B) At the left end
C) Opposite the middle
D) Any position is fine

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of rows in congregational prayer is: men first, then discerning boys, then khunathas, then women — based on the hadith 'Let those of you who are mature and prudent be near me.'

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Conditions for Invalidation of Prayer Due to a Woman's Alignment
Conditions for invalidity due to muhadhat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions that must be met for a woman's alignment to invalidate the man's prayer and apply them to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A woman's alignment invalidates the man's prayer only if she is desirable, the prayer is general, shared in takbir, place unified, and imam intends to lead her.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the precise conditions under which the Hanafi school rules that a woman's alignment (muhadhat) alongside a man during prayer invalidates the man's prayer. Understanding these conditions is crucial for imams and congregants to avoid invalidating their prayers. We will extract the five essential conditions and see how they apply in various scenarios, including cases where the woman is a latecomer or at a different height.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman aligning alongside a man during prayer. The ruling in the Hanafi school is that the man's prayer becomes fasid (invalid) under specific conditions. Note that the woman's prayer is not invalidated.
The text explicitly says 'فسدت صلاته' (his prayer becomes invalid), referring to the man.
2
Define 'desirable woman' (mughtah)
The woman must be 'mughtah' – one who is desired, i.e., an adult woman or a girl who is likely to incite desire. A girl not yet desired (e.g., infant) does not invalidate the man's prayer, even if she aligns.
The text includes both mahram and non-mahram women; the condition is about desirability, not marriage eligibility.
3
List the essential conditions
From the passage, extract the five conditions: (1) the woman is desirable; (2) the prayer is general (not janazah); (3) the prayers are shared in both takbir and performance (meaning they are following the same imam or the man is imam for the woman); (4) the place is unified (same level, no barrier); (5) if the man is imam, he must have intended to lead the woman.
The text also mentions that the alignment must be with a limb that matters (some say shin/ankle, others foot).
4
Examine the 'shared performance' condition
The text distinguishes between actual and estimated following. If a man and woman both follow an imam and then make up missed parts after the imam finishes, the alignment during the makeup invalidates because they are still considered behind the imam by estimation. But if the woman was behind the man actually, it still invalidates because they are not sharing performance.
This nuance is important for latecomers and those praying in congregation.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., a woman stands in the same row as a man in a congregational prayer, both following the imam; she is 25 years old; the mosque floor is level; the imam did not explicitly intend to lead her), determine if the man's prayer is invalidated. Answer: Yes, all conditions are met (desirable woman, general prayer, shared takbir and performance, unified place, and the imam's intention is not required when the woman is a follower of a follower – but the text says 'if he intends' refers to the imam's intention when he is the imam. In this case, the man is not the imam, so his intention is irrelevant; the conditions are met, so his prayer is invalid.
The condition of 'imam intending' applies only when the man is the imam for the woman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح) الخناثي جمع خنثى كحبالى جمع حبلى، أي بعد الصبيان. (ط) ثم النساء: [ أي بعدهم يصف النساء، بأن يأمرهم بذلك لقوله : "ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهى"، ويتفرع على هذا مسألة المحاذاة، فلذلك ذكرها بالفاء وقال: "فإن". (ع)] لما في "مسند الإمام أحمد": عن أبي مالك الأشعري أنه قال: "يا معشر الأشعريين اجتمعوا وأجمعوا نساءكم حتى أريكم صلاة رسول الله ، فاجتمعوا وجمعوا أبناءهم ونساءهم، ثم توضأ وأراهم كيف يتوضأ، ثم تقدم، فصف الرجال في أدنى الصف، وصف الولدان خلفهم، وصف النساء خلف الصبيان"؛ ولقوله علي: "أخروهن من حيث أخرهن الله"، ولم يذكر المصنف الخناثي جمع الخنثى، وهو الذي له آلة الرجال والنساء جميعاً، والمراد المشكل منه؛ لندرة هذا النوع، حتى لو وجد قدم على النساء. (فتح) مشتهاة صالحة للجماع عاقلة محرمة أو أجنبية ولو المحاذاة بعضو واحد، وخصه الزيلعي بالساق والكعب، وبعضهم اعتبر القدم. (ط ، ع) متحد فلو كان على دكان مثل قامة الرجل وهي على الأرض أو بالعكس، صلاته أي صلاة الرجل دون صلاتها لو مكلفا وإلا لا. إن نوى إشارة إلى شرط آخر من شرائط المحاذاة، وهو نية الإمام إمامتها، والشرائط منها: أن تكون المرأة من أهل الشهوة بأن تكون بالغة أو صبية مشتهاة، حتى لو كانت صبية لا تشتهى، وهي تعقل الصلاة فحاذت الرجل لا تفسد صلاته، ومنها أن تكون الصلاة مطلقة، حتى أن المحاذاة في صلاة الجنازة لا تفسد؛ لأنها دعاء، ومنها: أن تكون مشتركة تحريمة بأن يكونا بانيين تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام ومشتركة أداء بأن يكون أحدهما إماماً للآخر فيما يؤديه تحقيقاً أو تقديراً، حتى يشمل الشركة بين الإمام والمأموم فإن محاذاة المرأة للإمام مفسدة صلاته، حتى لو اقتدى رجل وامرأة بإمام فأحدثا وتوضئا، ثم جاءا وقد صلى الإمام، فقاما ليقضيا فحاذته فسدت صلاته؛ لأن اللاحق فيما يقضي كأنه خلف الإمام تقديراً؛ ولهذا لا يقرأ ولا يسجد للسهو، ولو كانت خلفه حقيقة فسدت صلاته؛ لأن الصلاة وإن اشتركت تحريمة؛ لكونهما بانيين تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام، حتى لا الاقتداء بالمسبوق، ولكنها ليست بمشتركة أداء؛ لأنه لا إمام لهما فيما يقضيان حقيقة ولا تقديراً، أما حقيقةً فظاهر، وأما تقديراً فلأنهما ما التزما الأداء مع الإمام فيما سبقا به؛ لأنه لا تتصور المتابعة فيما مضى، فلم يجعل كأنهما خلفه فكانا في حكم المنفردين، ولهذا يقرأ المسبوق ويسجد للسهو، ومنها: أن يكون المكان متحداً . لو كان الرجل على الدكان والمرأة على الأرض أو على العكس، والدكان مثل قامة الرجل لا تفسد صلاته، = [؟] يكي حتى
Then if a desirable woman stands alongside him in a general prayer, shared in the opening takbir, i.e., any female praying, as a precaution against command, i.e., one with bowing and prostration, after the men, and performance in a single place without a barrier, his prayer becomes invalid if he intends ... like a pillar and its like, answer: if he enters into the prayer of the imam, a boy... Apparently this ruling only applies when a congregation is present, men and boys. If there is a gap in the row, and if a man is present with him, he places him behind the row as indicated by the hadith of Anas: 'I and the orphan stood behind him, and the old woman behind us.' (Fath) The hermaphrodites are plural of khuntha, like habala from hubli, i.e., after the boys. (T) Then the women: i.e., after them the women are arranged, by instructing them to do so due to his statement: 'Let those of you who are mature and prudent be near me', and from this branches the issue of alignment, so he mentioned it with the 'fa' and said 'fa-in' (then if). ('Ayni) As in the Musnad of Imam Ahmad: from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari that he said: 'O gathering of Ash'aris, gather and bring your women so I can show you the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ). So they gathered and brought their sons and women, then he performed wudu and showed them how to do wudu, then he stepped forward, and he arranged the men in the front row, and the boys behind them, and the women behind the boys'; and due to his statement: 'Delay them as Allah has delayed them.' And the author did not mention the hermaphrodites, plural of khuntha, which is one who has both male and female parts, and the intended is the ambiguous one, due to the rarity of this type, so if found, it is placed before women. (Fath) 'Desirable woman' means one fit for intercourse, sane, whether a mahram or non-mahram, even if the alignment is with one limb. Al-Zayla'i specified the shin and the ankle, and some consider the foot. (T, Ayni) 'Single place' – so if he is on a platform the height of a man's stature and she is on the ground, or vice versa, his prayer is not invalid. (It means the man's prayer, not his prayer if he is obligated, otherwise no.) 'If he intends' indicates another condition of alignment, which is the imam's intention to be her imam. The conditions include: the woman must be one who is desired, i.e., an adult or a girl who is desired; if she is a girl who is not desired and she understands prayer and aligns with the man, it does not invalidate his prayer. Another condition: the prayer must be general (mootlaq), so alignment in a funeral prayer does not invalidate because it is a supplication. Another condition: the prayers must be shared in the opening takbir, meaning they both base their opening takbir on the imam's opening takbir, and shared in performance, meaning one is an imam for the other in what they perform, actually or by estimation. This includes the share between the imam and the follower. So the alignment of a woman with the imam invalidates his prayer. So if a man and a woman follow an imam, then they break wudu and perform wudu again, then come back after the imam has prayed, and they stand to make up what they missed, and she aligns with him, his prayer is invalid because the one who catches up (the later follower) in what he makes up is as if he is behind the imam by estimation; for this reason he does not recite and does not prostrate for forgetfulness. And if she was actually behind him, his prayer would be invalid because the prayer, even though shared in opening takbir, but it is not shared in performance; because he has no imam in what they make up, neither actually nor by estimation. Actually it is apparent; by estimation, because they were not obligated to follow the imam in what had passed; because following in what is passed is not possible, so they are not considered to be behind him; they are in the same position as individuals (munfarid), and for this reason the latecomer recites and prostrates for forgetfulness. Another condition: the place must be unified. If the man is on a platform and the woman on the ground, or vice versa, and the platform is the height of a man's stature, his prayer is not invalidated. = [؟] etc.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This lengthy passage exhaustively covers the conditions under which a prayer is invalidated when a woman stands alongside a man (muhadhat al-mar'a). The core ruling is: if a woman who is desirable (i.e., capable of inciting desire, adult or adolescent) stands alongside a man in the same prayer space without a barrier, while they are sharing the same prayer (both following the same imam or one is imam and the other follower), the man's prayer becomes invalid, provided he intends her as a follower or is aware of her alignment? The text says 'if he intends' which is a condition. The passage first defines the woman: she must be 'mughtah' (desired), which means she is fit for intercourse, sane, and could be either a mahram or non-mahram. It also mentions the part of the body that matters: some say the shin and ankle, others the foot. Then it lists the conditions: (1) The woman must be from the people of desire (i.e., adult or a desirable minor). (2) The prayer must be a general prayer (not funeral, which is a supplication). (3) The prayers must be shared in the opening takbir (both base their takbir on the same imam) and shared in performance (one is an imam for the other actually or by estimation). This includes the case where both are following an imam, or when the woman aligns with the imam. The passage discusses a scenario: a man and woman follow an imam, then both break wudu and return after the imam finished, and they make up the missed part. If they align, the man's prayer is invalid because the later follower is considered behind the imam by estimation. But if the woman was actually behind the man, it would still invalidate because they are not considered to have an imam in the makeup. (4) The place must be unified; if they are at different heights (like a platform), it may not invalidate. The passage concludes with the condition that the imam must have intended to lead her (intention to be her imam).

Key Terms
المحاذاة (al-muhadhat): The alignment of a woman alongside a man during prayer, which can invalidate the prayer.
مشتاة (mughtah): A woman who is desirable, capable of inciting desire, i.e., adult or adolescent girl.
مطلقة (mutlaqa): A general prayer with ruku' and sujud, i.e., not a funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a necessary condition for a woman's alignment to invalidate the man's prayer?
A) The woman must be a non-mahram
B) The prayer must be a funeral prayer
C) The woman must be desirable (mughtah), i.e., adult or adolescent girl
D) The man must be praying alone, not in congregation

Key Takeaway
A man's prayer becomes invalid in the Hanafi school if a desirable woman aligns alongside him in a general, shared prayer in a unified place, with additional conditions regarding the imam's intention.

Salah — Prayer

Imamah: Woman Alignment and Invalid Following
Exposition of rows order, woman's alignment conditions, and invalid imamates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's alignment invalidates a man's prayer and list the invalid imamates according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A woman's alignment invalidates the man's prayer only if she is desirable, same prayer, shared start, no barrier, and imam intends her leadership.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses critical rules of congregational prayer leadership. It begins with the order of rows, then gives the precise conditions for a woman's alignment affecting a man's prayer, and concludes with a list of invalid imamates that highlight the Hanafi insistence on congruence between imam and follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the row order
Note the sequence: adult men, boys, hermaphrodites, women. This order is based on the hadith 'Let those with understanding stand near me.'
The sick are also placed before women.
2
Parse conditions for woman alignment invalidation
Extract each condition from the phrase: desirable woman (mushthahat), absolute shared prayer (not funeral), same tahrimah, same place, no barrier, imam intending her imamate. Only when all are met does her alignment invalidate his prayer.
The text uses 'مطلقة' meaning any prayer except funeral, and 'مشتركة' meaning both share the same imam.
3
List the invalid imamates
Go through each case: woman leading man, boy leading man, pure leading one with excuse, illiterate leading reciter, naked leading clothed, gesture-imam leading bowing-imam, supererogatory leading obligatory, different fard leading another fard. Understand the rationale: the follower's prayer must be a valid replica of the imam's.
The last two cases are about obligation type; they generate an inter-madhhab dispute.
4
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Shafi'i and Zufar allow a follower performing one fard to follow an imam performing a different fard. Hanafis deem it invalid. The key difference: Hanafis consider the follower's prayer attached to the imam's, while Shafi'is view it as separate followership.
The practical consequence: in Hanafi masjids, the imam and follower must be performing the same fard prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإمامة
الصبيان ثم الخناثى ثم النساء، فإن جاذته مشتهاة في صلاة مطلقة مشتركة تحريمةً وأداءً في مكان متحد بلا حائل فسدت صلاته إن نوى إمامتها.
ولا يحضرن الجماعات، وفسد اقتداء رجل بامرأة أو صبي، وطاهر بمعذور، وخنثى في أي وقارئ بأمي، ومكتس بعار، وغير مؤم بمؤمٍ، ومفترض بمتنفل وبمفترض آخر، خلافا للشافعي وزفر وهو يصلي بالإيماء.
Chapter of Imamah: Boys, then hermaphrodites, then women. If a desirable woman aligns with him in an absolute prayer shared in tahrimah and performance, in one place without a barrier, his prayer becomes invalid if he intended her imamate. And they (women) should not attend congregations. And invalid is the following of a man by a woman or a boy, and a pure person by one with an excuse, and a hermaphrodite in any case, and a reciter by an illiterate, and a clothed person by a naked one, and one performing prayer with gestures by one performing with bowing, and one performing obligatory prayer by one performing supererogatory or by another obligatory prayer, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Zufar, and he (the imam) prays by gestures.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents core rulings on imamah (leadership in prayer). First, it establishes the order of rows: adult men first, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women. This order is based on the hadith 'Let those of you with understanding and wisdom stand near me.' The main ruling is about a woman standing alongside a man in the same row. If a desirable woman (mushthahat, i.e., one who is likely to attract desire, typically a mature woman or a girl who invites desire) aligns with a man in a shared obligatory prayer (both intending the same imam and performing the same prayer), in the same place, without a barrier, and the imam intended her imamate (i.e., he was leading her), then the man's prayer becomes invalid. This is a specific Hanafi position. The passage then lists several invalid imamates: a woman or boy leading (they cannot be imam for men), a pure person following one with an excuse (like one with urine incontinence), a reciter following an illiterate, a clothed person following a naked one, one performing prayer with gestures following one performing with bowing and prostration, and one performing fard following another performing supererogatory or a different fard prayer. The Hanafi school deems these invalid, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Zufar who allow following in a different fard prayer based on mere followership. The Hanafi view is based on the principle that the follower's prayer becomes part of the imam's prayer.

Key Terms
مشتهاة (mushthahat): A woman who is desirable, i.e., capable of attracting sexual desire, typically a mature woman or a girl who has reached an age where she is desired.
محاذاة (muhadhat): Alignment, meaning a woman standing exactly alongside a man in prayer, such that any part of her body is parallel to his.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and makes it forbidden (haram) to break.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for a woman's alignment to invalidate the man's prayer?
A) The woman must be a mahram.
B) The prayer is an obligatory prayer (fard).
C) The woman is behind the man.
D) The man intends to lead the woman.

Key Takeaway
A woman's alignment invalidates a man's prayer only when all six conditions are met; otherwise the prayer is valid. Also, the Hanafi school strictly limits valid imamates to those with full congruence in ability, purity, knowledge, and obligation type.

Conditions for Valid Following in Prayer
Listing conditions for valid following in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid following (iqtida') in Hanafi fiqh and identify which violation renders the follower's prayer invalid.

Core Idea
Valid following requires alignment in a complete pillar, no barrier, correct intention, and same direction.

This lesson examines the conditions for a follower's prayer to be valid when praying behind an imam. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists scenarios that invalidate following, such as a man following a woman or a boy, and adds essential conditions: no physical barrier, the imam's intention for women, alignment in a complete rak'ah, and uniform direction. It also highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar and a cross-madhhab difference with al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify invalid following scenarios
The passage first lists pairings that automatically invalidate iqtida', such as a man following a woman, a pure person following one with an excuse, a reciter following an illiterate, etc. Note that the Hanafi school considers these categorically invalid.
These are not conditions but absolute preventers (mawani').
2
Understand the barrier condition
The text states that a physical barrier (ha'il) like a pillar or a gap the size of a man invalidates following. However, a small barrier like the back of a saddle does not. This condition applies even if they are in the same place.
The barrier affects the connection (ittisal) between imam and follower.
3
Examine the intention condition for women
The imam must intend to lead the woman specifically; otherwise her prayer is invalid. The man's prayer remains valid because his leadership is unaffected. This differs from Zufar's view.
The ruling highlights the dependency of the woman's prayer on the imam's intent.
4
Explore the two omitted conditions
The commentator adds two conditions: (1) alignment (muhadha) must occur during a complete rak'ah, not just a part; (2) the directions of prayer must be the same. If directions differ, following is invalid except in cases of uncertainty (e.g., inside Kaaba).
These are derived from qiyas and are part of the mu'tamad position.
5
Analyze the dispute with Zufar
Zufar holds that absolute alignment (even in a partial rak'ah) invalidates, and that the imam's intention for women is not required. The three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) restrict the invalidation to alignment in a complete pillar and require intention for women. The mufta bihi follows the three.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: under Zufar, woman's prayer valid without imam's intention.

Chapter of Imamate. Her imamate. And she should not attend congregational prayers. And the following of a man by a woman or a boy is invalid, and of a pure person by one with a valid excuse. ... And also invalid is the following of a praying person by a reciter by an illiterate, and of a clothed by a naked, and of one who prays by gestures by one who prays by gestures, and of one performing obligatory prayer by one performing voluntary prayer and by another obligatory prayer, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Zufar ... And the woman on the ground or the opposite, and the platform like the height of a man does not invalidate his prayer. And among them: that there be no screen between them such that if they were in one place but there is a pillar or the size of the back of a saddle and its thickness like the thickness of a finger or a gap in which a man stands, it does not invalidate his prayer. And among them: that the imam intends to lead the woman; because if he does not intend, the man's prayer is not invalidated, but the woman's prayer is invalidated. These are conditions mentioned by the author, and two other conditions remain which he did not mention: first, that the alignment be in a complete pillar; second, that their directions be the same, so that if they differ it does not invalidate, and it is not conceivable inside the Kaaba or on a dark night and each prayed by ijtihad to a direction. And Zufar said: her following him is valid even if he did not intend her imamate. And the three said: alignment in absolute terms invalidates originally except in that, and that is qiyas. (Miskin, 'Ayni) Her imamate: at the time of his commencement, not after, otherwise her prayer is invalidated, as if he gestured for her to step back and she did not step back. (T)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists the conditions for valid following in prayer. It begins with the ruling that a woman should not attend congregational prayers (a separate ruling, discussed elsewhere). The core of this section is the list of scenarios where following (iqtida) is invalid: a man following a woman or a boy, a pure person following one with a chronic excuse, a skilled reciter following an illiterate, a clothed person following a naked, one praying with gestures following another, and one performing an obligatory prayer following one performing a voluntary or a different obligatory prayer. The author notes that al-Shafi'i and Zufar differ on some points. Additional conditions are given: there must be no physical barrier between imam and follower, even if they are in the same space, unless the barrier is a pillar or a small object; and the imam must have the intention to lead the woman if she is following, otherwise her prayer is invalid. Two further conditions omitted by the original author are added: the alignment (muhadha) must occur during a complete rak'ah, and the directions of prayer must be the same. Zufar holds that the woman's following is valid even without the imam's intention, while the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) consider absolute alignment to be a cause of invalidation except in exceptional cases. The passage ends with a note that the imam's intention is considered at the start of prayer, not later.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): The act of a follower (ma'mum) performing prayer behind an imam, intending to follow him.
المحاذاة (al-muhadha): Alignment of the follower with the imam in position, such that they are side by side or the follower slightly behind.
نية الإمامة (niyyat al-imama): The imam's intention to lead the specific follower(s), especially women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Valid following in Hanafi prayer requires no barrier, the imam's intention for women, alignment in a complete rak'ah, and uniform direction, with Zufar differing on intention and absolute alignment.

The Mufta Bihi Ruling on Women Attending Mosques
Ruling on women attending mosques with intra-Hanafi dispute and fatwa change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi ruling on women attending congregational prayers and explain why the ruling changed to karaha due to corruption.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa changed from permissibility to dislike because of social corruption, not because the act itself became haram.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a critical issue in contemporary fiqh: whether women may attend congregational prayers. The original positions of the Hanafi imams differed, but the later fatwa settled on karaha (dislike) for all prayers. This shift exemplifies how Hanafi jurists consider social context (al-fasad) in their rulings, a principle known as sadd al-dhara'i'. In this lesson, we will unpack the operative ruling, its reason, and its extension to other gatherings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is women attending congregational prayers (salat al-jama'ah). The mufta bihi ruling today is makruh (disliked), specifically makruh tahrimi due to the strong reason of fasad.
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; the fatwa considers the probability of fitnah.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa originally held that women should not attend (karaha), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permitted it for all prayers. The later fatwa adopted Abu Hanifa's view.
This is a classic example of tarjih based on changing circumstances.
3
Understand the reason (illah) for the fatwa change
The commentator says 'due to the prevalence of corruption (li-zuhur al-fasad).' The illah is not the act itself but the social consequences of women going out to mosques in times of moral decay.
The ruling is context-dependent; if corruption disappears, the permissibility may return.
4
Apply the extension to other gatherings
The passage extends the ruling to gatherings of admonition (majalis al-wa'z), especially those led by ignorant pretenders. The same illah applies, so the ruling is even stronger.
This is qiyas: if attending the mosque is disliked, attending a more dubious gathering is more disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يحضرن الجماعات :وقالا يخرجن في الصلوات كلها والفتوى اليوم على كراهة حضورهن في كل الصلوات؛ لظهور الفساد، ومتى كره حضورهن المسجد للصلاة لأن يكره حضورهن مجالس الوعظ خصوصاً عند هؤلاء الجهال الذين تحلوا بحلية العلماء أولى. (مسكين)
And they should not attend congregational prayers. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: they should go out for all prayers. And the fatwa today is on the dislike (karaha) of their attendance in all prayers due to the appearance of corruption. And when their attendance at the mosque for prayer is disliked, then their attendance at gatherings of admonition is more deserving of dislike, especially among these ignorant ones who adorn themselves with the garb of scholars. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on women attending congregational prayers. The matn states 'they should not attend,' which is the view of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that women may go out for all prayers (i.e., it is permissible). However, the fatwa today (in the later period) is that it is makruh (disliked) for women to attend any prayers due to the prevalence of corruption (fasad). The commentator extends this to gatherings of admonition (majalis al-wa'z), saying that if attending the mosque is disliked, then attending such gatherings is even more disliked, especially when ignorant people who pretend to be scholars are present. This reflects the Hanafi principle of blocking means to evil (sadd al-dhara'i').

Key Terms
كراهة (karaha): Dislike, legal disapproval that may be tanzihi (slight) or tahrimi (close to haram). Here it is strong due to fasad.
الفساد (al-fasad): Corruption or moral decay in society that would result from women attending mosques.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib if she has no other means of prayer.
B) It is makruh (disliked) due to the prevalence of corruption.
C) It is mubah (permissible) as long as she is modestly dressed.
D) It is haram to even leave the house.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on women attending mosques is karaha due to social corruption, not because the act itself is intrinsically impermissible.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Women Attending Congregational Prayers
Intra-Hanafi dispute on women attending mosques with later tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on women attending congregational prayers and evaluate the later tarjih that made Abu Hanifa's view the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prohibited or strongly disliked; his two disciples permitted; later Hanafi fatwa adopted Abu Hanifa's view due to changed social conditions.

The Hanafi school is known for its internal ikhtilaf, and few issues illustrate this better than the ruling on women attending mosques. The text records the stark disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two principal disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. While Abu Hanifa held that women should not attend congregational prayers, the Sahibayn allowed it for all prayers. Later Hanafi jurists reassessed the issue and settled on Abu Hanifa's view as the operative fatwa. This lesson explores the nature of this intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, its basis, and how the tarjih was made.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
The matn states 'they should not attend' (view of Abu Hanifa). Then 'the two said: they should go out for all prayers' (Sahibayn). Then 'the fatwa today is karaha' (later tarjih).
The fatwa today agrees with Abu Hanifa but uses the term karaha, not haram.
2
Understand the basis of each position
Abu Hanifa likely relied on blocking means to evil (sadd al-dhara'i') and hadith recommending women pray at home. The Sahibayn may have prioritized general permission to attend mosque and considered that women should not be prevented from worship.
The text does not give proofs, but these are common principles invoked by each side.
3
Analyze the reason for the fatwa change
The commentator explicitly says the fatwa changed 'due to the appearance of corruption (fasad).' This indicates that the later scholars re-evaluated the illah and decided that the context had shifted, making Abu Hanifa's precautionary view more suitable.
This is a key example of fatwa changing with time and place (taghayyur al-fatwa bi taghayyur al-azman).
4
Recognize the authority weight
The fatwa today is classified as 'fatawa mutakhkhirin' (later fatwa), which overrides the 'zahir al-riwayah' position of the Sahibayn in practice, though the Sahibayn's view remains part of the school's transmitted corpus.
The mufta bihi need not be the strongest in dalil; it is the most suitable for the era.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that women may go out for all prayers (i.e., it is permissible). However, the fatwa today (in the later period) is that it is makruh (disliked) for women to attend any prayers due to the prevalence of corruption (fasad). The commentator extends this to gatherings of admonition (majalis al-wa'z), saying that if attending the mosque is disliked, then attending such gatherings is even more disliked, especially when ignorant people who pretend to be scholars are present. الفساد (al-fasad): Corruption or moral decay in society that would result from women attending mosques.
أولى (awla): More deserving, priority; used in qiyas avla (a fortiori analogy) to indicate that if something is disliked, something similar with greater reason is even more disliked.

Key Takeaway

Imamate of a Minor: Hanafi Position and Disputes
Ruling on a boy leading prayer, with Shafi'i and intra-Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a boy leading prayer, explain the evidence from the Sahaba, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A boy cannot lead any prayer – his imamate is invalid absolutely.

Ever wondered if a gifted child can lead adults in prayer? This lesson dissects the Hanafi position that a pre-pubescent boy's imamate is invalid in all prayers, contrasting with the Shafi'i view. We'll explore the proof texts that shape this ruling and the intra-Hanafi debate that ultimately settled on absolute invalidity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: 'absolute invalidity' – that a minor cannot lead any prayer, whether tarawih, absolute voluntary, or obligatory.
The word مطلقاً (absolutely) is key.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Al-Shafi'i permits a boy's imamate based on the hadith of 'Amr ibn Salama, who led his people at age six or seven. Understand the evidence the other school uses.
This hadith is cited in Shafi'i sources.
3
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
Hanafis argue that the 'Amr hadith is not authentically from the Prophet (a companion action), and they rely on stronger evidence: the sayings of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas demanding puberty for the imam.
Note the chain of transmission criticism.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that a boy can lead in absolute voluntary prayers (nafl mutlaq), while Abu Yusuf disagrees. Understand why the mukhtar (chosen) position is absolute invalidity.
The commentator says 'al-mukhtar' ends the dispute.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if a boy leads any prayer, Hanafis require followers to repeat it; Shafi'is deem it valid. Within Hanafism, the mufta bihi is that repetition is needed in all cases.
This affects real‐life congregational prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو صبي: مطلقاً سواء كان في التراويح أو النفل المطلق أو غيرهما، وقال الشافعي: يجوز لما روي أن عمرو بن سلمة قدمه قومه وهو ابن ست أو سبع، وكان يصلي بهم، ولنا قول ابن مسعود الله: "لا يؤم الغلام الذي لا تحب عليه الحدود"، وعن ابن عباس ما: "حتى يحتلم"، وإمامة عمرو ليست بمسموعة منه عليه، وعند محمد يصح إمامته في النفل المطلق خلافاً لأبي يوسف، والمختار أن لا يصح الاقتداء في الصلوات كلها. (فتح)
Or a boy: absolutely, whether in tarawih or absolute voluntary prayer or others. Al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible based on the narration that 'Amr ibn Salama was put forward by his people when he was six or seven years old, and he led them in prayer. And we have the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): 'A boy upon whom the prescribed punishments are not obligatory should not lead the prayer.' And from Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Until he reaches puberty.' And the imamate of 'Amr is not authentically heard from him (the Prophet). And according to Muhammad, his imamate is valid in absolute voluntary prayer, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And the chosen (mukhtar) is that following is not valid in all prayers. (Fath)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of a pre-pubescent boy leading the prayer. The matn declares it invalid absolutely, irrespective of the type of prayer (tarawih, voluntary, etc.). Al-Shafi'i argues for permissibility based on the hadith of 'Amr ibn Salama, a boy who led his tribe. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of 'Amr is not authentically established as a prophetic practice, and they have stronger evidence: the saying of Ibn Mas'ud that a boy not subject to hudud should not lead, and Ibn 'Abbas's condition of puberty. Within the Hanafi school, Muhammad holds that a boy's imamate is valid for absolute voluntary prayers (najh al-mutlaq) while Abu Yusuf disagrees. The relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that following a boy is invalid in all prayers, including tarawih and voluntary.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabi): A male child who has not reached puberty (before first wet dream or age 15).
النفل المطلق (al-nafl al-mutlaq): A voluntary prayer not restricted to a specific time or reason.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or relied-upon position in the school after weighing evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Valid if the boy can recite well.
D) Valid only if adults are present.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a pre-pubescent boy cannot lead any prayer; his imamate is absolutely invalid, and followers must repeat the prayer.

Following a Mutayammim and Sitting Imam: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on following in purity and posture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on following a mutayammim and a sitting imam, identify Muhammad's opposing view, and apply the relied-upon ruling to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
A person with wudu may follow a mutayammim, and a standing person may follow a sitting imam—this is the mufta bihi despite Muhammad's objection.

This passage tackles several cases where the validity of following (iqtida) is disputed within the Hanafi school. The main disagreements concern whether a person with wudu can pray behind a mutayammim, and whether a standing person can follow a sitting imam. The majority view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that both are valid, supported by explicit prophetic practice. Muhammad al-Shaybani dissents, arguing that tayammum is a mere substitute and that the sitting imam contradicts the Prophet's command. Understanding this ikhtilaf and the proofs involved is essential for a mufti who must issue fatwa on such common situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial rulings in the matn
The passage opens with a series of negations: 'There is no following of a mutawaddi' by a mutayammim... of a standing person by a sitting one...' Note that this is the base text (matn) statement, which appears to prohibit these cases.
This matn is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq; the commentary (Fath) will qualify it.
2
Recognize Muhammad's ikhtilaf and its basis
Muhammad explicitly denies validity for the mutayammim and sitting imam cases. His reasoning: tayammum is a necessary purification, building a strong (wudu) on weak is invalid; and the hadith 'Let no one lead after me sitting.'
Muhammad's view is a minority within the school.
3
Examine the proofs of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
For mutayammim: they cite the practice of 'Amr ibn al-'As, who led his companions in tayammum while they had wudu, and the Prophet did not order repetition. For sitting: the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet leading while sitting and Abu Bakr conveying. This establishes the legitimacy of sitting imam and the practice of tabligh.
These are authentic hadith; the objecting hadith is considered abrogated or specific to the Prophet.
4
Understand the tarjih and mufta bihi
The commentator (Fath) and others weigh the proofs and adopt the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The mufta bihi is that both following a mutayammim and following a sitting imam are valid.
This is the relied-upon position in fatwa.
5
Apply the principle to other cases (hunchback, mu'mi, etc.)
The passage extends the reasoning: hunchback imamate is valid unless hump reaches ruku' according to Muhammad; mu'mi leading mu'mi is valid if similar postures; voluntary follower behind obligatory imam is valid because the follower's prayer adopts the imam's ruling.
These are applications of the same principle of equality or need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

متوضئ بمتيمم وقال محمد لا يجوز؛ لأن التيمم طهارة ضرورية لا يصار إليه إلا عند العجز، ولهما: أنه طهارة حتى لا تتقيد بوقت الصلاة. (ع) بماسح على الخف أو الجبيرة؛ لاستواء حالهما إجماعا. وقائم بقاعد لأن القعود كالقيام وقال محمد: لا يقتدي المتوضئ بمتيمم ولا قائم بقاعد، أما عدم الجواز في المسألة الأولى عنده؛ فلأن طهارة المتيمم ،ضرورية وبالماء أصلية، فيكون بناء القوي على الضعيف، ولهما: ما أن عمرو بن العاص صلى بأصحابه، وهو متيمم عن الجنابة وهم متوضؤون، فعلم عليه ولم يأمرهم بالإعادة. وأجمعوا على الصحة في الجنازة، وقيل: هذا الخلاف بناء على أن التراب خلف عن الماء عندهما، فيعمل عمله، وعند محمد الطهارة بالتراب بدل عن الطهارة بالماء، فيكون بناء القوي على الضعيف، وأما عدم الجواز في المسألة الثانية عنده، فلقوله عليه: "لا يؤمن أحد بعدي جالساً، ولهما: حديث عائشة لما أنه عليه أمر أبا بكر أن يصلي بالناس، فلما دخل أبو بكر في الصلاة وجد في نفسه خفة، فقام يهادى بين رجلين، فجاء فجلس عن يسار أبي بكر، فكان عليها يصلي بالناس جالسا وأبو بكر قائما، يقتدي أبو بكر بصلاة النبي ، ويقتدي الناس بصلاة أبي بكر، وهذا صريح في أنه علي كان إماماً وأبو بكر كان مبلغاً؛ إذ لا يجوز أن يكون للناس إمامان في صلاة واحدة، وكانت هذه الصلاة صلاة الظهر يوم السبت أو الأحد، وتوفي عليها يوم الاثنين، وهذا أصل مشروعية التبليغ، وجوازه إجماعاً إذا كانت الجماعة لا يصل إليهم صوت الإمام، إما لضعفه أو كثرة الجماعة، واتفق المذاهب الأربعة على كراهة التبليغ عند عدم الحاجة وقالوا: إنه بدعة منكرة. (فتح) بأحدب : يقال له بالفارسية : كوزه پشت" سواء بلغت حدبته حد الركوع أو لا. وفي "الفتاوى الظهيرية": لا تصح إمامة الأحدب للقائم عند محمد إذا بلغ حدبه حد الركوع، وتصح عندهما. (فتح، عيني) ومؤم بمثله : أي لا يفسد أيضاً اقتداء المؤمي بالمؤمي سواء كان الإمام قائماً أو قاعداً؛ لاستواء حالهما، وإن كان مضطجعاً والمؤتم قائماً أو قاعداً لا يجوز على المختار. (ط) ومتنفل بمفترض : أطلقه فعم اقتداء من يصلي التراويح بالمكتوبة لا يقال إن القراءة في الأخريين فرض في حق المتنفل نفل في حق المفترض، فيكون في الأخريين اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل وهو لا يجوز؛ لأنا نقول: صلاة المقتدي أخذت حكم صلاة الإمام بسبب الاقتداء، ولهذا يلزمه قضاء ما لم يدركه مع الإمام من الشفع الأول، وكذا لو أفسد المقتدي صلاته يلزمه أربع ركعات في الرباعية، فكان تبعاً للإمام، فتكون القراءة في الشفع الثاني نفلاً في حقه كما نفل في حق الإمام. (فتح) محدث أو جنب أو في ثوبه أو بدنه نجاسة.
مطلقة، روي
هي
There is no following of a person with wudu by a mutayammim, and of a person who washes by one who wipes, and of a standing person by a sitting one and by a hunchback; and of one who prays by gestures by one like him. Also, the following of a person praying voluntary prayer by one praying obligatory prayer is not invalidated. And if it becomes apparent that his imam was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity) for an absolute reason, it is narrated that it is not invalidated. ... A person with wudu following a mutayammim: Muhammad said it is not permissible because tayammum is a necessary purification (tahara daruriyya) which is only resorted to when unable (to use water). And for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad himself? Actually the text says 'لهما', meaning Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? But here Muhammad is being opposed; likely 'لهما' refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? Or a different context. Let me correct: The text says 'وقال محمد لا يجوز' and then 'ولهما' which likely refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? But that would be contradictory. Possibly 'لهما' means Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, or it is a transmission error. In any case, the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold it is permissible because tayammum is purification. For wiping on khuff or splint: due to their state being equal in purity. For standing following a sitting person: because sitting is like standing. And Muhammad said: a person with wudu should not follow a mutayammim, nor should a standing person follow a sitting person. As for non-permissibility in the first issue according to him: because the purification of the mutayammim is necessary (emergency) and with water is original, so it is building the strong on the weak. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): that 'Amr ibn al-'As prayed with his companions while in a state of junub with tayammum and they had wudu, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) came to know (or saw) and did not order them to repeat. And they agreed on the validity in funeral prayer. And it is said: this difference is based on whether dust is a substitute (khalaf) for water (according to them) so it acts as water, or a replacement (badal) according to Muhammad, so building strong on weak. And as for the second issue (standing following sitting) according to him: due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Let no one lead after me while sitting.' And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): the hadith of 'A'isha that he (peace be upon him) ordered Abu Bakr to lead the people, and when Abu Bakr entered the prayer he felt lightness, so he (the Prophet) stood supported between two men, then came and sat to the left of Abu Bakr, and he (the Prophet) led the people sitting while Abu Bakr was standing, and Abu Bakr followed the prayer of the Prophet, and the people followed the prayer of Abu Bakr. This is explicit that he (the Prophet) was the imam and Abu Bakr was the conveyor, for it is not permissible for the people to have two imams in one prayer. This prayer was Dhuhr on Saturday or Sunday, and he died on Monday. This is the basis for the legitimacy of tabligh (conveying) and its permissibility by consensus when the congregation cannot hear the imam's voice due to weakness or large crowd. The four schools agreed on the dislike of tabligh when not needed, and they said it is an innovation (bid'a). (Fath) Hunchback: it is called in Persian 'kuze pusht', whether his hump reaches the level of ruku' or not. In Fatawa Zahiriyya: the imamate of a hunchback for a standing person is not valid according to Muhammad if his hump reaches the level of ruku', but it is valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And one who prays by gestures following one like him: i.e., it is not invalidated even if the imam is standing or sitting, due to their equality. But if the imam is lying down (mudtaji') and the follower is standing or sitting, it is not permissible according to the chosen position. And one performing voluntary prayer following one performing obligatory prayer: he made it general, including one praying tarawih following the written prayer. It might be said that recitation in the last two rak'ahs is obligatory for the one praying voluntary and voluntary for the one praying obligatory, so in the last two it would be following by the one performing obligatory (the follower) of the one performing voluntary (the imam), which is not permissible. We answer: the prayer of the follower takes the ruling of the imam's prayer due to following, and therefore the follower must make up what he missed of the first set (shaf') with the imam. And similarly, if the follower's prayer becomes spoiled, he must make up four rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer. So he is a follower of the imam, and thus the recitation in the second set becomes voluntary for him just as it is voluntary for the imam. (Fath) ... an imam who is in a state of hadath or janaba, or has impurity on his garment or body: an absolute (report) that it is not invalidated. Narrated: it is.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from page 100 covers multiple rulings on the validity of following in specific cases. It begins by stating that a person with wudu following a mutayammim (dry ablution) is invalid, as is a person who washes (ghasil) following one who wipes (masih) on khuff or splint, and a standing person following a sitting person or a hunchback, and one who prays with gestures following another like him. However, it then qualifies that these are not invalidated (la yafsud) in certain interpretations. The core dispute is with Muhammad (one of the Sahibayn) who holds that a mutayammim cannot lead a mutawaddi' (one with wudu), and a sitting person cannot lead a standing person. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold permissibility based on the precedent of 'Amr ibn al-'As and the hadith of the Prophet's sitting prayer during his illness, where Abu Bakr was a conveyor. The discussion about the hunchback includes a detail from Fatawa Zahiriyya that Muhammad invalidates if the hump reaches the ruku' level. The topic of a person with gestures (mu'mi) leading another is valid if both are in similar states but not if the imam is lying down. Finally, the section on a voluntary follower behind an obligatory imam (e.g., tarawih behind Fard) clarifies that the follower's prayer inherits the imam's ruling, resolving the potential conflict of recitation in the second half. The passage ends with a note on the imam becoming hadath or having najasa, and a narration that it is not invalidated (perhaps referring to a known ruling).

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
التبليغ (al-tabligh): Conveying the imam's takbir and recitation to the congregation when they cannot hear him.
مؤم (mu'mi): One who prays by gestures (ishaara) due to inability to perform physical movements.
الخلاف البناء على أن التراب خلف عن الماء (al-khilaf bina' 'ala anna al-turab khalaf 'an al-ma'): The dispute is based on whether dust (tayammum) is a substitute (khalaf) for water, acting like water, or a mere replacement (badal) that does not fully substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, can a standing person follow a sitting imam?
A) Yes, because sitting is like standing in prayer.
B) No, because the follower must be equal or higher.
C) Only if the imam is standing for tashahhud.
D) Only in voluntary prayers.

Key Takeaway
Following a mutayammim or a sitting imam is valid in the Hanafi school according to the majority, despite Muhammad's dissent.

Following a Mutayammim: Hanafi Positions on Imamate
States ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on imamah of mutayammim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad regarding a mutawaddi' praying behind a mutayammim, explain their proofs from hadith and qiyas, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid but weaker; the dispute is whether a stronger purity can follow a weaker one.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a dispute within the Hanafi school about the imamah of a mutayammim. While the matn states a general prohibition, the commentators explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi usul principles like taqrir (tacit approval) and the nature of tayammum as a badal (substitute) are applied in deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the three imams
The core question: Can a person with wudu validly follow a mutayammim as imam? Recognize that 'lahuma' refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and 'Muhammad' is Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
Intra-Hanafi dispute: the two vs Muhammad.
2
Understand Muhammad's argument
Muhammad considers it invalid because tayammum is a necessary purification (darurah) and weaker than original wudu. Building the strong on the weak is invalid.
He analogizes to other weak imams like a seated person leading a standing one.
3
Understand the argument of the two
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that tayammum is a complete purification that lifts hadath, so it is equal to wudu. They cite the hadith of Amr ibn al-As where the Prophet tacitly approved the prayer.
They also note consensus on validity in funeral prayer.
4
Analyze the usul basis
The dispute hinges on whether tayammum is a badal (substitute) that fully replaces water (view of the two) or a mere replacement that is inferior (Muhammad). This is a usul al-fiqh issue of al-ibdal.
The two use taqrir from the hadith, Muhammad uses a qiyas based on weakness.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, making the prayer valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi). This is because the hadith evidence is strong and the consensus on janazah supports it.
Thus, the matn's blanket prohibition is not the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة ۱۱ باب الإمامة لا اقتداء متوضئ بمتيمم وغاسل بماسح وقائم بقاعد وبأحدب؛ متوضئ بمتيمم وقال محمد لا يجوز؛ لأن التيمم طهارة ضرورية لا يصار إليه إلا عند العجز، ولهما: أنه طهارة حتى لا تتقيد بوقت الصلاة. (ع) بماسح على الخف أو الجبيرة؛ لاستواء حالهما إجماعا. وقائم بقاعد لأن القعود كالقيام وقال محمد: لا يقتدي المتوضئ بمتيمم ولا قائم بقاعد، أما عدم الجواز في المسألة الأولى عنده؛ فلأن طهارة المتيمم ،ضرورية وبالماء أصلية، فيكون بناء القوي على الضعيف، ولهما: ما أن عمرو بن العاص صلى بأصحابه، وهو متيمم عن الجنابة وهم متوضؤون، فعلم عليه ولم يأمرهم بالإعادة. وأجمعوا على الصحة في الجنازة، وقيل: هذا الخلاف بناء على أن التراب خلف عن الماء عندهما، فيعمل عمله، وعند محمد الطهارة بالتراب بدل عن الطهارة بالماء، فيكون بناء القوي على الضعيف، وأما عدم الجواز في المسألة الثانية عنده، فلقوله عليه: "لا يؤمن أحد بعدي جالساً، ولهما: حديث عائشة لما أنه عليه أمر أبا بكر أن يصلي بالناس، فلما دخل أبو بكر في الصلاة وجد في نفسه خفة، فقام يهادى بين رجلين، فجاء فجلس عن يسار أبي بكر، فكان عليها يصلي بالناس جالسا وأبو بكر قائما، يقتدي أبو بكر بصلاة النبي ، ويقتدي الناس بصلاة أبي بكر، وهذا صريح في أنه علي كان إماماً وأبو بكر كان مبلغاً؛ إذ لا يجوز أن يكون للناس إمامان في صلاة واحدة، وكانت هذه الصلاة صلاة الظهر يوم السبت أو الأحد، وتوفي عليها يوم الاثنين، وهذا أصل مشروعية التبليغ، وجوازه إجماعاً إذا كانت الجماعة لا يصل إليهم صوت الإمام، إما لضعفه أو كثرة الجماعة، واتفق المذاهب الأربعة على كراهة التبليغ عند عدم الحاجة وقالوا: إنه بدعة منكرة. (فتح) بأحدب : يقال له بالفارسية : كوزه پشت" سواء بلغت حدبته حد الركوع أو لا. وفي "الفتاوى الظهيرية": لا تصح إمامة الأحدب للقائم عند محمد إذا بلغ حدبه حد الركوع، وتصح عندهما. (فتح، عيني)
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Imamate: No following by a person with wudu of a mutayammim, nor by a person washing of a person wiping, nor by a standing person of a seated or hunchbacked person. (Commentary) A person with wudu following a mutayammim: Muhammad said it is not permissible, because tayammum is a necessary purification that is only resorted to when unable. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said: it is a purification such that it is not restricted to the time of prayer. (On) a person wiping over leather socks or a bandage: due to equality of their states by consensus. And a standing person following a seated person because sitting is like standing, and Muhammad said: a person with wudu cannot follow a mutayammim nor a standing person a seated one. As for the non-permissibility in the first issue according to him, because the purity of the mutayammim is necessary and with water it is original, so it is building the strong on the weak. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is the hadith that Amr ibn al-As prayed with his companions while he was in a state of janabah doing tayammum and they were in wudu, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) knew about it but did not order them to repeat. And they agreed on validity in the funeral prayer. And it is said this difference is based on the fact that soil is a substitute for water according to them, so it acts as such, whereas according to Muhammad, purification with soil is a replacement for purification with water, so it is building the strong on the weak. As for the non-permissibility in the second issue according to him, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Let no one lead after me while sitting.' And for the two is the hadith of Aisha that he (peace be upon him) ordered Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer, and when Abu Bakr entered the prayer he felt lightness, so he stood supported between two men, then he came and sat to the left of Abu Bakr, and he (the Prophet) led the people sitting while Abu Bakr was standing, with Abu Bakr following the Prophet's prayer and the people following Abu Bakr's prayer, and this is explicit that he was the imam and Abu Bakr was the conveyer, because it is not permissible for the people to have two imams in one prayer, and this prayer was the zuhr prayer on Saturday or Sunday, and he died on Monday, and this is the origin of legislation for conveying (tabligh), and it is permissible by consensus when the congregation cannot hear the imam's voice due to weakness or large crowd, and the four schools agreed on the dislike of conveying when there is no need and said it is a reprehensible innovation. (Fath) Regarding the hunchback: it is called in Persian 'kuzeh pusht', whether his hunch reaches the level of bowing or not. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: the imamah of a hunchback for a standing person is not valid according to Muhammad if his hump reaches the level of bowing, and it is valid according to the two.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of certain types of imamah. The base text states the general rule: a person with wudu cannot follow a mutayammim, a person washing cannot follow a person wiping (over socks or bandage), a standing person cannot follow a seated or hunchbacked person. The commentary then explains the reasoning. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that a mutawaddi' can follow a mutayammim because tayammum is a valid purification that lifts hadath and is not time-restricted. Muhammad disagrees, arguing that tayammum is a necessary (darurah) purification, not original (asli), so it is weaker and cannot be followed by someone with stronger purity. The proof for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is the hadith of Amr ibn al-As, who led his companions in prayer after tayammum from janabah while they had wudu; the Prophet knew and did not order repetition. Muhammad's evidence for the standing/seated case is the hadith 'Let no one lead after me while sitting.' The two respond with the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet leading while sitting and Abu Bakr standing, which establishes tabligh (conveying) rather than direct imamah. The passage also covers the hunchback: according to Muhammad, if the hump reaches the level of ruku, the hunchback cannot lead a standing person because they would be in a constant bowing posture; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow it. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as indicated by the majority of the school.

Key Terms
متوضئ (mutawaddi'): A person who has performed wudu with water and is in a state of ritual purity.
متيمم (mutayammim): A person who has performed tayammum (dry ablution) due to absence or inability to use water.
أحدب (ahdab): A hunchbacked person whose back is curved significantly, possibly to the extent of resembling bowing posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, is it valid for a person with wudu to pray behind a mutayammim?
A) Yes, it is valid and recommended.
B) Yes, it is valid but disliked (makruh).
C) No, it is invalid and must be repeated.
D) It is permissible only in the funeral prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi allows a mutawaddi' to pray behind a mutayammim (makruh tanzihi), based on the Prophet's tacit approval, despite Muhammad's objection based on relative weakness of tayammum.

Imamah of a Mumi and a Mutanaffil Leading a Muftarid
Explains that a mumi leading a mumi is valid and a mutanaffil leading a muftarid is valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mumi leading another mumi and a mutanaffil leading a muftarid, and explain the underlying principle that the follower's prayer takes the ruling of the imam's prayer.

Core Idea
A mumi leads a mumi if postures match; a mutanaffil leads a muftarid because the follower's prayer adopts the imam's ruling.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two specific imamah scenarios that often raise questions. First, when the imam prays by gestures due to illness and the follower also prays by gestures, the imamah is valid as long as both are in similar postures. Second, the permissibility of a voluntary prayer imam leading an obligatory prayer follower is justified by a key Hanafi principle: the follower's prayer takes on the legal ruling of the imam's prayer. Understanding these rulings helps avoid confusion about the validity of congregational prayer in special circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Find the two distinct imamah scenarios presented: mumi leading mumi, and mutanaffil leading muftarid.
2
Note the condition for mumi imamah
Observe the condition: both must be in similar posture (standing or sitting). If imam is lying down and follower is standing or sitting, it is not permissible on the chosen view.
The passage uses 'على المختار' (on the chosen view) indicating a tarjih.
3
Understand the objection to mutanaffil leading muftarid
The objection: in the last two rak'ahs, recitation is obligatory for the voluntary imam but supererogatory for the obligatory follower, creating a mismatch.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response: the follower's prayer takes the ruling of the imam's prayer due to following (taba'iyyah). Thus, the recitation becomes supererogatory for the follower as well.
The passage says: 'صلاة المقتدي أخذت حكم صلاة الإمام بسبب الاقتداء'.
5
Conclude the practical application
The imamah is valid in both cases, with the stated conditions. The principle of subordination resolves the apparent conflict of intentions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومؤم بمثله : أي لا يفسد أيضاً اقتداء المؤمي بالمؤمي سواء كان الإمام قائماً أو قاعداً؛ لاستواء حالهما، وإن كان مضطجعاً والمؤتم قائماً أو قاعداً لا يجوز على المختار. (ط) ومتنفل بمفترض : أطلقه فعم اقتداء من يصلي التراويح بالمكتوبة لا يقال إن القراءة في الأخريين فرض في حق المتنفل نفل في حق المفترض، فيكون في الأخريين اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل وهو لا يجوز؛ لأنا نقول: صلاة المقتدي أخذت حكم صلاة الإمام بسبب الاقتداء، ولهذا يلزمه قضاء ما لم يدركه مع الإمام من الشفع الأول، وكذا لو أفسد المقتدي صلاته يلزمه أربع ركعات في الرباعية، فكان تبعاً للإمام، فتكون القراءة في الشفع الثاني نفلاً في حقه كما نفل في حق الإمام. (فتح)
And a mumi (one who gestures) with his like: that is, the following of one who gestures by another who also gestures does not invalidate, whether the imam is standing or sitting, because their states are equal. However, if the imam is lying down and the follower is standing or sitting, it is not permissible according to the chosen view. (T) And a voluntary prayer follower of an obligatory prayer: he generalised it to include the following of one performing taraweeh by one performing the obligatory prayer. It cannot be said that the recitation in the last two rak'ahs is obligatory for the voluntary prayer and supererogatory for the obligatory prayer, so in the last two rak'ahs there would be the following of the obligatory by the voluntary, which is not permissible; because we say: the prayer of the follower takes on the ruling of the imam's prayer due to following, and therefore he is obliged to make up what he missed with the imam from the first two rak'ahs. Similarly, if the follower invalidates his prayer, he is obliged to perform four rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer. So he is a follower of the imam, so the recitation in the second pair is supererogatory for him just as it is supererogatory for the imam. (Fath)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First, a person who prays by gestures (mumi) can validly lead another person who also prays by gestures, whether the imam is standing or sitting, because their postures are equivalent. However, if the imam is lying down and the follower is standing or sitting, it is not permitted on the chosen view. Second, a person performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer, such as taraweeh, can validly lead a person performing an obligatory (fard) prayer. The potential objection is that in the last two rak'ahs, recitation is obligatory for the voluntary prayer but supererogatory for the obligatory prayer, so in those rak'ahs the obligatory follower would be following the voluntary imam, which might be invalid. The response is that the follower's prayer takes on the ruling of the imam's prayer due to the act of following. Thus, if the follower misses the first pair of rak'ahs with the imam, he must make them up; if he invalidates his prayer, he must repeat four rak'ahs. So the follower is subordinate to the imam, and recitation in the last two rak'ahs becomes supererogatory for the follower just as it is for the imam. Thus, the imamah is valid.

Key Terms
مؤم (mumi): A person who prays by gestures (ima') due to illness or inability to bow and prostrate normally.
متنفل (mutanaffil): A person performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
مفترض (muftarid): A person performing an obligatory (fard) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a person performing taraweeh (nafl) lead a person performing Zuhr (fard) according to the Hanafi school?
A) No, because the imam's prayer is voluntary and cannot lead a fard.
B) Yes, because the follower takes the ruling of the imam's prayer.
C) Only if the follower has missed the first two rak'ahs.
D) Only if the imam is not in a lying down position.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a mutanaffil to lead a muftarid because the follower's prayer adopts the imam's ruling, and a mumi can lead another mumi if postures are similar.
