Discovery of Imam's Hadath: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on imam's hadath after prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules the followers' prayer invalid when the imam is discovered to have hadath, and contrast this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
If the imam's prayer is invalid, the followers' prayer built upon it is also invalid.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a critical inter-madhhab dispute: what happens when after prayer it is discovered that the imam was in a state of impurity? The Hanafi school holds that the followers must repeat their prayer, while the Shafi'i school considers their prayer valid if they were unaware. Through prophetic hadith and scholarly reasoning, the Hanafi position is established.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the followers' prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated, whether the imam had minor impurity (hadath) or major impurity (janabah).
This applies regardless of the followers' knowledge.
2
Identify the opposing Shafi'i view
The Shafi'i school holds that the followers' prayer is valid if they were unaware of the imam's impurity, based on the narration of Umar (RA) and the principle that each person's prayer is independent.
Umar (RA) is reported to have prayed while junub and only repeated his own prayer.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi school rejects the Umar narration because it is contradicted by an explicit prophetic hadith and the practice of Ali (RA). The hadith directly states: 'If the imam's prayer becomes invalid, then the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.'
The hadith is considered stronger evidence (dalil naqli).
4
Examine the Hanafi proof (qiyas)
The follower's prayer is built (mabniyyah) upon the imam's prayer. If the foundation is invalid, the superstructure is invalid. This is analogy (qiyas) to the Friday prayer and to cases where the imam is discovered to be a kafir or insane.
By consensus, those cases also invalidate the followers' prayer.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, the congregation must repeat the prayer. In the Shafi'i school, they do not repeat unless they also had impurity.
This difference matters in daily congregational life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محدث أو جنب أو في ثوبه أو بدنه نجاسة. أعاد [ أي المقتدى مطلقاً . سواء كان محدثا أو جنباً خلافاً للشافعي، ويلزم للإمام إعلام القوم لو معينين بالقدر الممكن، ولو بكتاب أو رسول، ولو أخبر الإمام أنه كان مجوسياً لا يقبل قوله وصلاة القوم جائزة. (مسكين)] خلافاً لما روي عن عمر الله : أنه صلى بالناس وهو جنب، وأعاد ولم يأمر القوم بالإعادة، ولنا قوله عليه: "إذا فسدت صلاة الإمام فسدت صلاة خلفه"، وعن علي ه: أنه عليها صلى بهم ثم جاء ورأسه يقطر ماءً وأعاد بهم؛ ولأن صلاته مبنية على صلاة الإمام والبناء على الفاسد فاسد فصار كالجمعة، وكما إذا بان أن الإمام كافر أو مجنون أو امرأة أو خنثى أو أمّي، فإنه لا يجوز بالإجماع. (فتح)
If the imam is in a state of minor hadath or janabah, or if there is impurity on his garment or body, he repeats. (The commentary says:) That is, the follower repeats absolutely, whether the imam was in minor hadath or janabah, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And it is obligatory for the imam to inform the people if they are specific individuals, to the extent possible, even by writing or a messenger. And if the imam informs them that he was a Magian, his statement is not accepted and the people's prayer is valid. Contrary to what is narrated from Umar ibn al-Khattab that he prayed with the people while in janabah and repeated but did not order the people to repeat. And our proof is his statement (peace be upon him): 'If the imam's prayer becomes invalid, then the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' And from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he led them in prayer, then came with water dripping from his head and repeated with them. And because his prayer is built on the imam's prayer, and building on an invalid foundation is invalid, so it becomes like the Friday prayer, and just as if it becomes apparent that the imam was an unbeliever, or insane, or a woman, or a hermaphrodite, or an ummi, it is not permissible by consensus.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage deals with the case where after the prayer it is discovered that the imam was in a state of hadath (minor impurity) or janabah (major impurity), or had impurity on his body or clothes. The ruling is that the followers' prayer is invalid and must be repeated. This is the Hanafi position, which differs from al-Shafi'i, who holds that the followers' prayer is valid if they were unaware. The proof is the hadith: 'If the imam's prayer becomes invalid, then the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' Additionally, the practice of Ali (RA) supports this: after leading prayer, he discovered he was in janabah, so he repeated the prayer with the people. The analogy is that the follower's prayer is built upon the imam's prayer; if the foundation is invalid, the superstructure is invalid. This is analogous to the Friday prayer, where if the imam's prayer is invalid, the followers' prayer is also invalid. It is also similar to cases where the imam is discovered to be an unbeliever, insane, a woman, a hermaphrodite, or an ummi (illiterate) - all render the prayer invalid by consensus. The text also notes that the imam is obligated to inform the congregation if he knows, but if he falsely claims he was a Magian (meaning he was not Muslim), his claim is not accepted and the congregation's prayer remains valid.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdath): A person in a state of minor impurity (hadath asghar) that invalidates wudu.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if after the prayer it is discovered that the imam was in a state of janabah, what must the followers do?
A) Their prayer is valid, no action needed.
B) Only the imam must repeat his prayer.
C) Both the imam and the followers must repeat their prayers.
D) They must repeat only if the imam knew he was in janabah.

Key Takeaway
The followers' prayer is invalid when the imam's prayer is found to be invalid, regardless of their knowledge, due to the derivative nature of congregational prayer.

Followers Must Repeat When Imam Was Impure
Ruling and proof for repeating prayer when imam was in state of impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires followers to repeat their prayer when the imam was impure and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
If the imam's prayer is invalid, the followers' prayer is invalid too — because it is built upon his.

Imagine you prayed behind an imam, then after the prayer you discovered that the imam had been in a state of impurity (hadath) during the prayer. Did your prayer count? In the Hanafi school, it does not: you must repeat your prayer. This lesson explores the ruling, its proofs, and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on the followers' prayer when the imam was impure? The text states 'He repeats' – meaning the follower must repeat the prayer. This is a wajib (obligatory) repetition.
The ruling applies whether the imam had minor impurity (muhdith) or major impurity (junub).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'If the prayer of the imam becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' Also the action of 'Ali (RA) who repeated with the people after realizing he was junub.
These are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut) but their meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses a conditional clause (idha…fasada…fasada) indicating a direct causal link: the invalidity of the imam's prayer necessarily causes invalidity for followers. Additionally, qiyas (analogy) is used: the follower's prayer is built upon the imam's prayer; building upon something invalid yields an invalid result.
This is similar to the ruling of Jumu'ah prayer if the imam's prayer is invalid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text explicitly says 'contrary to al-Shafi'i'. Al-Shafi'i holds that only the imam repeats his prayer; the followers' prayer is valid because they followed in good faith.
The Hanafi response is that the follower's prayer is dependent on the imam's validity, not on the follower's knowledge.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) within the school. It is based on strong textual evidence and qiyas. The opposing view is considered weak if the imam's impurity is certain.
If the imam claims after prayer that he was a Magian (disbeliever), his claim is not accepted due to the presumption of Islam; the followers' prayer remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعاد [ أي المقتدى مطلقاً . سواء كان محدثا أو جنباً خلافاً للشافعي، ويلزم للإمام إعلام القوم لو معينين بالقدر الممكن، ولو بكتاب أو رسول، ولو أخبر الإمام أنه كان مجوسياً لا يقبل قوله وصلاة القوم جائزة. (مسكين)] خلافاً لما روي عن عمر الله : أنه صلى بالناس وهو جنب، وأعاد ولم يأمر القوم بالإعادة، ولنا قوله عليه: "إذا فسدت صلاة الإمام فسدت صلاة خلفه"، وعن علي ه: أنه عليها صلى بهم ثم جاء ورأسه يقطر ماءً وأعاد بهم؛ ولأن صلاته مبنية على صلاة الإمام والبناء على الفاسد فاسد فصار كالجمعة، وكما إذا بان أن الإمام كافر أو مجنون أو امرأة أو خنثى أو أمّي، فإنه لا يجوز بالإجماع. (فتح)
He repeats [the prayer]. That is, the follower absolutely. Whether the imam was in a state of minor impurity or janabah, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And it is incumbent upon the imam to inform the people, if known, to the extent possible, even by a letter or a messenger. And if the imam claims he was a Magian, his statement is not accepted and the prayer of the people is valid. (Miskin) Contrary to what is narrated from 'Umar (Allah be pleased with him): that he prayed with the people while in janabah, and he repeated but did not command the people to repeat. And for us is his statement (peace be upon him): 'If the prayer of the imam becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' And from 'Ali (Allah be pleased with him): that he prayed with them, then came while water dripped from his head, and he repeated with them. And because his prayer is built upon the prayer of the imam, and building upon what is invalid is invalid, so it becomes like Jumu'ah, and as if it becomes apparent that the imam is a disbeliever, insane, a woman, a hermaphrodite, or illiterate, for which it is not valid by consensus. (Fath)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that if it becomes known after the prayer that the imam was in a state of impurity (hadath), whether minor or major (janabah), the followers must repeat their prayer. This is the Hanafi position, opposed to al-Shafi'i who holds that only the imam repeats. The text provides several proofs: a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that the follower's prayer is based on the imam's, the action of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who repeated with the people, and an analogy (qiyas) to cases where the imam is found to be a disbeliever, insane, etc., where all agree the prayer is invalid. The text also notes the obligation on the imam to inform the congregation if he knows of his impurity beforehand. If the imam claims after the prayer that he was a Magian (i.e., a disbeliever), his claim is not accepted because of the presumption of Islam, and the people's prayer remains valid.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdith): One who is in a state of minor impurity (hadath)
جنب (junub): One who is in a state of major impurity requiring ghusl
مقتدى (muqtadi): The follower in prayer, i.e., the one who prays behind an imam

Ruling on the Illiterate Imam and Its Implications
Ruling on prayer validity when illiterate imam leads and when replaced by illiterate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer when an illiterate imam leads a congregation containing a literate person, and evaluate the effect of replacing the imam with another illiterate in the final rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Every rak'ah requires recitation; an illiterate cannot provide it, so leading a literate person invalidates the prayer.

This lesson delves into a specific Hanafi ruling concerning the illiterate (ummi) imam. The key principle is that each rak'ah of prayer must include recitation of the Quran, either directly or by estimation. An illiterate person lacks the ability to recite, so his prayer is deficient. When he leads others, the presence of a literate follower triggers invalidity. Additionally, if he appoints another illiterate as his successor in the last rak'ahs, further complications arise. We will examine the positions of Abu Hanifa and his disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled? The prayer of an illiterate imam leading a mixed congregation. Ruling: invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
The reasoning: every rak'ah requires recitation; the illiterate cannot fulfill it.
The text uses the principle that recitation is a pillar of each rak'ah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalala
The need for recitation is derived from the Quranic command to recite, and the illiterate cannot provide actual or estimative recitation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Sahibayn differ on the first issue; Abu Yusuf and Zufar differ on the second.
The two companions hold that the imam's prayer is valid if there are illiterate followers; only the literate follower's prayer is invalid.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, as indicated by the text and later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فسدت صلاتهم الأن كل ركعة صلاة فلا تخلو عن القراءة تحقيقاً أو تقديراً، ولا تقدير في الأمي لعدم أهليته، وكذا الإمام؛ لأن استخلافه عمل كثير من غير ضرورة لعدم الحاجة لاستخلاف من لا يصلح. (فتح)] سواء علم الإمام أن خلفه قارئاً أم لم يعلم، أما المسألة الأولى أي اقتداء أمي وقارئ بأمي- ففيها خلاف الصاحبين، فإنهما قالا: صلاة الإمام ومن لا يقرأ تامة، وذكر عبد الله الجرجاني : أن صلاة الإمام إنما تفسد عنده إذا علم أن خلفه قارئاً، وأما إذا لم يعلم ،فلا وأما المسألة الثانية – أي استخلاف أمي في الأخريين، ولو في التشهد قبل الفراغ - ففيها خلاف أبي يوسف وزفر، فإنهما قالا : لا تفسد صلاتهم؛ لتأدي فرض القراءة في الأوليين، أما لو استخلفه بعد التشهد صحت الصلاة بالإجماع؛ لخروجه بصنعه. (مسكين)
Their prayer becomes invalid because every rak'ah is a prayer, and it is not free from recitation either actually or estimatively, and there is no estimative recitation for the illiterate due to lack of eligibility, and likewise the imam; because his appointing a successor is a large action without necessity, as there is no need to appoint one who is not suitable. (Fath) Whether the imam knows that behind him there is a reciter or not. As for the first issue – i.e., an illiterate and a reciter following an illiterate – there is a difference of opinion among the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). They said: The prayer of the imam and the one who does not recite is complete. And 'Abdullah al-Jurjani mentioned that the imam's prayer is only invalidated according to him if he knows that behind him there is a reciter; if he does not know, then not. As for the second issue – i.e., appointing an illiterate successor in the last two rak'ahs, even in the tashahhud before finishing – there is a difference of opinion between Abu Yusuf and Zufar. They said: Their prayer does not become invalid because the obligation of recitation has been fulfilled in the first two rak'ahs. But if he appointed him after the tashahhud, the prayer is valid by consensus, because he has left the prayer by his own action. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues concerning the illiterate (ummi) imam. First, if an illiterate imam leads a prayer that includes both a literate (qari') and an illiterate follower, the prayer of the congregation becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa. This is because every rak'ah requires recitation, either actually (if the person can read) or estimatively (if the person cannot read, a reading is deemed to occur). An illiterate person cannot have estimative recitation, so the prayer is invalid. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the prayer of the illiterate imam and the illiterate follower is valid; only the literate follower's prayer is invalid. 'Abdullah al-Jurjani adds a nuance: Abu Hanifa's ruling applies only if the imam knows there is a literate person behind him; if he is unaware, his prayer is valid. The second issue is when an illiterate imam appoints another illiterate person as his successor (istikhlaf) during the last two rak'ahs. According to Abu Hanifa, this invalidates the prayer of the entire congregation because the appointed person cannot recite. Abu Yusuf and Zufar disagree, arguing that since the obligation of recitation was fulfilled in the first two rak'ahs, the replacement does not invalidate the prayer. However, if the replacement occurs after the tashahhud (when the prayer is essentially complete), all agree the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
أمي (ummi): An illiterate person who cannot read the Quran
قارئ (qari'): A person who can recite the Quran properly
استخلاف (istikhlaf): The act of the imam appointing another person to lead the remainder of the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if an illiterate (ummi) imam leads a prayer that includes a literate follower (qari'), what is the ruling on the prayer?
A) The prayer is valid for all.
B) The prayer of the imam and illiterate follower is valid; the literate follower's prayer is invalid.
C) The prayer of the entire congregation is invalid.
D) The prayer is valid if the imam did not know there was a literate follower.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the prayer of an illiterate imam is invalid when a literate person follows him, and appointing another illiterate in the last rak'ahs also invalidates the prayer.

Building (Bina) After Hadath in Prayer
Definition and conditions for building upon prayer after hadath occurs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building after hadath, identify the conditions, and differentiate between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
Prayer interrupted by minor hadath can be resumed after wudu – building is the Hanafi default.

This lesson explains the unique Hanafi concept of building (bina) when a minor pre-emptive event occurs during prayer. Unlike other schools that require restart, the Hanafi school permits continuation under specific conditions, supported by a prophetic hadith. Understanding the conditions and the rationale behind building helps appreciate Hanafi fiqh's practical flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is building (bina) after hadath. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) when conditions are met, but starting anew (isti'naf) is also permissible.
The text states: 'يجب عليه أن ينصرف ويتوضأ ويبني' - it is obligatory to leave, perform wudu, and build.
2
List the conditions for building
The text enumerates several conditions: the hadath must not require ghusl, not be rare, the person did not perform a pillar, did no avoidable contradictory act, did not delay without excuse, etc.
These conditions ensure the continuity of the original prayer is not broken.
3
Compare with the opposing view
Al-Shafi'i requires restarting the prayer. The Hanafi proof is a hadith from Ibn Majah explicitly permitting building; the Shafi'i proof is interpreted as either recommendatory or applying when conditions are absent.
The disagreement is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the ruling to different roles
An imam should appoint a successor; a follower (muqtadi) should build to preserve congregation; one praying alone has the choice but starting anew is better.
The ruling varies based on the role to maintain the virtue of jama'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحدث في الصلاة ك ف و باب الحدث في الصلاة ك ف س من سبقه حدث توضأ وبنى واستخلف لو إماماً، كما لو حصر من يصلح للإمامة يستخلف عجز باب الحدث إلخ : أي هذا باب بيان أحكام سبق الحدث، ففي العنوان حذف المبتدأ ومضافين، وإقامة المضاف إليه مقامهما لعدم الالتباس، وأخره لكونه من العوارض وقدمه على المفسدات؛ لأنه قد لا يكون مفسداً، والحدث وصف شرعي يحل بالأعضاء يزيل الطهارة، وحكمه المانعية مما جعلت الطهارة شرطاً له. (فتح) حدث: [سماوي غير مانع للبناء كالجنابة. (ط)] ولو من تنحنح أو عطاس، وهو الصحيح، وقيد بالسبق؛ لأنه لو خاف الحدث فانصرف، ثم سبقه استأنف، والمراد بالحدث: أن يكون غير موجب لغسل، ولا نادر الوجود، ولم يؤد ركناً، و لم يفعل منافياً له منه بد، ولم يتراخ بلا عذر لزحمة، ولم يظهر حدثه السابق كمضي مدة مسحه، و لم يتذكر فائتة وهو ذو ترتيب، ولم يستخلف غير صالح لها، فصاحب هذا النوع من الحدث يبني صلاته على ما مضى. (فتح) وبني ولو منفردا أو امرأة على صلاته والاستئناف أفضل. (ط)] أي يجب عليه أن ينصرف ويتوضأ ويبني، أي يتم ما بقي من صلاته إن شاء، وإن شاء استأنف أي ترك ما مضى وصلى من الابتداء، ويشترط للبناء أن لا يمكث أداء قدر ركن، وأن لا يفعل المنافي للصلاة حالة الذهاب للتوضئ والإياب، وأن لا يفعل فعلاً. منه بد كالذهاب إلى موضع أبعد مع تيسر التوضئ في موضع أقرب، وأن لا يتراخى بعد الفراغ من الوضوء بلا عذر، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز له البناء بل يستأنف؛ لفساد الصلاة بانتقاض الطهارة والمشي للتوضئ؛ وللحديث الوارد: "إذا فسا أحدكم في الصلاة فلينصرف وليتوضأ وليعد الصلاة، أخرجه أصحاب السنن ولنا قوله عليه: "من قاء أو رعف في صلاته فلينصرف وليتوضأ وليبن على صلاته ما لم يتكلم" ، أخرجه ابن ماجه، والحديث السابق محمول على الاستحباب، أو على ما إذا فقد شرطاً من شروط البناء، والحديث الثاني مذهب الخلفاء الراشدين، وكلمة "من" تتناول الإمام والمنفرد والمقتدي، والأولى للمنفرد أن يستقبل وللمقتدي أن يبني؛ إحرازاً لفضيلة الجماعة، فالمنفرد بعد الوضوء يتخير بين إتمام صلاته في بيته، وبين رجوعه إلى مصلاه وهو أفضل، والمقتدي يعود إلى مكانه إن لم يفرغ إمامه من الصلاة، ولو أتم بقية صلاته في بيته لم يجز إلا أن يكون بيته بحذاء المسجد بحيث لو اقتداءه، وإن كان إمامه قد فرغ يتخير. (فتح، عيني)
Chapter on Hadath in Prayer. Whoever is overtaken by hadath (pre-emptive event) should perform wudu and build (bina) and appoint a successor if he is an imam, just as if he is constrained (to appoint) one who is suitable for imamate, he appoints a successor if unable. ... The chapter on hadath: i.e., this is a chapter explaining the rulings of being overtaken by hadath. In the title, the subject and two genitives are omitted, and the genitive is placed in their position to avoid ambiguity. He delayed it because it is among the incidental matters, and he presented it before the invalidators because it may not be an invalidator. Hadath is a legal description that occurs in the limbs, removing purity; its ruling is prevention from that for which purity is made a condition. (Fath) Hadath: [celestial, not preventing building like janabah. (T) Even from clearing the throat or sneezing, and this is the correct view. It is restricted by 'overtaken' because if he feared the hadath and left, then it overtook him, he must start anew. The intended meaning of hadath is: that which does not necessitate ghusl, and is not rare in occurrence, and he did not perform a pillar, and he did not do something contradictory from which he had no alternative, and he did not delay without an excuse such as crowding, and his previous hadath did not become apparent such as the expiry of his wiping period, and he did not remember an missed prayer while he is one who observes order, and he did not appoint a successor who is not suitable for it. So the possessor of this type of hadath builds his prayer upon what has passed. (Fath) He builds even if he is alone or a woman upon his prayer, and starting anew is better. (T) i.e., it is obligatory upon him to leave, perform wudu, and build, i.e., complete the remainder of his prayer if he wishes, and if he wishes he may start anew, i.e., leave what has passed and pray from the beginning. Conditions for building: that he does not remain for the duration of performing a pillar, that he does not do anything contradictory to the prayer while going and returning for wudu, that he does not do an act from which he has no alternative such as going to a farther place when wudu is available nearer, and that he does not delay after finishing wudu without an excuse. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible for him to build; rather he must start anew, because the prayer is invalidated by the breaking of purity and walking for wudu, and because of the hadith: 'If any of you passes wind during prayer, let him leave, perform wudu, and repeat the prayer.' This is narrated by the authors of the Sunan. And for us is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever vomits or has a nosebleed during his prayer, let him leave, perform wudu, and build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.' Narrated by Ibn Majah. The previous hadith is interpreted as recommendatory, or as when a condition of building is missing. The second hadith is the way of the rightly-guided caliphs. The word 'whoever' includes the imam, the one praying alone, and the follower. It is better for the one alone to start anew, and for the follower to build, in order to preserve the virtue of congregation. So the one alone after wudu has the choice between completing his prayer in his house and returning to his prayer place, and returning is better. The follower should return to his place if his imam has not finished the prayer; if he completes the remainder of his prayer in his house, it is not permissible unless his house is adjacent to the mosque such that he could follow the imam. If his imam has finished, he has the choice. (Fath, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on hadath in prayer provides a detailed ruling on what a person should do when overtaken by a pre-emptive event (like breaking wind, vomiting, etc.) during prayer. The Hanafi school permits building (bina), i.e., performing wudu and continuing from the point where the event occurred, provided certain conditions are met. These conditions include: the event is not a major impurity (janabah), it is not rare, the person did not perform a pillar during the event, did not do an avoidable contradictory act, did not delay unnecessarily, etc. The builder may also choose to start the prayer anew, which is considered better for one praying alone but not for a follower (who should build to maintain congregation). The text contrasts the Hanafi position with that of al-Shafi'i, who requires the prayer to be restarted entirely. The Hanafi proof is a hadith explicitly permitting building after vomiting or nosebleed, while the Shafi'i proof (a hadith about passing wind) is interpreted as recommending a new start or applying when conditions for building are not met.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A pre-emptive event that invalidates wudu, such as passing wind, vomiting, etc.
بناء (bina): Continuing the prayer from where it was interrupted after performing wudu
استئناف (isti'naf): Starting the prayer anew from the beginning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the permissibility of building (bina) after hadath in the Hanafi school?
A) The hadath must require ghusl.
B) The person must not have performed a pillar after the hadath.
C) The person must speak to indicate he is still in prayer.
D) The imam must always appoint a successor.

Key Takeaway
Building (bina) after a minor hadath is permitted in the Hanafi school under specific conditions, allowing the worshiper to continue the same prayer after wudu.

Ruling on Imam Appointing a Successor (Istikhlaf) After Hadath
Rules for imam appointing a successor when overtaken by hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and method of istikhlaf according to the Hanafi school and identify what invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
The imam must appoint a successor by gesture before leaving; speaking invalidates the prayer.

When an imam is overtaken by hadath and must leave for wudu, he cannot simply abandon the congregation. Islamic law provides a procedure for appointing a successor (istikhlaf) to preserve the prayer's validity. This lesson details the Hanafi rulings on who may be appointed, how the transfer is made, and what time and action limits apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause for istikhlaf
Determine when istikhlaf becomes necessary: when the imam is overtaken by hadath (e.g., breaking wudu) or any other reason that forces him to leave the prayer.
The imam must intend to return or appoint a successor; merely leaving invalidates the prayer.
2
Determine the eligible appointee
Identify who can be appointed: a suitable person from the congregation, preferably from the row immediately behind. A man cannot appoint a woman for a male congregation; for a female congregation, a woman may be appointed.
A masbuq (latecomer) is less preferred because he missed part of the prayer.
3
Describe the proper method of appointment
The imam must appoint by gesture (e.g., pulling the person forward) and should avoid speaking. Speaking invalidates the prayer of the followers. The imam should also subtly signal his reason (e.g., pretending to have a nosebleed) to avoid suspicion.
4
Specify the time and place limits
The imam may appoint only before leaving the mosque (or passing all rows in an open space). If he leaves without appointing, the followers' prayer becomes invalid; there are two narrations regarding the imam's own prayer.
5
Note the successor's actions
The successor should step forward before the imam leaves the prayer area and intend to be the imam. If he delays, the validity of his following is affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستخلف [ والمدرك للاستخلاف أولى من لاحق ومسبوق. (ط)] أي يجر الإمام من كان صالحاً المقتدين من للإمامة إلى مكانه حتى لو استخلف امرأة فسدت صلاة المأمومين ولو نساء، ويتأخر بنفسه محدودبا واضعا يده على أنفه، يوهم أنه قد رعف فينقطع عنه الظنون، ولا يستخلف بالكلام بل بالإشارة، ولو تكلم بطلت صلاتهم خلافاً لمالك، ويقدّم من الصف الذي يليه، وله أن يستخلف ما لم يجاوز الصفوف في الصحراء، وفي المسجد ما لم يخرج منه، ولو لم يستخلف حتى جاوز الكل بطلت صلاة القوم، وفي صلاة الإمام روايتان. رمز الحقائق: ۷۰/۱] ثم إذا استخلف ينبغي للخليفة أن يقوم مقامه قبل خروجه من المسجد، وينوي أن يكون إماماً، ولو لم يقم إلا بعد = اقتدی به صح
And he appoints a successor. [And the one who is aware of the appointment is more entitled than one who is later or one who is lagging behind (mashuq). (T)] i.e., the imam pulls forward one who is suitable for imamate from the followers to his place, such that if he appoints a woman as successor, the prayer of the male followers becomes invalid, even if they are women. And he himself moves back, stooping, placing his hand on his nose, giving the impression that he has a nosebleed, so that suspicions end. He does not appoint by speech but by gesture; if he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid, contrary to Malik. And he appoints from the row next to him. He may appoint as long as he has not passed the rows in the desert, and in the mosque as long as he has not left it. If he does not appoint until after passing all, the prayer of the people becomes invalid; regarding the imam's prayer, there are two narrations. (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 70/1) Then, when he appoints, it is proper for the successor to take his place before he leaves the mosque, and to intend to be imam. If he does not take his place except after [the imam leaves], his following is valid? (cut off)
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for istikhlaf (appointing a successor) when the imam is overtaken by hadath and needs to leave for wudu. The imam should select a suitable person, preferably from the row immediately behind him, by pulling him forward with a gesture, not by speaking (speaking would invalidate the prayer). He should signal that he is leaving due to a nosebleed to avoid suspicion. He cannot appoint a woman as successor, as that would invalidate the men's prayer. He may only appoint before leaving the mosque or passing the rows in an open space. If he delays until after leaving completely, the followers' prayer is invalid, though there are two narrations on whether the imam's own prayer is also invalid. The successor should step forward before the imam leaves the prayer area and intend to be imam.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaf): The imam's act of appointing another person to lead the remainder of the prayer due to his own inability to continue
خليفة (khalifah): The person appointed to succeed the imam in leading the prayer
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joined the prayer late (after the first rak'ah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How should an imam appoint a successor (istikhlaf) when overtaken by hadath, according to the Hanafi school?
A) By saying 'You lead the prayer' to a suitable person.
B) By gesturing and pulling forward a suitable person from the row.
C) By leaving silently and letting the congregation choose someone.
D) By making a gesture only if he has no suitable person behind him.

Key Takeaway
The imam must appoint a successor by gesture before leaving; failure to do so invalidates the followers' prayer.

Building After a Preceding Hadath: Ruling and Conditions
Commentary on building after hadath with conditions and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building after a preceding hadath, list the conditions for valid building, and explain the proof and the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Building after a minor hadath is permitted; restarting is superior for the individual.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a practical concern: what should a person do if they experience a minor hadath (like a nosebleed or passing wind) while in prayer? The Hanafi school provides a middle path: one may perform wudu and continue the prayer from where it stopped (building), but restarting is also allowed and preferred for the one praying alone. Understanding the conditions and the proof behind this ruling will help you navigate unexpected situations in salah with confidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is 'building' (al-bina') — continuing the prayer after a hadath. What is the hukm level? The text states it is permissible and preferable, but restarting is also allowed and is afdal (better) for the individual.
The ruling is not wajib; it is sunnah muakkadah for those who choose to build.
2
Define the type of hadath that allows building
Not every hadath permits building. The hadath must not require ghusl (i.e., it is minor), must not be rare, must not have occurred after performing a complete rak'ah, and the person must not have done a violating act like speaking. List the conditions from the text.
This narrows the scope significantly.
3
List the conditions for valid building
The text enumerates conditions during the act of building: no delaying the performance of a pillar, no committing a violation during wudu (e.g., speaking), no going to a distant place for wudu unnecessarily, and no delaying after completing wudu without an excuse.
These ensure the prayer remains uninterrupted in spirit.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'Whoever vomits or has a nosebleed in his prayer, let him perform wudu and build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.' (Ibn Majah). Identify the imperative and its legal implication.
The imperative indicates permissibility, not obligation.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith: 'If one of you passes wind in prayer, let him leave and perform wudu and repeat the prayer.' The Hanafi response interprets this as recommending restarting or applying when conditions for building are absent. The Hanafi proof is upheld by the practice of the caliphs.
This is a classic case of ta'arud (conflict of evidences) resolved by tarjih.

(فتح) حدث: [سماوي غير مانع للبناء كالجنابة. (فتح، عيني)
The chapter of hadath etc.: i.e., this chapter is about explaining the rulings of the precedence of hadath. In the title, the predicate and two additions are omitted, and the annexed is placed in their place to avoid confusion. It is delayed because it is from the incidental matters and is placed before the invalidators because it may not be invalidating. Hadath is a legal description that arises in the limbs, removing purification. Its ruling is prevention from that for which purification is made a condition. (Fath) Hadath: [heavenly?] that does not prevent building, like janabah. (Tahawi) Even if from clearing the throat or sneezing, and this is correct. It is restricted to 'preceding' because if he fears hadath and leaves, then it precedes him, he restarts. What is meant by hadath is that it does not necessitate ghusl, is not rare, he has not performed a rak'ah, he does not do something that necessarily causes a violation, he does not delay without an excuse due to crowding, his previous hadath does not appear like the expiry of his wipe period, he does not remember a missed prayer while he is one who observes order, and he does not appoint someone unfit for it. The one with this type of hadath builds his prayer on what has passed. (Fath) 'And he builds, even if alone or a woman, on his prayer, and restarting is superior.' (Tahawi) i.e., he must leave and perform wudu and build, i.e., complete what remains of his prayer if he wishes, and if he wishes he restarts, i.e., leaves what passed and prays from the beginning. Conditions for building: that he does not delay the performance of a pillar, that he does not do something that violates the prayer while going for wudu and returning, that he does not do something unnecessary like going to a further place when wudu is easy nearby, that he does not delay after completing wudu without excuse. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible for him to build; rather he must restart because the prayer is invalidated by the nullification of purification and walking for wudu, and due to the hadith: 'If one of you passes wind in prayer, let him leave and perform wudu and repeat the prayer.' Narrated by the authors of Sunan. And our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever vomits or has a nosebleed in his prayer, let him leave and perform wudu and build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.' Narrated by Ibn Majah. The previous hadith is interpreted as recommendation or for when a condition of building is missing. The second hadith is the practice of the rightly guided caliphs. The word 'man' includes the imam, the individual, and the follower. It is better for the individual to restart, and for the follower to build, to preserve the virtue of congregation. The individual after wudu has the choice between completing his prayer at home and returning to his prayer place, and returning is better. The follower returns to his place if his imam has not finished the prayer. If he completes the rest of his prayer at home, it is not permissible unless his home is adjacent to the mosque such that if he follows... and if his imam has finished, he has the choice. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of building (bina) after a preceding hadath in prayer. The commentator first explains the chapter title, noting that 'hadath' is a legal description that nullifies purification, but here it refers specifically to hadath that does not prevent building on the prayer. The types of hadath that allow building are those that do not require ghusl, are not rare, occur before performing a rak'ah, do not involve a necessary violation, and other conditions. The original ruling from the matn states that when such a hadath precedes, the person should perform wudu and build on the prayer, but they may also choose to restart. The commentator then lists conditions for building: not delaying a pillar, not doing something that violates the prayer, not going to a distant place for wudu without need, and not delaying after wudu. The Shafi'i view is presented: they require restarting because the prayer is invalidated by the hadath and walking. The hashiya cites two hadiths: one that seems to support restarting (about passing wind), and the Hanafi proof hadith about vomiting or nosebleed. The Hanafi response reconciles them by stating the first hadith is for recommendation or when conditions of building are absent, and the second is the practice of the caliphs. The commentator also discusses preferences: it is better for the individual (munfarid) to restart, and for the follower (muqtadi) to build. The follower should return to his place if the imam hasn't finished; otherwise he may choose.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): A legal description that arises in the limbs, removing purification. Here it refers to a minor hadath that does not require ghusl and is not rare.
البناء (al-bina'): Continuing the prayer from where it was interrupted after performing wudu, as opposed to restarting the entire prayer.
الاستئناف (al-isti'naf): Restarting the prayer from the beginning, which is also permissible but considered superior for the individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which condition is NOT required for building after hadath according to the Hanafi text?
A) The hadath must not require ghusl.
B) The hadath must be rare.
C) The hadath must occur before performing a full rak'ah.
D) The person must not speak during the process.

Key Takeaway
Building after a preceding hadath is a sunnah provision in Hanafi fiqh, subject to specific conditions that preserve the validity of the prayer and provide ease for the worshipper.

Appointing a Substitute Imam (Istikhlaf): Rules and Procedures
Ruling with proof on istikhlaf procedures and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of istikhlaf, apply the conditions for its validity, and distinguish the Hanafi position on appointing a substitute when the imam cannot recite due to fatigue or shyness (hissar).

Core Idea
The imam must appoint a substitute by gesture only, feigning a nosebleed, and the substitute must be a suitable male from the nearest row.

When an imam cannot complete the prayer due to a valid excuse, he may appoint a substitute (istikhlaf) to preserve the congregation's prayer. The Hanafi school specifies a precise procedure to avoid nullifying the prayer: the imam must use gestures, not speech, and pretend to have a nosebleed to prevent suspicion. This commentary also addresses an intra-madhhab dispute regarding inability to recite (hissar) and the binding consensus when the imam has already recited enough.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Istikhlaf is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasised recommendation) for the imam when he cannot continue. The passage prescribes specific actions to ensure the congregation's prayer remains valid.
The ruling is not fard or wajib; it is an option to preserve the prayer.
2
Understand the method of appointment
The imam must pull a suitable person from the followers forward by gesture, not speech. If he speaks, the prayer becomes invalid. He should retreat bending forward, placing his hand on his nose to pretend he has a nosebleed.
This avoids whispers of doubt. The gesture can be a tap or a pointing motion.
3
Determine who can be appointed
The substitute must be a suitable male follower. Appointing a woman invalidates the prayer of the congregation, even if the followers are all women.
The phrase 'من كان صالحاً للإمامة' indicates the substitute must be qualified.
4
Apply place and timing limitations
In an open area (desert), the imam may appoint as long as he has not passed the rows. In a mosque, as long as he has not left the mosque. If he delays and exceeds these boundaries, the congregation's prayer becomes invalid.
The substitute should stand in place before the imam leaves the mosque and must intend to be the imam.
5
Analyze the special case of hissar (inability to recite)
If the imam cannot recite due to shyness, fatigue, or similar (hissar), Abu Hanifa permits istikhlaf provided the imam has not yet recited the minimum amount for validity. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. The text sides with Abu Hanifa as the relied-upon view.
If the imam has already recited enough (e.g., one verse), he must bow and cannot appoint a substitute—by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستخلف [ والمدرك للاستخلاف أولى من لاحق ومسبوق. (ط)] أي يجر الإمام من كان صالحاً المقتدين من للإمامة إلى مكانه حتى لو استخلف امرأة فسدت صلاة المأمومين ولو نساء، ويتأخر بنفسه محدودبا واضعا يده على أنفه، يوهم أنه قد رعف فينقطع عنه الظنون، ولا يستخلف بالكلام بل بالإشارة، ولو تكلم بطلت صلاتهم خلافاً لمالك، ويقدّم من الصف الذي يليه، وله أن يستخلف ما لم يجاوز الصفوف في الصحراء، وفي المسجد ما لم يخرج منه، ولو لم يستخلف حتى جاوز الكل بطلت صلاة القوم، وفي صلاة الإمام روايتان. رمز الحقائق: ۷۰/۱] ثم إذا استخلف ينبغي للخليفة أن يقوم مقامه قبل خروجه من المسجد، وينوي أن يكون إماماً، ولو لم يقم إلا بعد = عن القراءة: الحصر: العي وضيق الصدر، أي منع الإمام عن القراءة الخجل أو التعب ونحوهما في الصلاة، فاستخلف أحداً جاز عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما، هذا إذا لم يقرأ قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة، فإن قرأ عليه أن يركع، ولم يجز الاستخلاف إجماعاً، وكذا إذا نسى القرآن وصار أمياً فاستخلافه لا يجوز إجماعاً. (فتح، عيني)
And he appoints a substitute. [The one who is comprehending (the prayer) for istikhlaf is more deserving than the one who is late or preceded. (Tahawi)] i.e., the imam pulls someone suitable from the followers to his place, even if he appoints a woman, the prayer of the followers would be invalidated, even if they are women. He himself retreats bending forward, placing his hand on his nose, pretending that he has a nosebleed so that suspicions are cut off. He does not appoint by speech but by gesture. If he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid, contrary to Malik. He gives precedence from the row next to him. He may appoint as long as he has not passed the rows in the desert, and in the mosque as long as he has not left it. If he does not appoint until he has passed everything, the prayer of the people becomes invalid, and regarding the prayer of the imam there are two narrations. Riz al-Haqaiq 1/70. Then, when he appoints a substitute, the substitute should stand in his place before he leaves the mosque, and intend to be an imam. This is if he has not recited the amount sufficient for the prayer to be valid. If he has recited, he should bow, and istikhlaf is not permissible by consensus. Similarly, if he forgets the Quran and becomes illiterate, his istikhlaf is not permissible by consensus. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings on istikhlaf – appointing a substitute imam. The text explains that the imam should physically bring a suitable person forward, not appoint by speaking but by gesture. He should pretend to have a nosebleed to avoid suspicion. The substitute should be from the nearest row. If the imam appoints a woman, even for a female congregation, the prayer is invalid. The imam may appoint as long as he has not passed beyond the rows (in an open area) or left the mosque. If he delays and passes beyond, the congregation's prayer is void; there are two narrations about his own prayer. Then the protocol for the substitute: he must stand in place before the imam leaves the mosque and intend to be imam. The text then discusses a specific case: if the imam is unable to recite due to fatigue or shyness (hissar), Abu Hanifa permits istikhlaf, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, provided he has not yet recited enough to make the prayer valid. If he has recited enough, he should bow, and istikhlaf is unanimously not allowed. Similarly, if he forgets the Quran, istikhlaf is not allowed by consensus.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaf): The imam's action of appointing a substitute to lead the prayer when he cannot continue due to hadath or other reason.
الحصر (al-hasr): Inability to recite due to fatigue, shyness, or similar, preventing the imam from continuing the recitation.

The imam must appoint a substitute by gesture, feigning a nosebleed, and the substitute must be from the nearest row; istikhlaf is not allowed if enough recitation has occurred.

Mutayammim Seeing Water After Tashahhud
Commentary expanding the ruling on mutayammim seeing water after tashahhud to include the follower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mutayammim sees water after sitting for tashahhud and identify whether the follower's prayer is also invalidated.

Core Idea
A mutayammim's prayer becomes invalid upon seeing water after tashahhud; the follower's prayer is also invalid.

This short passage from a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a key detail within the 'Twelve Issues' (al-ithna 'ashariyyah) concerning tayammum. The base ruling is that when a mutayammim sees water after sitting for the tashahhud, his prayer becomes invalid. However, the commentator expands this to clarify that if a person with valid wudu was praying behind that mutayammim as a follower, his prayer also becomes invalid, even though his own purification was valid at the time. This expansion highlights the legal connection between the imam and the follower in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The base text (matn) states that if a mutayammim sees water after sitting for tashahhud, his prayer becomes invalid. This is the first of the 'Twelve Issues'.
The ruling is batil (void), not just fasid.
2
Note the restriction in the matn
The matn restricts the ruling to the mutayammim himself. It does not mention the follower.
The commentator finds this insufficient.
3
Understand the commentator's critique
The commentator argues that if a person with wudu was praying behind the mutayammim, his prayer also becomes invalid when the imam sees water. The imam's prayer is invalid because he lost his excuse (tayammum no longer valid), and the follower's prayer is tied to the imam's.
The commentator suggests the author should have said 'or the follower sees water' to cover both.
4
Apply the expanded ruling
Consider a follower with wudu behind a mutayammim imam. After tashahhud, the imam sees water. Both prayers become invalid. The imam's because his tayammum is broken, the follower's because his prayer depends on the imam's validity in this context.
The follower's own wudu remains intact, but his prayer is invalid due to the connection.
5
Recognize the underlying principle
The principle is that in Hanafi fiqh, the follower's prayer is legally connected to the imam's prayer. If the imam's prayer becomes invalid for a reason that also affects the follower (like loss of tayammum), the follower's prayer is also invalidated.
This is subject to specific conditions; not all imam invalidation triggers follower invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن رأى هذه المسألة مع المسائل الآتية إلى أو زال عذر المعذور " ملقبة بالاثنا عشرية، وهذه أولى منها، أي رؤية المتيمم الماء بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد وتقييده بالمتيمم لبطلان الصلاة عند رؤية الماء لا يفيد؛ لأنه لو كان متوضئاً يصلي خلف متيمم فرأى المتيمم الماء بطلت صلاته، وصلاة الإمام تامة؛ لعدم قدرته، ولو قال: "وبطلت إن رأى متيمم أو المقتدي به "ماء لشمل الكل. [رمز الحقائق: ۷۰/۱]
He saw [this issue along with the following issues until 'or the excuse of the excused one is removed' is called the 'Twelve Issues', and this is the first of them, i.e., the mutayammim seeing water after he has sat for the measure of tashahhud. Restricting it to the mutayammim for the invalidation of prayer upon seeing water is not beneficial, because if a person with wudu was praying behind a mutayammim and the mutayammim sees water, his prayer is also invalidated, and the prayer of the imam is complete because he is incapable. If he said: 'And it is invalidated if the mutayammim or the one following him sees water', it would include all. [Riz al-Haqaiq 1/70]
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific case known as the first of the 'Twelve Issues' (al-ithna 'ashariyyah): when a mutayammim sees water after he has sat for the measure of tashahhud. The ruling is that his prayer becomes invalid. The commentator notes that restricting the ruling to the mutayammim is insufficient because if a person who had wudu was praying behind a mutayammim as a follower, and the mutayammim imam sees water, the follower's prayer is also invalidated. The imam's prayer remains valid because he is excused (he could not find water). The commentator suggests the author should have said 'it is invalidated if the mutayammim or the one following him sees water' to cover all cases.

Key Terms
المتيمم (al-mutayammim): One who performs tayammum instead of wudu due to unavailability of water.
الاثنا عشرية (al-ithna 'ashariyyah): A set of twelve specific legal issues related to tayammum and similar, of which this is the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No prayer is invalidated

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a mutayammim sees water after sitting for tashahhud, both his prayer and the prayer of anyone following him become invalid.

The Twelve Invalidating Events in Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Listing and commentary on twelve events that invalidate prayer according to Abu Hanifa, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the twelve events that invalidate prayer according to Abu Hanifa, explain the underlying principle of al-khuruj min al-salah, and evaluate why the mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Exiting prayer is fard for Abu Hanifa, so any interruption before that invalidates; the Sahibayn disagree, and fatwa follows them.

This lesson unpacks a classic passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that lists twelve specific events occurring after tashahhud but before salam that, according to Abu Hanifa, invalidate the prayer. Understanding these events requires grasping the key principle that Abu Hanifa considers exiting prayer (al-khuruj min al-salah) a fard obligation. The Sahibayn dissent, and it is their view that is ultimately relied upon in practice (mufta bihi). We will examine each event, the principle behind the dispute, and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the text's statement: 'بناء على أن الخروج من الصلاة بفعل المصلي فرض عند أبي حنيفة'. Understand that Abu Hanifa's ruling on all twelve events hinges on this principle. According to him, the worshipper must actively exit the prayer by performing the salam; any event before that is like an interruption during the prayer itself.
The Sahibayn hold that exiting is not fard; the prayer is complete after tashahhud, so these events are like those after salam.
2
List the Twelve Events
Go through the matn and note each event: 1) finding water sufficient for wudu, 2) expiry of masah period, 3) removing khuffs with slight action, 4) an illiterate person learning a surah, 5) finding a garment to cover awrah, 6) ability to perform ruku and sujud (for someone praying while sitting or by gesture), 7) remembering a missed prayer (for a person of order), 8) appointing an illiterate deputy imam, 9) sunrise during Fajr, 10) entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah, 11) splint falling due to healing, 12) cessation of excuse for a mustahada.
The text provides detailed conditions for each, e.g., the water must be sufficient for wudu and the person able to use it.
3
Analyze the Dispute
For each event, note that Abu Hanifa rules the prayer becomes fasid (invalid), while the Sahibayn say it remains valid (sahih). The text states: 'وبطلان الصلاة في هذه المسائل كلها قول أبي حنيفة، وعندهما تمت'. The root cause is the difference regarding whether exiting is fard.
The text also mentions exceptions where the invalidated prayer becomes nafl (in three cases: remembering missed prayer, sunrise in Fajr, exit of Zuhr time in Jumu'ah).
4
Determine the Practical Outcome (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The source concludes: 'وبقولهما يفتى' (fatwa is given according to them). Thus, in practice, none of these events invalidate the prayer. The mufti should apply the Sahibayn's view. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
The later Hanafi masters (e.g., al-Haskafi, Ibn Abidin) consistently follow the Sahibayn in these cases.

Source Text

Book of Prayer, Chapter of Hadath in Prayer. Water: sufficient for his ablution and he is able to use it; or the period of his wiping (masah) expires; or he removes his khuffs with a small action; or an illiterate person learns a surah; or he finds a garment to cover his awrah; or he is able to perform the pillars (rukuk and sujud); or he remembers a missed prayer; or he appoints an illiterate person as deputy; or the sun rises during Fajr; or the time of Asr enters during Jumu'ah; or his splint falls off due to healing; or the excuse of the excused one (mustahada) ceases. [Then detailed commentary on each case.] The invalidation of prayer in all these cases is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Sahibayn) the prayer is complete. The principle is that exiting the prayer by one's own action is fard according to him, contrary to them, and fatwa is given according to their saying. The excused one: a mustahada who performs wudu with flowing blood, begins Zuhr, sits for the tashahhud, then the blood stops and continues until sunset—she must repeat Zuhr according to him, just as if it stopped during the prayers. And the prayer is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa in these cases, while according to them it remains valid, based on the fact that exiting the prayer by the worshiper's action is fard according to Abu Hanifa, so these occurrences interrupt after tashahhud before salam like interrupting during prayer; if they interrupt during prayer, they invalidate it, so here too. According to them, exiting is not fard, so these occurrences after tashahhud are like occurrences after salam; if they occur after salam, they do not invalidate, so here too. Then, if the prayer is invalidated in these cases, it does not turn into nafl except in three cases: remembering a missed prayer, sunrise, or the exit of Zuhr time in Jumu'ah. Al-Hawi added: 'if he is able to perform the pillars,' and the case of a wudu-performing person following a mutayammim is added, and it appears that the sun's declination on Eid and entering of disliked times in qada are similar, and also the case of finding water to remove impurity from the garment he prayed in.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the chapter on invalidating events during prayer. It begins by listing twelve specific events according to Abu Hanifa that render a prayer invalid if they occur after tashahhud but before salam. The text then provides a detailed commentary on each event, often citing opinions from Fath al-Qadir, al-Zayla'i, and others. The key principle underlying the dispute is that Abu Hanifa considers exiting the prayer (al-khuruj min al-salah) as a fard (obligatory act), so any event that interrupts the final sitting before salam is like an interruption during the prayer itself. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that exiting is not fard, so such events do not invalidate. The fatwa is given according to their saying. The passage also notes that in most of these cases the invalidated prayer does not become nafl, except in three situations: remembering a missed prayer (if one is a person of order), sunrise during Fajr, and the exit of Zuhr time during Jumu'ah. Additional cases are added from al-Hawi and Fath. The commentary explains each event's conditions and exceptions, such as the mustahada case and the requirement that the splint falls off due to healing. This lesson is an expansion probe into the matn of Kanz, clarifying the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A state of ritual impurity (minor or major) that invalidates prayer if it occurs during the prayer.
مسح على الخفين (masah ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks as a substitute for washing feet in wudu; its validity is limited to a set period (24 hours for resident, 3 days for traveler).
استخلاف (istikhlaf): Appointing a substitute imam when the original imam cannot continue due to hadath or other reason.
الخروج من الصلاة (al-khuruj min al-salah): Exiting the prayer by performing the final salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the underlying principle that causes Abu Hanifa to rule that the twelve events invalidate prayer after tashahhud?
A) The events are considered major sins.
B) Exiting the prayer by one's own action is a fard according to Abu Hanifa.
C) The events break wudu automatically.
D) The Sahibayn agreed with him.

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is that the twelve events listed do not invalidate prayer after tashahhud, following the Sahibayn, because exiting prayer is not considered fard.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on the Deputy Imam (Khalifa) and the Masbuq
Explaining the rules for a masbuq acting as deputy imam and its validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a masbuq to act as deputy imam and apply the Hanafi rulings when the original imam's prayer becomes invalid.

Core Idea
A masbuq can validly lead as deputy, but must yield to a mudrik for salam and his prayer invalidates if the imam's fails before he finishes.

In congregational prayer, if the original imam becomes unable to continue, a deputy (khalifa) may be appointed. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the specific case where the deputy is a masbuq—someone who missed part of the prayer. It establishes the validity of such an appointment but introduces important conditions and caveats. The scholars also debate the consequences if the original imam's prayer is later invalidated. Understanding these rulings ensures that the congregation's prayer remains sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
The text rules that appointing a masbuq as deputy (khalifa) is valid (sahih). Note this as the baseline.
The validity is established from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Examine the preferred procedure
The masbuq deputy should complete the imam's prayer up to the point of salam, then step back and advance a mudrik (one who caught the full prayer) to lead the salam. Then the masbuq stands to make up his missed rak'ahs.
The hadith about preferring the more deserving (man qallada insanan 'amalan) supports this.
3
Analyze the dispute on invalidation when the original imam's prayer becomes invalid
Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on whether the masbuq deputy's (and the congregation's) prayer becomes invalid if the original imam's prayer is invalidated (e.g., by hadath). The text presents both views and gives the most correct (al-ashah) as: if the deputy finished his own prayer before the invalidation, it remains valid; otherwise it invalidates.
The congregation's prayer is not invalidated according to the majority.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference matters for when a masbuq deputy must repeat his prayer. According to the mufta bihi, his prayer is only invalid if he hasn't finished his own part.
Similar reasoning applies to other invalidating events like laughter at the end of prayer.

Source Text

(مسكين، فتح) استخلاف المسبوق أي الذي لم يدرك أول صلاة الإمام، والأولى للإمام أن يقدم مدر كا وينبغي لهذا المسبوق أن لا يتقدم، فلو تقدم يبتدأ من حيث انتهى إليه الإمام، فإذا انتهى إلى موضع السلام تأخر وقدم مدركاً للسلام بالناس، ثم يقوم هو فيقضي ما بقي عليه، فإن توضأ الإمام الأول وصلى في بيته ما بقي عليه بعد فراغ الإمام الثاني تمت صلاته وقبل فراغه ،تفسد، وإنما قلنا بأولوية تقديم المدرك؛ لأنه أقدر على إتمام صلاة الإمام؛ ولقوله عليها: "من قلد إنسانا عملاً وفي رعيته من هو أولى منه، فقد خان الله ورسوله وجماعة المؤمنين"، ومن أحكام المسبوق أنه إذا كان مسبوقاً بركعة أو ركعتين يقضيهما بالفاتحة والسورة عندهما، وعند محمد بالفاتحة فقط؛ لأنه عندهما يقضي أول صلاته، وعند محمد آخرها، وإن لم يعلم المسبوق كمية صلاة الإمام ولا القوم بأن كان الكل مسبوقين مثله أتم ركعة وقعد ثم قام وأتم صلاة نفسه، ولا يتابعه القوم بل يصبرون إلى فراغه فيصلون ما عليهم وحداناً، ويقعد هذا الخليفة على كل ركعة احتياطاً. (مسكين، فتح) بالمنافي: كالضحك والكلام والخروج من المسجد. رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱] صلاته أي صلاة المسبوق؛ لأن المفسد وجد في خلال صلاته رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱۸] دون القوم: وقال أبو يوسف: تفسد صلاة القوم أيضاً، الأول إن فرغ لا تفسد صلاته، وإن لم يفرغ تفسد، وهو الأصح؛ لأنه لما استخلف صار مقتدياً به فتفسد صلاته بفساد صلاته، ولهذا لو صلى ما بقي من صلاته في منزله قبل فراغ الخليفة تفسد صلاته؛ لأن انفراده قبل فراغ الإمام لا يجوز. [رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱] والإمام لدى اختتامه وقالا : لا تفسد ؛ لأن العارض لم يؤثر في صلاة الإمام مع أنه صدر منه، فلأن لا يؤثر في فساد صلاة المسبوق و لم يصدر منه أولى، ولأبي حنيفة أنه مفسد للجزء الذي يلاقيه من صلاة الإمام، فيفسد في المقتدي مثله، إلا أن الإمام لا يحتاج إلى البناء لانتهاء الأركان، ففساد ذلك الجزء لا يضره، والمسبوق يحتاج إلى البناء،
And the appointment of a masbuq (one who missed part of prayer) as deputy is valid. If he completes the imam's prayer, he advances a mudrik (one who caught the prayer) to lead the salam for the people. And it is invalidated by something contrary (munafi) for the masbuq deputy, whether mudrik or not. The imam who was overtaken by hadath, his prayer is invalid with the congregation, but not the prayer of the congregation. Similarly, it is invalidated by the laughter of his imam at its conclusion, not by his exiting the mosque. The prayer of the masbuq is not invalidated. [Then repeats the earlier principle about the twelve cases and exceptions.] The appointment of the masbuq: he is one who did not catch the beginning of the imam's prayer. It is preferable for the imam to advance a mudrik, and it is not appropriate for this masbuq to step forward. If he does step forward, he begins from where the imam left off. When he reaches the point of salam, he steps back and advances a mudrik to give salam to the people, then he stands to make up what he missed. If the first imam performs wudu and prays at home what he missed after the second imam finishes, his prayer is complete; before the second imam finishes, it is invalidated. We say the preference for advancing a mudrik is because he is more capable of completing the imam's prayer, and due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever appoints a person to a position while among his subjects there is someone more deserving has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the believers.' Among the rulings of the masbuq: if he missed one or two rak'ahs, he makes them up with al-Fatiha and a surah according to them (Sahibayn), and according to Muhammad with al-Fatiha alone; because according to them he begins his own prayer first, according to Muhammad he ends with them. If the masbuq does not know the amount of prayer the imam or the congregation prayed, and they are all masbuq like him, he completes one rak'ah, sits, then stands and completes his own prayer. The congregation does not follow him but waits until he finishes, then they pray individually what they owe. This deputy sits at every rak'ah as a precaution. (Miskin, Fath). By munafi: such as laughter, speech, and leaving the mosque. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq] His prayer, i.e. the masbuq's prayer. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq] Not the congregation: Abu Yusuf said: the congregation's prayer is also invalidated. The first opinion: if he finished, his prayer is not invalidated; if he has not finished, it is invalidated. And this is the most correct, because when he deputized, he became a follower, so his prayer is invalidated by the invalidation of the imam's prayer. Therefore, if he prays what he missed in his home before the deputy finishes, his prayer is invalidated, because his separation before the imam finishes is not permissible. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq] And the imam at its conclusion, and they (Sahibayn) said: it does not invalidate, because the occurrence did not affect the imam's prayer even though it originated from him, so it is even more likely not to affect the masbuq's prayer since it did not originate from him. According to Abu Hanifa, it invalidates the part of the imam's prayer that it occurs in, so it invalidates for the follower as well, except that the imam does not need to rebuild because the pillars are finished, so that part's invalidation does not harm him, but the masbuq needs to rebuild.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the appointment of a masbuq (one who missed part of the congregation prayer) as substitute imam (khalifa). It begins by stating that such an appointment is valid. The primary ruling is that the masbuq deputy should, after completing the imam's prayer up to the point of salam, step back and advance a mudrik (one who caught the full prayer) to lead the salam for the congregation. Then the masbuq rises to complete his missed rak'ahs. The text then discusses various scenarios and disputes: if the original imam's prayer becomes invalid (e.g., due to hadath), the deputy's prayer also becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa, but not the congregation's prayer. Abu Yusuf differs, saying the congregation's prayer also invalidates. The relied-upon ruling (الأصح) is that if the deputy has not yet finished his own prayer, it invalidates. Several conditions are mentioned: the masbuq should not step forward to lead unless no mudrik is available; if he does, he should yield at salam. There is also an intra-Hanafi dispute about how a masbuq makes up missed rak'ahs: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, he recites al-Fatiha and a surah; according to Muhammad alone, only al-Fatiha—this is based on whether he considers his missed rak'ahs as the beginning or end of his prayer. The passage also contains a hadith about preferring the most qualified person for leadership. The commentary concludes with the rule that if the imam laughs during prayer at the end, it invalidates the imam's prayer but according to Abu Hanifa also invalidates the masbuq's prayer, while the Sahibayn say it does not because the imam's prayer is already complete except for exiting, which is not fard. This lesson is an expansion probe into the matn's rulings on istikhlaf.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joins the congregation late and misses one or more rak'ahs of the imam's prayer.
الخليفة (al-khalifa): The person appointed as substitute imam when the original imam is unable to continue.
المدرك (al-mudrik): A person who caught the entire prayer with the imam from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if the original imam's prayer becomes invalid (e.g., due to hadath) while a masbuq is acting as deputy?
A) The masbuq's prayer becomes invalid only if he has not yet finished his own prayer.
B) Both the masbuq's and congregation's prayers become invalid.
C) Only the imam's prayer becomes invalid; others remain valid.
D) The masbuq must start his prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
A masbuq can validly serve as deputy imam, but he must follow strict procedures to avoid invalidation of his own prayer, especially regarding the timing of the original imam's invalidation.

The Effect of the Imam's Hadath After Conclusion on the Masbuq's Prayer
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi debate about the masbuq's prayer after the Imam's hadath at conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether the masbuq's prayer is invalidated by the Imam's hadath after tashahhud, and explain the legal basis for each.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: masbuq builds on Imam, so invalid foundation collapses prayer. Sahibayn: Imam's hadath does not affect masbuq since not from him.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to the masbuq's prayer if the Imam's prayer becomes invalid due to hadath after the conclusion (ikhtitam) of the Imam's prayer? The difference arises from whether exiting prayer is considered fard. Understanding this helps clarify the masbuq's relationship with the Imam's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
The Imam completes tashahhud but before taslim, his prayer becomes invalid due to hadath. What is the ruling for the masbuq?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds the masbuq's prayer is invalid because the Imam's invalidity transfers to the follower who builds upon it.
The principle: building on the invalid is invalid.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold the masbuq's prayer remains valid because the hadath did not originate from him and exiting prayer is not fard.
They analogize to hadath after taslim.
4
Analyze the dalil for each side
Abu Hanifa uses the hadith 'building on the invalid is invalid' and the principle that impediments before taslim are like during prayer. Sahibayn counter that the Imam's prayer was unaffected in its completed pillars.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, the masbuq must start his prayer anew; according to Sahibayn, he may continue and complete his missed rak'ahs.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice is the Sahibayn's view.
