(مسكين، فتح) بالمنافي: كالضحك والكلام والخروج من المسجد. رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱] صلاته أي صلاة المسبوق؛ لأن المفسد وجد في خلال صلاته رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱۸] دون القوم: وقال أبو يوسف: تفسد صلاة القوم أيضاً، الأول إن فرغ لا تفسد صلاته، وإن لم يفرغ تفسد، وهو الأصح؛ لأنه لما استخلف صار مقتدياً به فتفسد صلاته بفساد صلاته، ولهذا لو صلى ما بقي من صلاته في منزله قبل فراغ الخليفة تفسد صلاته؛ لأن انفراده قبل فراغ الإمام لا يجوز. [رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱] والإمام لدى اختتامه وقالا : لا تفسد ؛ لأن العارض لم يؤثر في صلاة الإمام مع أنه صدر منه، فلأن لا يؤثر في فساد صلاة المسبوق و لم يصدر منه أولى، ولأبي حنيفة أنه مفسد للجزء الذي يلاقيه من صلاة الإمام، فيفسد في المقتدي مثله، إلا أن الإمام لا يحتاج إلى البناء لانتهاء الأركان، ففساد ذلك الجزء لا يضره، والمسبوق يحتاج إلى البناء، ففساد ذلك الجزء يمنعه من بناء ما بقي عليه؛ لأن البناء على الفاسد فاسد، فلزمه الاستقبال. رمز الحقائق: ٧٢/١] وقيد بالاختتام؛ لأن الحدث العمد لو حصل قبل القعود بطلت صلاة الكل اتفاقاً، واعلم أن المسبوق منفرد فيما يقضي إلا في أربعة مواضع: الأول: لا يقتدي والثاني: لا يقتدى به والثالث: يلزمه السجود بسهو إمامه وإن لم يحضره في سهوه والرابع يأتي بتكبيرات التشريق. (عيني، فتح) وكلامه: بعد ما قعد في آخر الصلاة إجماعاً؛ لأن الكلام والخروج من المسجد قاطع لا مفسد. رمز الحقائق: ۷۲/۱] وبني على صلاته، وعند الشافعي يستقبل. (ع)] أي ما لم يرفع رأسه منهما مريداً للأداء، أما إذا رفع رأسه مريداً بأداء ركن فلا يبني بل تفسد، ولو لم يرد الأداء فروايتان. رمز الحقائق: ۷۲/۱] وأعادهما [ أي الركوع والسجود اللذين أحدث فيهما وجوباً؛ لأن الانتقال من ركن إلى ركن بالطهارة شرط ولم يوجد، ولو لم يعدهما تفسد صلاته. (ع)] لعدم الاعتداد بما فعل أولاً، أما على قول محمد؛ فلأن إتمام الركن بالانتقال و لم يوجد، وأما على قول أبي يوسف وإن تم إلا أن القومة والجلسة فرض عنده، ولا تحقق لهما بغير الطهارة حتى لو لم يعدهما فسدت. (فتح) ذكر أن عليه سجدة صلبية فانحط غير أن يرفع رأسه. راكعاً أو ساجداً: قيد به؛ من ركوعه أو سجوده من . لأنه لو تذكرها في القعدة فسجدها أعاد القعدة، وأطلق السجدة، فعم الصلاتية والتلاوية، وقيد بالسجدة؛ لأنه لو تذكر في الركوع أنه لم يقرأ السورة فعاد إليها أعاد الركوع، والتلاوية كالصلاتية في رفع القعود بخلاف السهوية، فإنها ترفع التشهد فقط. (فتح) : لم يعدهما : [ أي الركوع والسجود الذي كان فيه والأفضل أن يعيدهما . (ط) (ع)] لأن الترتيب في أفعال الصلاة - أي في ما شرع مكرراً - ليس بشرط بخلاف المتحد، فإن مراعاة الترتيب فيما شرع متحدا وهو القعدة شرط، لا يقال: ما ذكره المصنف هنا من عدم الإعادة مخالف لما ذكره في الوافي حيث نص على الإعادة، فقد تناقض قولاه؛ لأنا نقول ما ذكره في الكنز من عدم الإعادة بالنظر لعدم الوجوب وما ذكره في الوافي بالنظر لما هو الأفضل، وكان ينبغي وجوب الإعادة لترك واجب الترتيب، وأجاب المصنف في الكافي بأن وجوب الترتيب سقط بعذر النسيان ونظر فيه في البحر بأن الذي يسقط بالنسيان ترتيب الفوائت، وأما ترك واجب الصلاة الذي منه مراعاة الترتيب فيما شرع مكرراً فموجب بسجود السهو فيسجد للسهو ولو مع الإعادة، والإعادة أفضل لتقع الأفعال مرتبة بالقدر الممكن، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يلزمه إعادة الركوع. (فتح) للاستخلاف من الإمام لعدم المزاحم، فإذا توضأ الإمام دخل معه في صلاته لتحول الإمامة إليه.(ع) بلا نية: فلو استخلف غير الصالح كالصبي والمرأة بطلت صلاة الإمام إجماعاً، وإلا بطلت صلاة المقتدي فقط؛ لأن الإمامة لم تتحول إليه لعدم صلاحيته، فبقي بلا ،إمام، وهذا إذا خرج الإمام من المسجد، وإذا لم يخرج فهو على إمامته .
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Occurrence of Impurity in Prayer. It is valid for the masbuq to appoint a substitute. If he completes the prayer of the Imam, he forwards one who is perceptive (mudrik) to give the salutation to them. It (the prayer of the masbuq who becomes substitute) is invalidated by that which is contrary (al-munafi) – i.e., the prayer of the masbuq, not the prayer of the people – just as it is invalidated by the loud laughter of his Imam at the conclusion. Not by his exit from the mosque. Twelve [cases]? = the zuhr with him, like if he breaks during the prayers and the prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa in these issues, and according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is complete; based on the fact that exiting the prayer by the action of the one praying is obligatory (fard) according to Abu Hanifa, so the occurrence of these impediments after tashahhud before taslim is like their occurrence during the prayer, and if they occur during it they invalidate it, so here likewise. According to them both, exiting the prayer is not obligatory, so the occurrence of these impediments in this state is like their occurrence after taslim, and if they occur after it they do not invalidate the prayer, so here likewise. Then, if the prayer becomes invalid in these cases, it does not turn into supererogatory (nafl) except in three cases: remembering a missed prayer, or the sun rises, or the time of zuhr exits in Friday prayer. Al-Hawi added: 'When he is able to perform the pillars, and added the issue of the one performing wudu who follows a mutayammim, and it appears that the setting of the sun in Eid and the entering of disliked times in making up are likewise, and similarly what if he finds enough water to remove the impurity of the garment in which he prayed.' (Miskin, Fath) 'The substitution of the masbuq' i.e., who did not attend the first part of the Imam's prayer. It is better for the Imam to forward a mudrik, and this masbuq should not go forward. If he does go forward, he begins from where the Imam had reached. When he reaches the point of greeting, he withdraws and forwards a mudrik to give the greeting to the people, then he stands and completes what remains. If the first Imam performs wudu and prays in his house what remained after the second Imam's completion, his prayer is complete; if before his completion, it is invalid. We said the preference of forwarding the mudrik because he is more capable of completing the Imam's prayer, and due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever appoints a man to a task while among his subjects there is one more worthy than him, has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the believers.' Among the rulings of the masbuq: if he missed one or two rak'ahs, he completes them with al-Fatihah and a surah according to them both, and according to Muhammad with al-Fatihah only; because according to them both he completes the first part of his prayer, and according to Muhammad the last. If the masbuq does not know the amount of the Imam's prayer or the people's, if all are masbuqs like him, he completes one rak'ah and sits, then stands and completes his own prayer. The people do not follow him but wait until he finishes and then pray what is upon them individually. This khalifah sits at every rak'ah as a precaution. (Miskin, Fath) 'By al-munafi' like laughter, speech, and exiting the mosque. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 71/1] 'his prayer' i.e., the prayer of the masbuq; because the invalidating factor occurred during his prayer. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 71/18] 'not the prayer of the people' – And Abu Yusuf said: The prayer of the people is also invalid. The first view: if he finished, his prayer is not invalid; if he did not finish, it is invalid, and this is the soundest; because when he appointed a successor, he became a follower of him, so his prayer becomes invalid by the invalidity of his prayer. For this, if he prays what remained of his prayer in his house before the khalifah finishes, his prayer is invalid; because his separation before the Imam's finish is not allowed. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 71/1] 'And the Imam at his conclusion' – And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not invalid; because the occurrence did not affect the Imam's prayer even though it came from him, so it is even more fitting that it not affect the invalidity of the masbuq's prayer when it did not come from him. For Abu Hanifa: It invalidates the part that meets it from the Imam's prayer, so it invalidates in the follower likewise, except that the Imam has no need to build (restart) due to completion of the pillars, so the invalidity of that part does not harm him. The masbuq needs to build, so the invalidity of that part prevents him from building what remains; because building upon an invalid foundation is invalid, so he must start anew. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 72/1] 'Restricted to conclusion' because if intentional hadath occurs before the sitting, the prayer of all is invalid by agreement. Know that the masbuq is alone in what he completes except in four matters: First: he does not follow; Second: he is not followed; Third: he must perform prostration for the forgetfulness of his Imam even if he was not present during his forgetfulness; Fourth: he says the takbirs of tashriq. ('Ayni, Fath) 'And his speech' – after he sits at the end of the prayer by consensus; because speech and exiting the mosque are disruptors (qati'), not invalidators (mufsid). [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 72/1] 'And he builds upon his prayer' – according to al-Shafi'i he starts anew. ('Ayni) i.e., as long as he has not raised his head from them intending performance. If he raised his head intending to perform a pillar, he does not build but rather it is invalid. If he did not intend performance, there are two narrations. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 72/1] 'And he repeats them' - i.e., the bowing and prostration in which he had hadath, wajiban (obligatorily); because the transition from pillar to pillar with purity is a condition and it was not met. If he does not repeat them, his prayer is invalid. ('Ayni) Because what was done first is not considered. According to Muhammad: because completion of the pillar is by transition and it did not occur. According to Abu Yusuf: even though it was completed, the standing and sitting are fard according to him, and they cannot be realized without purity, so if he does not repeat them, it becomes invalid. (Fath) Mentioned that he had a spinal prostration upon him, so he descended without raising his head from his bowing or prostration? 'While bowing or prostrating' – restricted to that; because if he remembers it while sitting and prostrates, he repeats the sitting. He used the absolute word 'sajdah', so it includes both prayer and tilawah sajdahs. He restricted it to sajdah because if he remembers while bowing that he did not recite the surah and returns to it, he repeats the bowing. 'The tilawah sajdah is like the prayer sajdah in lifting the sitting, unlike the forgetfulness sajdah, for it only lifts the tashahhud.' (Fath) 'He does not repeat them' - i.e., the bowing and prostration he was in, and it is better to repeat them. (Tatarkhani, 'Ayni) Because order in the actions of prayer – i.e., in what is legislated repeatedly – is not a condition, unlike the singular (al-mutahid); for observing order in what is legislated as a singular (i.e., the sitting) is a condition. It cannot be said: what the author mentioned here of non-repetition contradicts what he mentioned in al-Wafi where he mandated repetition, so his statements conflict; because we say: what he mentioned in al-Kanz of non-repetition is from the perspective of lack of obligation, and what he mentioned in al-Wafi is from the perspective of what is better. It would be appropriate for repetition to be wajib due to leaving a wajib of order. The author answered in al-Kafi that the obligation of order is dropped due to forgetfulness. Al-Bahr considered it: that which is dropped by forgetfulness is the order of missed prayers; while leaving a wajib of prayer, which includes observing order in what is legislated repeatedly, requires prostration for forgetfulness. So he prostrates for forgetfulness even with repetition, and repetition is better so that the actions occur in order to the extent possible. From Abu Yusuf: he is obligated to repeat the bowing. (Fath) 'For the substitution from the Imam due to lack of a competitor, so if the Imam performs wudu, he enters into his prayer because the imamah transfers to him. ('Ayni) 'Without intention' – If he appoints an unsuitable person like a boy or a woman, the Imam's prayer is invalid by consensus, otherwise only the prayer of the follower is invalid; because the imamah did not transfer to him due to his unsuitability, so he remained without an imam. This is if the Imam leaves the mosque; if he does not leave, he remains on his imamah.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a foundational Hanafi text, covers the chapter on occurrence of impurity (hadath) during prayer, focusing on the masbuq (one who joined late) being appointed as substitute (khalifah) for the Imam whose prayer becomes invalid. The passage is a combination of the base matn and its commentary (sharh), indicated by references like '(Miskin, Fath)' and '(Ayni, Fath)'. It opens with the ruling that it is valid for the masbuq to substitute for the Imam. The masbuq should forward a mudrik (one who caught the entire prayer) to give the salutation to the congregation. The substitute's prayer is invalidated by actions contrary to prayer (al-munafi) like laughter, speech, or leaving the mosque, but this invalidation applies only to the masbuq's own prayer, not the congregation's. A major ruling is that if the Imam's prayer becomes invalid due to hadath after he has completed his prayer (i.e., after tashahhud before taslim), the masbuq's prayer is also invalidated according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that the masbuq's prayer remains valid. The commentary explains the legal basis: Abu Hanifa considers the act of exiting prayer (al-khuruj min al-salah) to be obligatory (fard), so impediments before taslim are like during prayer; the Sahibayn consider it not fard, so impediments are like after taslim. The text then lists three exceptions where an invalidated prayer does not become nafl, which are nuanced scenarios. Further, it details the procedure for a masbuq being substituted: he should not step forward unless necessary, and if he does, he begins from where the Imam left off, then defers to a mudrik for the final salutation. An important hadith is cited about appointing the most worthy person. The passage also discusses disputes among the Hanafi imams: regarding the number of rak'ahs completed by the masbuq, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say he recites Fatihah and a surah, while Muhammad says only Fatihah. In a situation where the masbuq does not know how many rak'ahs the Imam or congregation completed, he prays one rak'ah and sits, then completes alone. The text then addresses the ruling on hadath occurring during ruku' or sujud: the person performs wudu, builds on his prayer, and must repeat the ruku' and sujud. It also covers the case of recalling a missed sajdah while bowing or prostrating, with a distinction between prayer sajdah, tilawah sajdah, and forgetfulness sajdah. Finally, it discusses the appointment of a specific person for substitution without intention (niyyah), noting that if an unsuitable person like a boy or woman is appointed, the Imam's prayer is invalid by consensus, but if the Imam does not leave the mosque, his imamah remains.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who did not attend the first part of the Imam's prayer, i.e., who missed one or more rak'ahs and completes them after the Imam's taslim.
الاختتام (al-ikhtitam): The conclusion of prayer, specifically after the final sitting (tashahhud) but before taslim, or after completing the pillars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what happens to a masbuq's prayer if the Imam has a hadath after tashahhud?
A) The masbuq's prayer is invalid.
B) The masbuq's prayer is valid.
C) The masbuq must repeat only the missed rak'ahs.
D) The congregation's prayer is all invalid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the masbuq's prayer is not automatically invalidated by the Imam's hadath after the conclusion; the Sahibayn's view (valid) is the mufta bihi.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
Rulings on Substitution (Istikhlaf) by the Masbuq
This passage explains the rulings on substitution (istikhlaf) by the masbuq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the procedure and conditions for a masbuq to act as substitute for the Imam, and identify the preferred order and consequences of invalid substitution.

Core Idea
The masbuq may substitute, but the ideal is a mudrik; the masbuq who leads must hand over the taslim to a mudrik.

This lesson covers the rules of istikhlaf when the masbuq is appointed as substitute. It discusses the preferred order, the actions of the substitute, and the effect on his prayer. Understanding these rules ensures proper conduct in congregational prayer when the Imam is incapacitated.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
It is valid (sahih) for the masbuq to appoint a substitute and lead the rest of the prayer.
2
Identify the preferred candidate
The Imam should prefer a mudrik (one who caught the entire prayer) as substitute, because he is more capable of completing the Imam's prayer. The masbuq should not step forward if a mudrik is present.
A hadith warns against appointing someone less worthy.
3
Describe the procedure if masbuq steps forward
The masbuq begins from where the Imam left off. When he reaches the point of taslim, he steps back and lets a mudrik give the salutation. Then he stands to complete his own missed rak'ahs.
4
Explain the effect on the original Imam's prayer
If the original Imam performs wudu and prays what remains at home, his prayer is valid only if he finishes after the substitute's completion; otherwise it is invalid.
This is because the Imam's imamah has transferred.
5
Note conditions for a valid substitution
The substitute must be a suitable person (e.g., sane male adult). If an unsuitable person like a boy or woman is appointed, the prayer of the Imam becomes invalid by consensus, and the followers' prayer may also be invalid.
If the Imam remains in the mosque, his imamah continues.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة باب الحدث في الصلاة وصح استخلاف المسبوق، فلو أتم صلاة الإمام قدّم مدركاً يسلم بهم، وتفسد بالمنافي المسبوق الخليفة س م أي مدرك كان الإمام الذي سبقه الحدث مع القوم صلاته دون القوم كما تفسد بقهقهة إمامه لدى اختتامه، لا بخروجه من صلاة المسبوق لا تفسد صلاة المسبوق المسجد اثنا عشر، = الظهر عنده، كما لو انقطع في خلال الصلوات وبطلت الصلاة عند أبي حنيفة في هذه المسائل، وهي وعندهما تمت؛ بناء على أن الخروج من الصلاة بفعل المصلي فرض عند أبي حنيفة فاعتراض هذه العوارض بعد التشهد قبل التسليم كاعتراضها في أثناء الصلاة، ولو اعترضت في أثنائها تفسدها فكذا هنا، وعندهما الخروج من الصلاة ليس بفرض، فاعتراضها في هذه الحالة كاعتراضها بعد التسليم، ولو اعترضت بعده لا تفسد الصلاة فكذا هنا، ثم إذا بطلت الصلاة في هذه المسائل لا تنقلب نفلا إلا في ثلاث مسائل: تذكر فائتة، أو طلعت الشمس، أو خرج وقت الظهر في الجمعة، زاد "الحاوي": "إذا قدر على الأركان، ويزاد مسألة المتوضئ المؤتم بمتيمم، والظاهر أن زوال الشمس في العيد ودخول الأوقات المكروهة في القضاء كذلك، وكذا يزاد ما لو وجد من الماء ما يزيل به نجاسة الثوب الذي صلى فيه. (مسكين، فتح) استخلاف المسبوق أي الذي لم يدرك أول صلاة الإمام، والأولى للإمام أن يقدم مدر كا وينبغي لهذا المسبوق أن لا يتقدم، فلو تقدم يبتدأ من حيث انتهى إليه الإمام، فإذا انتهى إلى موضع السلام تأخر وقدم مدركاً للسلام بالناس، ثم يقوم هو فيقضي ما بقي عليه، فإن توضأ الإمام الأول وصلى في بيته ما بقي عليه بعد فراغ الإمام الثاني تمت صلاته وقبل فراغه ،تفسد، وإنما قلنا بأولوية تقديم المدرك؛ لأنه أقدر على إتمام صلاة الإمام؛ ولقوله عليها: "من قلد إنسانا عملاً وفي رعيته من هو أولى منه، فقد خان الله ورسوله وجماعة المؤمنين"، ومن أحكام المسبوق أنه إذا كان مسبوقاً بركعة أو ركعتين يقضيهما بالفاتحة والسورة عندهما، وعند محمد بالفاتحة فقط؛ لأنه عندهما يقضي أول صلاته، وعند محمد آخرها، وإن لم يعلم المسبوق كمية صلاة الإمام ولا القوم بأن كان الكل مسبوقين مثله أتم ركعة وقعد ثم قام وأتم صلاة نفسه، ولا يتابعه القوم بل يصبرون إلى فراغه فيصلون ما عليهم وحداناً، ويقعد هذا الخليفة على كل ركعة احتياطاً. (مسكين، فتح) بالمنافي: كالضحك والكلام والخروج من المسجد. رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱] صلاته أي صلاة المسبوق؛ لأن المفسد وجد في خلال صلاته رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱۸] دون القوم: وقال أبو يوسف: تفسد صلاة القوم أيضاً، الأول إن فرغ لا تفسد صلاته، وإن لم يفرغ تفسد، وهو الأصح؛ لأنه لما استخلف صار مقتدياً به فتفسد صلاته بفساد صلاته، ولهذا لو صلى ما بقي من صلاته في منزله قبل فراغ الخليفة تفسد صلاته؛ لأن انفراده قبل فراغ الإمام لا يجوز. [رمز الحقائق: ۷۱/۱] والإمام لدى اختتامه وقالا : لا تفسد ؛ لأن العارض لم يؤثر في صلاة الإمام مع أنه صدر منه، فلأن لا يؤثر في فساد صلاة المسبوق و لم يصدر منه أولى، ولأبي حنيفة أنه مفسد للجزء الذي يلاقيه من صلاة الإمام، فيفسد في المقتدي مثله، إلا أن الإمام لا يحتاج إلى البناء لانتهاء الأركان، ففساد ذلك الجزء لا يضره، والمسبوق يحتاج إلى البناء، ففساد ذلك الجزء يمنعه من بناء ما بقي عليه؛ لأن البناء على الفاسد فاسد، فلزمه الاستقبال. رمز الحقائق: ٧٢/١] وقيد بالاختتام؛ لأن الحدث العمد لو حصل قبل القعود بطلت صلاة الكل اتفاقاً، واعلم أن المسبوق منفرد فيما يقضي إلا في أربعة مواضع: الأول: لا يقتدي والثاني: لا يقتدى به والثالث: يلزمه السجود بسهو إمامه وإن لم يحضره في سهوه والرابع يأتي بتكبيرات التشريق. (عيني، فتح) وكلامه: بعد ما قعد في آخر الصلاة إجماعاً؛ لأن الكلام والخروج من المسجد قاطع لا مفسد. رمز الحقائق: ۷۲/۱] وبني على صلاته، وعند الشافعي يستقبل. (ع)] أي ما لم يرفع رأسه منهما مريداً للأداء، أما إذا رفع رأسه مريداً بأداء ركن فلا يبني بل تفسد، ولو لم يرد الأداء فروايتان. رمز الحقائق: ۷۲/۱] وأعادهما [ أي الركوع والسجود اللذين أحدث فيهما وجوباً؛ لأن الانتقال من ركن إلى ركن بالطهارة شرط ولم يوجد، ولو لم يعدهما تفسد صلاته. (ع)] لعدم الاعتداد بما فعل أولاً، أما على قول محمد؛ فلأن إتمام الركن بالانتقال و لم يوجد، وأما على قول أبي يوسف وإن تم إلا أن القومة والجلسة فرض عنده، ولا تحقق لهما بغير الطهارة حتى لو لم يعدهما فسدت. (فتح) ذكر أن عليه سجدة صلبية فانحط غير أن يرفع رأسه. راكعاً أو ساجداً: قيد به؛ من ركوعه أو سجوده من . لأنه لو تذكرها في القعدة فسجدها أعاد القعدة، وأطلق السجدة، فعم الصلاتية والتلاوية، وقيد بالسجدة؛ لأنه لو تذكر في الركوع أنه لم يقرأ السورة فعاد إليها أعاد الركوع، والتلاوية كالصلاتية في رفع القعود بخلاف السهوية، فإنها ترفع التشهد فقط. (فتح) : لم يعدهما : [ أي الركوع والسجود الذي كان فيه والأفضل أن يعيدهما . (ط) (ع)] لأن الترتيب في أفعال الصلاة - أي في ما شرع مكرراً - ليس بشرط بخلاف المتحد، فإن مراعاة الترتيب فيما شرع متحدا وهو القعدة شرط، لا يقال: ما ذكره المصنف هنا من عدم الإعادة مخالف لما ذكره في الوافي حيث نص على الإعادة، فقد تناقض قولاه؛ لأنا نقول ما ذكره في الكنز من عدم الإعادة بالنظر لعدم الوجوب وما ذكره في الوافي بالنظر لما هو الأفضل، وكان ينبغي وجوب الإعادة لترك واجب الترتيب، وأجاب المصنف في الكافي بأن وجوب الترتيب سقط بعذر النسيان ونظر فيه في البحر بأن الذي يسقط بالنسيان ترتيب الفوائت، وأما ترك واجب الصلاة الذي منه مراعاة الترتيب فيما شرع مكرراً فموجب بسجود السهو فيسجد للسهو ولو مع الإعادة، والإعادة أفضل لتقع الأفعال مرتبة بالقدر الممكن، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يلزمه إعادة الركوع. (فتح) للاستخلاف من الإمام لعدم المزاحم، فإذا توضأ الإمام دخل معه في صلاته لتحول الإمامة إليه.(ع) بلا نية: فلو استخلف غير الصالح كالصبي والمرأة بطلت صلاة الإمام إجماعاً، وإلا بطلت صلاة المقتدي فقط؛ لأن الإمامة لم تتحول إليه لعدم صلاحيته، فبقي بلا ،إمام، وهذا إذا خرج الإمام من المسجد، وإذا لم يخرج فهو على إمامته .
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Occurrence of Impurity in Prayer. It is valid for the masbuq to appoint a substitute. If he completes the prayer of the Imam, he forwards one who is perceptive (mudrik) to give the salutation to them. It (the prayer of the masbuq who becomes substitute) is invalidated by that which is contrary (al-munafi) – i.e., the prayer of the masbuq, not the prayer of the people – just as it is invalidated by the loud laughter of his Imam at the conclusion. Not by his exit from the mosque. Twelve [cases]? = the zuhr with him, like if he breaks during the prayers and the prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa in these issues, and according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is complete; based on the fact that exiting the prayer by the action of the one praying is obligatory (fard) according to Abu Hanifa, so the occurrence of these impediments after tashahhud before taslim is like their occurrence during the prayer, and if they occur during it they invalidate it, so here likewise. According to them both, exiting the prayer is not obligatory, so the occurrence of these impediments in this state is like their occurrence after taslim, and if they occur after it they do not invalidate the prayer, so here likewise. Then, if the prayer becomes invalid in these cases, it does not turn into supererogatory (nafl) except in three cases: remembering a missed prayer, or the sun rises, or the time of zuhr exits in Friday prayer. Al-Hawi added: 'When he is able to perform the pillars, and added the issue of the one performing wudu who follows a mutayammim, and it appears that the setting of the sun in Eid and the entering of disliked times in making up are likewise, and similarly what if he finds enough water to remove the impurity of the garment in which he prayed.' (Miskin, Fath) 'The substitution of the masbuq' i.e., who did not attend the first part of the Imam's prayer. It is better for the Imam to forward a mudrik, and this masbuq should not go forward. If he does go forward, he begins from where the Imam had reached. When he reaches the point of greeting, he withdraws and forwards a mudrik to give the greeting to the people, then he stands and completes what remains. If the first Imam performs wudu and prays in his house what remained after the second Imam's completion, his prayer is complete; if before his completion, it is invalid. We said the preference of forwarding the mudrik because he is more capable of completing the Imam's prayer, and due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever appoints a man to a task while among his subjects there is one more worthy than him, has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the believers.' Among the rulings of the masbuq: if he missed one or two rak'ahs, he completes them with al-Fatihah and a surah according to them both, and according to Muhammad with al-Fatihah only; because according to them both he completes the first part of his prayer, and according to Muhammad the last. If the masbuq does not know the amount of the Imam's prayer or the people's, if all are masbuqs like him, he completes one rak'ah and sits, then stands and completes his own prayer. The people do not follow him but wait until he finishes and then pray what is upon them individually. This khalifah sits at every rak'ah as a precaution. (Miskin, Fath) 'By al-munafi' like laughter, speech, and exiting the mosque. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 71/1] 'his prayer' i.e., the prayer of the masbuq; because the invalidating factor occurred during his prayer. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 71/18] 'not the prayer of the people' – And Abu Yusuf said: The prayer of the people is also invalid. The first view: if he finished, his prayer is not invalid; if he did not finish, it is invalid, and this is the soundest; because when he appointed a successor, he became a follower of him, so his prayer becomes invalid by the invalidity of his prayer. For this, if he prays what remained of his prayer in his house before the khalifah finishes, his prayer is invalid; because his separation before the Imam's finish is not allowed. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 71/1] 'And the Imam at his conclusion' – And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not invalid; because the occurrence did not affect the Imam's prayer even though it came from him, so it is even more fitting that it not affect the invalidity of the masbuq's prayer when it did not come from him. For Abu Hanifa: It invalidates the part that meets it from the Imam's prayer, so it invalidates in the follower likewise, except that the Imam has no need to build (restart) due to completion of the pillars, so the invalidity of that part does not harm him. The masbuq needs to build, so the invalidity of that part prevents him from building what remains; because building upon an invalid foundation is invalid, so he must start anew. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 72/1] 'Restricted to conclusion' because if intentional hadath occurs before the sitting, the prayer of all is invalid by agreement. Know that the masbuq is alone in what he completes except in four matters: First: he does not follow; Second: he is not followed; Third: he must perform prostration for the forgetfulness of his Imam even if he was not present during his forgetfulness; Fourth: he says the takbirs of tashriq. ('Ayni, Fath) 'And his speech' – after he sits at the end of the prayer by consensus; because speech and exiting the mosque are disruptors (qati'), not invalidators (mufsid). [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 72/1] 'And he builds upon his prayer' – according to al-Shafi'i he starts anew. ('Ayni) i.e., as long as he has not raised his head from them intending performance. If he raised his head intending to perform a pillar, he does not build but rather it is invalid. If he did not intend performance, there are two narrations. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 72/1] 'And he repeats them' - i.e., the bowing and prostration in which he had hadath, wajiban (obligatorily); because the transition from pillar to pillar with purity is a condition and it was not met. If he does not repeat them, his prayer is invalid. ('Ayni) Because what was done first is not considered. According to Muhammad: because completion of the pillar is by transition and it did not occur. According to Abu Yusuf: even though it was completed, the standing and sitting are fard according to him, and they cannot be realized without purity, so if he does not repeat them, it becomes invalid. (Fath) Mentioned that he had a spinal prostration upon him, so he descended without raising his head from his bowing or prostration? 'While bowing or prostrating' – restricted to that; because if he remembers it while sitting and prostrates, he repeats the sitting. He used the absolute word 'sajdah', so it includes both prayer and tilawah sajdahs. He restricted it to sajdah because if he remembers while bowing that he did not recite the surah and returns to it, he repeats the bowing. 'The tilawah sajdah is like the prayer sajdah in lifting the sitting, unlike the forgetfulness sajdah, for it only lifts the tashahhud.' (Fath) 'He does not repeat them' - i.e., the bowing and prostration he was in, and it is better to repeat them. (Tatarkhani, 'Ayni) Because order in the actions of prayer – i.e., in what is legislated repeatedly – is not a condition, unlike the singular (al-mutahid); for observing order in what is legislated as a singular (i.e., the sitting) is a condition. It cannot be said: what the author mentioned here of non-repetition contradicts what he mentioned in al-Wafi where he mandated repetition, so his statements conflict; because we say: what he mentioned in al-Kanz of non-repetition is from the perspective of lack of obligation, and what he mentioned in al-Wafi is from the perspective of what is better. It would be appropriate for repetition to be wajib due to leaving a wajib of order. The author answered in al-Kafi that the obligation of order is dropped due to forgetfulness. Al-Bahr considered it: that which is dropped by forgetfulness is the order of missed prayers; while leaving a wajib of prayer, which includes observing order in what is legislated repeatedly, requires prostration for forgetfulness. So he prostrates for forgetfulness even with repetition, and repetition is better so that the actions occur in order to the extent possible. From Abu Yusuf: he is obligated to repeat the bowing. (Fath) 'For the substitution from the Imam due to lack of a competitor, so if the Imam performs wudu, he enters into his prayer because the imamah transfers to him. ('Ayni) 'Without intention' – If he appoints an unsuitable person like a boy or a woman, the Imam's prayer is invalid by consensus, otherwise only the prayer of the follower is invalid; because the imamah did not transfer to him due to his unsuitability, so he remained without an imam. This is if the Imam leaves the mosque; if he does not leave, he remains on his imamah.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a foundational Hanafi text, covers the chapter on occurrence of impurity (hadath) during prayer, focusing on the masbuq (one who joined late) being appointed as substitute (khalifah) for the Imam whose prayer becomes invalid. The passage is a combination of the base matn and its commentary (sharh), indicated by references like '(Miskin, Fath)' and '(Ayni, Fath)'. It opens with the ruling that it is valid for the masbuq to substitute for the Imam. The masbuq should forward a mudrik (one who caught the entire prayer) to give the salutation to the congregation. The substitute's prayer is invalidated by actions contrary to prayer (al-munafi) like laughter, speech, or leaving the mosque, but this invalidation applies only to the masbuq's own prayer, not the congregation's. A major ruling is that if the Imam's prayer becomes invalid due to hadath after he has completed his prayer (i.e., after tashahhud before taslim), the masbuq's prayer is also invalidated according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that the masbuq's prayer remains valid. The commentary explains the legal basis: Abu Hanifa considers the act of exiting prayer (al-khuruj min al-salah) to be obligatory (fard), so impediments before taslim are like during prayer; the Sahibayn consider it not fard, so impediments are like after taslim. The text then lists three exceptions where an invalidated prayer does not become nafl, which are nuanced scenarios. Further, it details the procedure for a masbuq being substituted: he should not step forward unless necessary, and if he does, he begins from where the Imam left off, then defers to a mudrik for the final salutation. An important hadith is cited about appointing the most worthy person. The passage also discusses disputes among the Hanafi imams: regarding the number of rak'ahs completed by the masbuq, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say he recites Fatihah and a surah, while Muhammad says only Fatihah. In a situation where the masbuq does not know how many rak'ahs the Imam or congregation completed, he prays one rak'ah and sits, then completes alone. The text then addresses the ruling on hadath occurring during ruku' or sujud: the person performs wudu, builds on his prayer, and must repeat the ruku' and sujud. It also covers the case of recalling a missed sajdah while bowing or prostrating, with a distinction between prayer sajdah, tilawah sajdah, and forgetfulness sajdah. Finally, it discusses the appointment of a specific person for substitution without intention (niyyah), noting that if an unsuitable person like a boy or woman is appointed, the Imam's prayer is invalid by consensus, but if the Imam does not leave the mosque, his imamah remains.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who did not attend the first part of the Imam's prayer, i.e., who missed one or more rak'ahs and completes them after the Imam's taslim.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaf): The act of the Imam appointing a substitute (khalifah) to complete the prayer when the Imam becomes unable due to hadath.
المدرك (al-mudrik): One who caught the entire prayer with the Imam from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred candidate for substitution when the Imam becomes incapacitated?
A) A masbuq
B) A mudrik
C) Any follower
D) The youngest follower

Key Takeaway
The masbuq can validly substitute, but the ideal is a mudrik; the masbuq must hand over the taslim to a mudrik.

Hadath During Ruku' or Sujud: Building and Repetition
Ruling on hadath during ruku' or sujud with proof and qualification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for hadath during ruku' or sujud after the final sitting, explain the reasoning behind repeating those positions, and identify the qualification regarding the final sitting.

Core Idea
After the final sitting, hadath allows building but invalid positions must be repeated.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in the prayer: what happens if a person experiences a hadath (ritual impurity event) while in ruku' or sujud? The Hanafi school has a detailed ruling that balances continuity and validity. The key distinction is whether the hadath occurs before or after the final sitting (qadah akhirah). Let us explore the ruling, its underlying reasoning, and the critical qualification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is having a hadath during ruku' or sujud. The ruling states: he performs wudu, builds on the prayer (continues from where he stopped), and repeats the ruku' and sujud.
The ruling applies specifically after the final sitting.
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
Why must he repeat those positions? The text says building on an invalid part is invalid. Since the positions performed in impurity are invalid, they must be redone; otherwise, the prayer is built on an invalid foundation.
This is a rational proof, not from a transmitted text.
3
Note the qualification
This ruling is restricted to after the final sitting (ikhtitam). If hadath occurs before the final sitting, the entire prayer is invalid by consensus, regardless of intention.
The text explicitly states this exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده توضأ وبنى وأعادهما. ففساد ذلك الجزء يمنعه من بناء ما بقي عليه؛ لأن البناء على الفاسد فاسد، فلزمه الاستقبال. وقيد بالاختتام؛ لأن الحدث العمد لو حصل قبل القعود بطلت صلاة الكل اتفاقاً.
And if he has an event during his ruku' or his sujud, he performs ablution, builds (upon his prayer), and repeats them. The invalidity of that part prevents him from building upon what remains; because building upon that which is invalid is invalid, so restarting is necessary. And it is restricted by the completion (final sitting); because deliberate event if it occurs before the sitting invalidates the entire prayer by consensus.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is a ruling on what happens when a worshipper has a hadath (ritual impurity event) during ruku' or sujud. The ruling states that he must perform wudu, then build on his prayer (i.e., continue from where he stopped after becoming pure), and repeat the positions (ruku' and sujud) that were performed while impure. The commentator explains the reasoning: since the part performed in a state of impurity is invalid, building upon an invalid foundation is itself invalid, so he must restart the prayer if he does not repeat those parts. However, there is a qualification: this ruling applies specifically after the final sitting (tashahhud). If the hadath occurs before the final sitting, the entire prayer is invalid by consensus, regardless of whether it was deliberate or not.

Key Terms
البناء (al-binā'): Continuing the prayer from the point where the hadath occurred after performing wudu, rather than restarting.
الاختتام (al-ikhtitām): The final sitting (qadah akhirah) of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the Hanafi school allow building on the prayer after hadath during ruku' or sujud?
A) Only if the hadath is unintentional.
B) Only after the final sitting.
C) Only before the final sitting.
D) In all cases.

Key Takeaway
Hadath during ruku' or sujud after the final sitting requires wudu, building, and repeating those positions; before the final sitting, the prayer is void.

Remembering a Missed Sajdah During Ruku' or Sujud
Ruling on remembering a sajdah during ruku' or sujud and not repeating them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a missed sajdah is remembered during ruku' or sujud, distinguish between repeated and singular acts, and apply the principle that order is not a condition in repeated acts.

Core Idea
Order is not required in repeated acts of prayer like sujud.

Imagine you are in the middle of your prayer, and suddenly you recall that you missed a prostration earlier. What should you do? This lesson covers the Hanafi ruling for such a situation, explaining why you do not need to repeat the ruku' or sujud you were in and highlighting a key principle about order in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The person is in ruku' or sujud and remembers that he owes a sajdah (either a prayer sajdah or a tilawah sajdah).
The sajdah is a missed structural prostration (sajdah salbiyyah).
2
State the ruling
He should immediately prostrate for the missed sajdah without completing the ruku' or sujud he is in. After performing it, he does not need to repeat the ruku' or sujud, though it is better to repeat them.
The text says 'لم يعدهما' (he does not repeat them).
3
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The reason is that order (tartib) is a condition only for acts that occur singularly (like the final sitting). For acts that are repeated multiple times (like sujud), order is not a condition. Therefore, interrupting a repeated act to perform a missed one does not invalidate the sequence.
This principle is explicitly stated: 'الترتيب في ما شرع مكرراً ليس بشرط'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf disagreed: he held that the ruku' or sujud must be repeated because order is required even in repeated acts. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say it is not required.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Apply the distinction to other cases
The text contrasts this with remembering a missed surah recitation during ruku'. In that case, because recitation is a singular act, order is a condition: he must return to recite and then repeat the ruku'.
Also, if the missed sajdah is remembered during the sitting, the sitting must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ذكر راكعاً أو ساجداً سجدة فسجدها لم يعدهما. ذكر أن عليه سجدة صلبية فانحط غير أن يرفع رأسه. راكعاً أو ساجداً: قيد به؛ لأنه لو تذكرها في القعدة فسجدها أعاد القعدة، وأطلق السجدة، فعم الصلاتية والتلاوية، وقيد بالسجدة؛ لأنه لو تذكر في الركوع أنه لم يقرأ السورة فعاد إليها أعاد الركوع، والتلاوية كالصلاتية في رفع القعود بخلاف السهوية، فإنها ترفع التشهد فقط. لم يعدهما: أي الركوع والسجود الذي كان فيه والأفضل أن يعيدهما. لأن الترتيب في أفعال الصلاة - أي في ما شرع مكرراً - ليس بشرط بخلاف المتحد، فإن مراعاة الترتيب فيما شرع متحدا وهو القعدة شرط. وعن أبي يوسف أنه يلزمه إعادة الركوع.
And if he remembers, while in ruku' or sujud, a sajdah (obligatory prostration), and he prostrates for it, he does not repeat them (the positions he was in). It is mentioned that he has a structural sajdah (sajdah salbiyyah), so he descends without raising his head. 'In ruku' or in sujud': a restriction; because if he remembers it in the sitting and prostrates for it, he repeats the sitting. And he (the author) made 'sajdah' unrestricted, so it includes both prayer and recitation prostrations. And he restricted it to sajdah; because if he remembers in ruku' that he did not recite the surah, and he returns to it, he repeats the ruku'. And the recitation prostration is like the prayer prostration in raising the sitting, unlike the prostration of forgetfulness, for it only elevates the tashahhud. 'He does not repeat them': meaning the ruku' and sujud that he was in, though it is better to repeat them; because order in the acts of prayer - i.e., in what is prescribed repeatedly - is not a condition, unlike that which is singular. Observing order in what is prescribed singularly, which is the sitting, is a condition. And from Abu Yusuf that he must repeat the ruku'.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a person who, while in ruku' or sujud, remembers that he missed a sajdah (either a prayer sajdah or a recitation sajdah). He performs that missed sajdah immediately without first completing the ruku' or sujud. The ruling is that he does not need to repeat the ruku' or sujud after performing the sajdah. The commentator explains the reason: order (tartib) in acts that are repeated (like sujud, which occurs multiple times) is not a condition for validity, unlike order in acts that are singular (like the final sitting, which must be in sequence). However, it is preferable (afdal) to repeat the ruku' and sujud to maintain proper order. There is a difference of opinion: Abu Yusuf holds that he must repeat the ruku' because order is required even in repeated acts. The text also distinguishes between a forgotten prostration and a forgotten recitation of a surah: if he remembers missing a surah during ruku', he must return and recite, then repeat the ruku'.

Key Terms
السجدة الصلبية (al-sajdah al-salbiyyah): A prostration that is an integral part of the prayer (rukn), as opposed to a tilawah or sahw sajdah.
الترتيب في ما شرع مكرراً (al-tartīb fī mā shuri'a mukarraran): Order in acts that are repeated multiple times in the prayer, such as sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person remembers a missed sajdah while in ruku', what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He must finish the ruku', then do the sajdah, then repeat the ruku'.
B) He should immediately prostrate for the missed sajdah and not repeat the ruku'.
C) He should complete the ruku', then perform the sajdah without repeating.
D) He must restart the prayer.

Key Takeaway
When a missed sajdah is remembered during ruku' or sujud, one may perform it immediately without repeating the interrupted act, reflecting the principle that order is not a condition in repeated actions.

Automatic Substitute Imam: Ruling for a Single Follower
Ruling on a single follower being appointed as substitute imam without intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on automatic designation of a single follower as substitute imam, and identify the conditions that affect validity.

Core Idea
A single qualified follower automatically becomes the imam when the original imam cannot continue — no intention needed.

When the imam in congregational prayer becomes invalidated (e.g., by breaking wudu), there must be a substitute to continue the prayer. The Hanafi school has a detailed ruling: if there is only one follower, he becomes the imam automatically, regardless of whether he intended it or not. This lesson explores the conditions, exceptions, and the precise scenario where this applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with istikhlaaf (substitution) of a single follower when the imam's prayer is broken. State the key ruling: the follower is designated without intention.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Determine the conditions for valid transfer
List the conditions that enable automatic designation: only one follower, follower must be qualified (adult male capable of leading), and the imam must leave the mosque (otherwise he remains imam).
3
Distinguish between qualified and unqualified followers
Analyze the text: if the imam appoints an unqualified person (e.g., boy or woman), his prayer is invalid by consensus; otherwise (automatic with unqualified), only the follower's prayer is invalid.
This distinction hinges on whether the imam actively appointed.
4
Apply the scenario of imam leaving the mosque
Consider the imam's movement: if he leaves the mosque, the transfer occurs; if he stays, he remains imam. Use this to evaluate the prayer of both parties.
Also note similar rulings for hermaphrodite, illiterate, mute, and nafil behind fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعيّن المأموم الواحد للاستخلاف بلا نية. للاستخلاف من الإمام لعدم المزاحم، فإذا توضأ الإمام دخل معه في صلاته لتحول الإمامة إليه. بلا نية: فلو استخلف غير الصالح كالصبي والمرأة بطلت صلاة الإمام إجماعاً، وإلا بطلت صلاة المقتدي فقط؛ لأن الإمامة لم تتحول إليه لعدم صلاحيته، فبقي بلا إمام، وهذا إذا خرج الإمام من المسجد، وإذا لم يخرج فهو على إمامته. حتى لو توضأ في المسجد وعاد إلى مكانه، صح، وحكم الخنثى والأمي والأخرس والمنتفل خلف المفترض كحكم الصبي، وصورة المسألة أنه إن أحدث الإمام ولم يكن خلفه إلا رجل صار إماماً مطلقاً قدمه الإمام أولا، نوى أن يكون إمام نفسه أو لا، فإذا توضأ الإمام دخل معه في صلاته؛ لتحول الإمامة إليه.
And a single follower is designated for being made a substitute without intention. For the substitute from the imam due to absence of one who would oppose. So when the imam performs ablution, he enters with him (the substitute) into his prayer because the imamate has transferred to him. 'Without intention': so if he appoints someone not qualified, like a boy or a woman, the imam's prayer is invalid by consensus, otherwise only the follower's prayer is invalid; because the imamate did not transfer to him due to his lack of qualification, so he remains without an imam. This is when the imam has left the mosque; but if he has not left, he remains upon his imamate. Even if he performs ablution in the mosque and returns to his place, it is valid. And the ruling of the hermaphrodite, the illiterate, the mute, and the one praying a supererogatory prayer behind one praying an obligatory prayer is like the ruling of a boy. And the scenario of the issue: if the imam has an event and there is no one behind him except a man, he becomes an absolute imam, whether the imam had advanced him first or not, whether he intended to be an imam of himself or not. So when the imam performs ablution, he enters with him into his prayer because the imamate has transferred to him.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on when a single follower is automatically designated as a substitute (istikhlaaf) for the imam when the imam has a hadath. The key point is that the follower does not need to make an intention; he automatically becomes the imam. If the original imam then performs wudu and returns to the mosque, he may join the prayer behind the substitute imam, as the imamate has transferred. However, if the follower is not qualified (e.g., a boy or woman), the imam's prayer is invalid if he appointed them, but if he just left, only the follower's prayer is invalid. The passage also distinguishes between whether the imam leaves the mosque or not: if he stays in the mosque, he remains imam. Then it discusses similar rulings for a hermaphrodite, illiterate, mute, and one praying nafil behind a fard prayer, all being like a boy (i.e., not qualified to lead). Finally, it gives the scenario: if the imam has an event and only one man is behind him, that man becomes imam absolutely, regardless of previous appointment or intention.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaaf): The act of a person being appointed as a substitute imam when the original imam is unable to continue.
المزاحم (al-muzāhim): One who could compete or object; here meaning another qualified person who could lead.
تعيّن (ta'ayyun): Designation; the automatic assignment of a person to a role without choice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When an imam has a hadath and there is only one follower behind him, what happens according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The prayer is invalid and everyone must restart.
B) The follower becomes the imam automatically, even without intention.
C) The follower must make an intention to lead and then lead.
D) The imam must perform tayammum and continue.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a single qualified follower is automatically designated as substitute imam without needing intention; the imamate transfers to him as soon as the imam leaves the prayer area.

Salah — Prayer

Speech Invalidates Prayer: The Hanafi Position and Its Proofs
Ruling with proof: speech invalidates prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speech in prayer, identify its proof from Quran and Sunnah, and explain why the Shafi'i and Maliki objections are rejected.

Core Idea
All speech in prayer — deliberate, forgetful, or mistaken — invalidates the prayer, regardless of intention.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling that human speech nullifies the prayer. While one might think only deliberate talk breaks the prayer, the Hanafi school holds that even unintentional speech — whether from forgetfulness or error — invalidates it. We will explore the textual proofs from the Quran and hadith that support this position, and understand how the Hanafi school defends its view against the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Guided Path
1
Define the act of speech
Identify what constitutes speech in prayer according to the Hanafi school: uttering two letters or one meaningful letter intended as human speech. Note that sounds without composition, such as calling an animal, do not count as speech.
One letter that conveys meaning, like 'Q' as a command, suffices.
2
Identify the three states of speech
Distinguish between sahw (forgetful: one is aware of the forgetfulness), khata (mistaken: one is not aware without alert), and amdan (deliberate). Understand the subtle differences between these states as defined in the text.
The text also differentiates between sahw and nisyan (forgetfulness that requires new effort to remember).
3
State the Hanafi ruling
All three states — deliberate, forgetful, and mistaken — invalidate the prayer. Cite the evidence: the verse 'وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ' (al-Baqarah 238) which was revealed commanding silence, and the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam that the Companions used to speak until this verse forbade all speech.
The Hanafi ruling is that any speech, even if unintended, nullifies the prayer.
4
Analyze the opposing proofs
Examine the Shafi'i reliance on the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان وما استكرهوا عليه' (error, forgetfulness, and coercion are lifted from my ummah). Understand the Hanafi response: this hadith lifts sin, not the ruling of invalidity. Then consider the Maliki position that deliberate speech for rectification does not invalidate, based on the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn. The Hanafi response: that hadith is abrogated by the later Madani verse.
The text also notes that the hadith of 'رفع' is interpreted as lifting of sin, not the ruling.
5
Apply the ruling to a real scenario
If a person in prayer mistakenly speaks while intending to recite Quran, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. This applies to deliberate, forgetful, and mistaken speech equally.
This shows the strictness of the Hanafi position.

يفسد الصلاة التكلم، والدعاء بما يشبه كلامنا، والأنين، والتأوه، وارتفاع بكائه من وجع. ويفسدها وهو أن يقول: أوه إن حصل به حروف. باب ما يفسد إلخ الفساد يرجع إلى ذات الصلاة، والكراهة ترجع إلى وصفها. شروع في العوارض الاختيارية بعد الفراغ من السماوية، وقدمها؛ لأنها أتم في العارضية لعدم قدرة العبد على دفعها. يفسد الصلاة: أي كلاً كانت أو بعضاً؛ ليشمل سجود التلاوة والسهو، والمراد من التكلم هو النطق بحرفين أو حرف مفهم كـ'ق' و'ع' أمراً، ولو استعطف كلباً أو هرة أو ساق حماراً لا تفسد؛ لأنه صوت لا هجاء له، سواء كان التكلم ساهياً بأن قصد كلام الناس ساهياً أنه في الصلاة أو مخطئاً بأن قصد القراءة، فجرى على لسانه كلام الناس، أو عامداً بأن قصد المفسد عالماً أنه في الصلاة أو ناسياً، والفرق بين السهو والنسيان أن الصورة الحاصلة عند العقل إن كان يمكنه الملاحظة أي وقت شاء سمي ذهولاً وسهواً، أو لا إلا بعد كسب جديد سمي نسيانا، والفرق بين السهو والخطأ أن السهو ما يتنبه له صاحبه والخطأ ما لا يتنبه إلا بالتنبيه أو تنبيه بعد إتعاب. وقال الشافعي: لا تفسد في الخطأ والنسيان؛ لقوله عليه: 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان وما استكرهوا عليه'، ولنا: حديث زيد بن أرقم أنه قال: كنا نتكلم في الصلاة يكلم الرجل صاحبه وهو إلى جنبه في الصلاة حتى نزل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ﴾ أمرنا بالسكوت ونهينا عن الكلام، وقال علي: 'إن صلاتنا هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس'، والمراد بما رواه رفع الاثم وعن مالك العمد أيضاً لا يفسدها إذا كان لإصلاح صلاته؛ استدلالاً بحديث ذي اليدين والجواب عنه: أنه منسوخ بالآية التي بها حرم الكلام، وهي مدنية؛ لأنها من البقرة، وهي مدنية إجماعا. التكلم مطلقاً سواء كان ساهياً أو مخطئاً ناسيا أو عامداً. كلامنا كقوله: اللهم ألبسني ثوباً، اللهم فلانة، وعند الشافعي لا تفسد. والأنين وهو الصوت الحاصل عن قوله: آه. من وجع الوجع المرض، والمصيبة ما يصيب الإنسان من كل ما يؤذيه من موت ومرض ونحو ذلك، أي من مرض في بدنه أو مصيبة في نفسه أو ماله فصار كأنه يقول: 'أنا مصاب فعزوني' من التعزية، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه قال: إن كان يمكن الامتناع عنه يقطع صلاته، وإلا لا، وعن محمد: إن كان المرض خفيفاً يقطع، وإن كان ثقيلاً لا، وإن كان من ذكر جنّة أو نار فعن أبي يوسف أن 'آه' لا تفسد سواء كان من وجع أو من ذكر جنة أو نار، و 'أوه' تفسد فيهما، والأصل عنده أن الكلمة اشتملت على حرفين زائدين أو أحدهما لا تفسد نحو: 'أح' و 'تف' و 'أف'، وإن كانا أصليين تفسد، وحروف الزوائد جمعوها في قولهم: 'اليوم تنساه'.
Speech invalidates prayer, and supplication resembling our speech, and groaning, and sighing, and loud crying due to pain. And it invalidates that he says 'Oh' if it contains letters. The chapter 'what invalidates etc.' invalidity pertains to the essence of prayer, and dislike pertains to its description. It is a start on voluntary impediments after finishing from heavenly ones, and he gave them priority because they are more complete in being impediments due to the servant's inability to repel them. 'Invalidates the prayer' meaning whether it is complete or partial; to include the prostration of recitation and forgetfulness. And the meaning of speech is pronouncing two letters or one meaningful letter like 'q' and 'a' as a command, and if one calls a dog or cat or drives a donkey, it does not invalidate because it is a sound without composition, whether the speech is forgetful (sahyan) by intending people's speech forgetful that he is in prayer, or mistaken (mukhti'an) by intending recitation but people's speech came out, or deliberate ('amidan) by intending to invalidate knowing he is in prayer or forgetful. And the difference between sahw (forgetfulness) and nisyan (forgetfulness) is that the image present to the mind if one can observe it anytime called dhuhool and sahw, otherwise only after new acquisition called nisyan. And the difference between sahw and khata is that sahw is what one is attentive to, and khata is what one is not attentive to except by alerting or alerting after exertion. And al-Shafi'i said: It does not invalidate in error and forgetfulness due to his statement عليه: 'Lifted from my ummah error, forgetfulness, and what they are coerced upon.' And for us (the Hanafi proof): the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam that he said: We used to speak in prayer; a man would speak to his companion beside him in prayer until the verse was revealed: 'And stand before Allah in devout obedience'; we were ordered to be silent and forbidden from speech. And Ali said: 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of people's speech.' And the meaning of what he narrated is lifting of sin. And from Malik: deliberate speech also does not invalidate it if it is for rectification of his prayer, deducing from the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn. The answer to it: that it is abrogated by the verse that forbade speech, and it is Madani because it is from al-Baqarah, and it is Madani by consensus. Speech absolutely whether forgetful or mistaken or forgetful or deliberate. 'Our speech' like his saying: 'O Allah clothe me a garment', 'O Allah so-and-so'. And according to al-Shafi'i it does not invalidate. And al-anin (groaning) is the sound resulting from saying 'Ah'. From pain: pain is sickness, and calamity is what afflicts a person from everything that harms him like death, illness and the like. That is, from sickness in his body or calamity in his self or wealth, so it becomes as if he says: 'I am afflicted, so console me' from consoling. And from Abu Yusuf: he said: if it can be refrained from, it cuts his prayer, otherwise no. And from Muhammad: if the sickness is light, it cuts; if severe, no. And if it is from mentioning Jannah or Hellfire, then from Abu Yusuf that 'Ah' does not invalidate whether from pain or from mentioning Jannah or Fire, and 'Oh' invalidates in both. And the principle with him is that a word contains two extra letters or one of them does not invalidate like 'Ah' and 'Tf' and 'Af', but if both are original, it invalidates. The extra letters they collected in their saying: 'al-yawma tansāh'.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from the chapter 'What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it' deals with speech and similar sounds. The main ruling: any form of human speech, whether deliberate, forgetful, or mistaken, invalidates the prayer. This includes groaning (anin) and sighing (ta'uwah) if they consist of letters. However, sounds that are not articulate, like calling an animal, do not invalidate. The text then explains the Hanafi proof against the Shafi'i view that error and forgetfulness should not invalidate based on the hadith of lifting. The Hanafi proof uses the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam that the Companions used to speak until the verse 'and stand before Allah in devout obedience' was revealed, which forbade all speech. The hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn (the one who spoke to the Prophet during prayer) is answered as abrogated. The passage also covers the view of Malik that deliberate speech for correcting the prayer does not invalidate, but this is rejected. Then it discusses specific words: 'Ah' and 'Oh' (وه and أوه). According to Abu Yusuf, if the pain is severe and one cannot refrain, then it does not invalidate; but if possible to refrain, it does. Muhammad distinguishes between light and severe illness. For words like 'Ah' and 'Oh' from pain or mentioning Paradise/Fire, there are detailed rulings based on whether the word contains two letters that are original or extra. The phrase 'al-yawma tansāh' is a mnemonic for the extra letters (y, w, m, t, n, s, h, alif).

Key Terms
التكلم (al-takallum): Uttering two letters or one meaningful letter intended as human speech.
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness that one is aware of; a state of heedlessness where one can recall without difficulty.
الخطأ (al-khata): Error where one is not aware without being alerted; often unintentional speech that differs from intention.
النسيان (al-nisyān): Forgetfulness that requires new effort to remember; the information is not easily retrievable.
القانتين (al-qānitīn): Devoutly obedient, silent in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person in prayer mistakenly says 'Amen' loudly as a response to an imam's recitation outside the prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because it is human speech.
B) The prayer remains valid because it is a form of dhikr.
C) The prayer is invalid only if it was deliberate.
D) The prayer is still valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Any human speech in prayer — whether deliberate, forgetful, or mistaken — invalidates the prayer based on the absolute command of silence in the Quran and the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam.

Groaning, Sighing, and the Ruling on Expressions Like 'Ah' and 'Oh'
Detailed rulings on groaning and sighing with intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between groaning (anin) and sighing (ta'uwah) and apply the Hanafi intra-madhhab differences to determine when such sounds invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Groaning and sighing that contain letters can invalidate prayer, but the ruling depends on intent, ability to refrain, and whether the letters are original or extra.

This lesson delves into the detailed rulings on involuntary sounds like groaning (anin) and sighing (ta'uwah) during prayer. While such sounds may seem like natural expressions of pain or emotion, the Hanafi school analyzes them based on whether they constitute human speech. We will examine the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and understand the principle for distinguishing between words like 'Ah' and 'Oh' based on the nature of their letters.

Guided Path
1
Define anin and ta'uwah
Anin is the sound 'Ah' (آه) from pain. Ta'uwah is sighing (أوه). The text also mentions loud crying due to pain. Determine if these sounds consist of letters (huroof).
If the sound has no hija (composed letters), it may not invalidate.
2
Apply the general rule: speech invalidates if it contains letters
The text states that 'يفسدها وهو أن يقول: أوه إن حصل به حروف' (it invalidates if he says 'Oh' provided it contains letters). So the first condition is that the sound is composed of letters.
If the sound is just a groan without letters, it does not invalidate.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi differences
Abu Yusuf holds that if one can refrain from groaning, it invalidates; if not (e.g., severe pain), it does not. Muhammad distinguishes by severity: light illness invalidates, severe does not.
These are differences within the Hanafi school, not between schools.
4
Distinguish between 'Ah' and 'Oh' when mentioning Paradise or Fire
According to Abu Yusuf, 'Ah' (آه) does not invalidate whether from pain or from mentioning Paradise/Fire, but 'Oh' (أوه) invalidates in both cases. The principle: if the word contains two original letters, it invalidates; if one or both are extra letters (huruf al-zawaaid), it does not.
Extra letters are memorized by the phrase 'اليوم تنساه' (al-yawma tansāh).
5
Apply the principle to other expressions
Examples: 'Ah' (أح), 'Tf' (تف), 'Af' (أف) — these contain extra letters and do not invalidate. But 'Oh' (أوه) contains two original letters (أ and ه, with و? Actually the text says أوه has two original letters; the extra letters are identified by the mnemonic.)
This requires knowledge of Arabic morphology to identify original vs extra letters.

Speech invalidates prayer, and supplication resembling our speech, and groaning, and sighing, and loud crying due to pain. And it invalidates that he says 'Oh' if it contains letters. The chapter 'what invalidates etc.' invalidity pertains to the essence of prayer, and dislike pertains to its description. And the meaning of speech is pronouncing two letters or one meaningful letter like 'q' and 'a' as a command, and if one calls a dog or cat or drives a donkey, it does not invalidate because it is a sound without composition, whether the speech is forgetful (sahyan) by intending people's speech forgetful that he is in prayer, or mistaken (mukhti'an) by intending recitation but people's speech came out, or deliberate ('amidan) by intending to invalidate knowing he is in prayer or forgetful. And the difference between sahw (forgetfulness) and nisyan (forgetfulness) is that the image present to the mind if one can observe it anytime called dhuhool and sahw, otherwise only after new acquisition called nisyan. And the difference between sahw and khata is that sahw is what one is attentive to, and khata is what one is not attentive to except by alerting or alerting after exertion. And al-Shafi'i said: It does not invalidate in error and forgetfulness due to his statement عليه: 'Lifted from my ummah error, forgetfulness, and what they are coerced upon.' And for us (the Hanafi proof): the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam that he said: We used to speak in prayer; a man would speak to his companion beside him in prayer until the verse was revealed: 'And stand before Allah in devout obedience'; we were ordered to be silent and forbidden from speech. And Ali said: 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of people's speech.' And the meaning of what he narrated is lifting of sin. And from Malik: deliberate speech also does not invalidate it if it is for rectification of his prayer, deducing from the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn. The answer to it: that it is abrogated by the verse that forbade speech, and it is Madani because it is from al-Baqarah, and it is Madani by consensus. Speech absolutely whether forgetful or mistaken or forgetful or deliberate. 'Our speech' like his saying: 'O Allah clothe me a garment', 'O Allah so-and-so'. And according to al-Shafi'i it does not invalidate. And al-anin (groaning) is the sound resulting from saying 'Ah'. From pain: pain is sickness, and calamity is what afflicts a person from everything that harms him like death, illness and the like. That is, from sickness in his body or calamity in his self or wealth, so it becomes as if he says: 'I am afflicted, so console me' from consoling. And from Abu Yusuf: he said: if it can be refrained from, it cuts his prayer, otherwise no. And from Muhammad: if the sickness is light, it cuts; if severe, no. And if it is from mentioning Jannah or Hellfire, then from Abu Yusuf that 'Ah' does not invalidate whether from pain or from mentioning Jannah or Fire, and 'Oh' invalidates in both. And the principle with him is that a word contains two extra letters or one of them does not invalidate like 'Ah' and 'Tf' and 'Af', but if both are original, it invalidates. The extra letters they collected in their saying: 'al-yawma tansāh'.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from the chapter 'What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it' deals with speech and similar sounds. The main ruling: any form of human speech, whether deliberate, forgetful, or mistaken, invalidates the prayer. This includes groaning (anin) and sighing (ta'uwah) if they consist of letters. However, sounds that are not articulate, like calling an animal, do not invalidate. The text then explains the Hanafi proof against the Shafi'i view that error and forgetfulness should not invalidate based on the hadith of lifting. The Hanafi proof uses the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam that the Companions used to speak until the verse 'and stand before Allah in devout obedience' was revealed, which forbade all speech. The hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn (the one who spoke to the Prophet during prayer) is answered as abrogated. The passage also covers the view of Malik that deliberate speech for correcting the prayer does not invalidate, but this is rejected. Then it discusses specific words: 'Ah' and 'Oh' (وه and أوه). According to Abu Yusuf, if the pain is severe and one cannot refrain, then it does not invalidate; but if possible to refrain, it does. Muhammad distinguishes between light and severe illness. For words like 'Ah' and 'Oh' from pain or mentioning Paradise/Fire, there are detailed rulings based on whether the word contains two letters that are original or extra. The phrase 'al-yawma tansāh' is a mnemonic for the extra letters (y, w, m, t, n, s, h, alif).

Key Terms
الأنين (al-anīn): Groaning, the sound 'Ah' from pain.
التأوه (al-ta'uwah): Sighing, the sound 'Oh'.
حروف الزوائد (ḥurūf al-zawā'id): Extra letters that can be added to a root; they do not affect the core meaning.
اليوم تنساه (al-yawma tansāh): A mnemonic for the extra letters: alif, lām, yā, wāw, mīm, tā, nūn, sīn, hā.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, if a person in prayer says 'Oh' (أوه) due to remembering Hellfire, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because 'Oh' has two original letters.
B) The prayer remains valid because it is from religious emotion.
C) The prayer is invalid only if it was loud.
D) The prayer remains valid because it is like 'Ah'.

Key Takeaway
Groaning and sighing during prayer are not automatically invalidating; the ruling depends on the composition of letters (original vs. extra), the ability to refrain, and the severity of the cause.

Saying 'La ilaha illallah' as Response in Prayer
Ruling that answering with tawheed invalidates prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person in prayer responds to a question with the words of tawheed, and explain why it invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
A deliberate response in prayer, even with tawheed, is human speech and invalidates the prayer.

This lesson addresses a crucial boundary in salah: the difference between reciting dhikr as part of worship and uttering words as a response to external speech. Even the most sacred phrase, 'La ilaha illallah', can nullify the prayer if spoken with the intention to answer someone. Understanding this distinction preserves the sanctity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What did the person in prayer do? He was asked a question and he responded verbally.
2
Determine the intention
Did he intend to answer the question or to make dhikr? The text says 'yuridu jawabahu' (intending to answer).
Intention is key.
3
Apply the ruling
The prayer is invalidated (batil).
4
Understand the rationale
The response counts as kalam al-nas (human speech), which breaks the state of prayer.
Even though the words are dhikr, the intention turns them into speech.
5
Distinguish from permissible dhikr
If the same words are recited as dhikr without intention to answer, the prayer remains valid.
The same words, different ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بـ"لا إله إلا الله : بأن قيل بين يديه: أمع الله إله آخر؟ فقال: لا إله إلا الله، يريد جوابه.
By saying 'la ilaha illallah': meaning that it is said in front of him: 'Is there another god with Allah?' So he says 'la ilaha illallah', intending to answer it.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on what invalidates prayer. The text states that if a person praying is asked, 'Is there another god with Allah?' and he responds with 'La ilaha illallah' (there is no god but Allah) with the intention of answering the question, his prayer is invalidated. The reason is that this constitutes speech (kalam al-nas) which is not part of the prayer and deliberately breaks the connection with Allah. The key principle here is that any deliberate response to external speech, even if it contains the words of tawheed, is considered kalam al-adami (human speech) and nullifies the prayer.

Key Terms
لا إله إلا الله (la ilaha illallah): The phrase of tawheed, when spoken as a response to a question, becomes human speech and invalidates prayer.
جواب (jawab): Intending to answer someone's question, which makes the utterance count as speech rather than prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person praying is asked 'Is there another god with Allah?' and he replies 'La ilaha illallah' intending to answer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because it is considered speech.
B) The prayer remains valid because he said the truth.
C) The prayer is invalid only if he says it loudly.
D) The prayer is invalid only if he repeats it three times.

Key Takeaway
Responding to a question during prayer, even with the words of tawheed, invalidates the prayer because it is considered human speech.

Intentional Greeting Salam Invalidates Prayer
Ruling that returning or initiating salam invalidates prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on greeting salam in prayer and identify when it invalidates and when it does not.

Core Idea
Intentional greeting to a person during prayer invalidates it; forgetful or closing salam does not.

In prayer, speaking human words intentionally breaks the validity. The greeting salam (assalamu alaykum) is a common form of speech. This lesson clarifies the critical distinction between three types of salam: the closing salam of prayer, a forgetful salam, and an intentional greeting salam. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of salam
Distinguish between the closing salam (exit from prayer), a greeting salam directed at a person, and a forgetful salam. Only the greeting salam invalidates if intentional.
2
Apply the condition of intention
Check whether the salam was uttered with the intention of greeting someone present. If yes, the prayer is invalid. If forgetful or part of prayer, it does not invalidate.
Forgetful salam requires sajdah sahw to compensate.
3
Recognize gestures as exceptions
Responding with a hand gesture or head nod does not invalidate the prayer. Only spoken words count as speech.
4
Know the disliked recipients
Even outside prayer, it is makruh to initiate salam to certain persons (e.g., one reciting Quran, in hadath, etc.) — a separate ruling about adab.
This list is from al-Ghazzi's Fath and is outside the main prayer invalidation ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسلام: أي سلام التحية بأن يكون المخاطب حاضراً ويسلم عليه بقصد التحية، لا سلام الصلاة؛ لما صرحوا أنه لو سلم على رأس الركعتين في الرباعية ساهياً لا تفسد، وكذا لو سلم المسبوق مع الإمام، ويدل عليه ما في "النهر": السلام على إنسان مبطل مطلقا، وأما السلام وهو الخروج من الصلاة فمفسد إن كان عمداً، أي لا ناسياً، وفي إطلاق لفظ "السلام" إشارة إلى أنه مفسد ولو بلا لفظ "عليكم"، والمراد برد السلام باللسان، أما إذا رد بيده، أو قيل له: "أجيد هذا" فأوماً برأسه بـ"لا" أو "نعم" لا تفسد ويكره السلام على المصلي والقارئ والذاكر والمحدث والخطيب والسامع لهما ومكرر الفقه والجالس للقضاء والباحث في العلم والمؤذن والمدرس والأجنبية الفتاة واللاعب بالشطرنج ونحوه ومن يتمتع مع أهله والكافر ومكشوف العورة ومن هو يتغوط والأكل والأستاذ المغني ومطير الطير ونظمها الشيخ الغزي (فتح)
And the salam: meaning the greeting salam, that the addressee is present and he greets him with the intention of greeting, not the salam of prayer; because they explicitly stated that if he says salam after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer forgetfully, it does not invalidate, and likewise if a latecomer says salam with the imam. And it indicates that which is in 'al-Nahr': salam to a person invalidates absolutely. And as for the salam which is exiting from prayer, it invalidates if intentional, not if forgetful. And in the absolute use of the word 'salam', it is an indication that it invalidates even without the word 'alaykum'. And what is intended is responding with the tongue. As for if he responds with his hand, or if it is said to him: 'Good this?' and he nods his head with 'no' or 'yes', it does not invalidate. And it is disliked to greet the praying person, the Quran reciter, the one remembering Allah, the one in hadath, the khatib, the listener to both, the one repeating fiqh, the one sitting for judgment, the researcher in knowledge, the mu'adhin, the teacher, the unrelated young woman, the chess player and the like, the one enjoying with his family, the disbeliever, the one with exposed awrah, the one defecating, the eater, the singing teacher, and the bird trainer and its organizer, as per al-Ghazzi (Fath).
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two types of salam in prayer: 1) The closing salam of prayer (Salam al-khuruj) which is part of the prayer and, if intentional, invalidates the prayer (but not if forgetful). 2) A greeting salam directed at a person with the intention of greeting (tahiyya) – this invalidates the prayer absolutely if the addressee is present and the speaker intends greeting, even if he does not say 'alaykum'. The text also clarifies that responding to a greeting with a hand gesture or a head nod (saying 'no' or 'yes') does not invalidate. The latter part lists persons to whom it is disliked to give salam (even outside prayer), including those engaged in various acts of worship or study, chess players, etc. This ruling is based on the principle that deliberate speech (kalam) in prayer invalidates it, and salam is a form of speech.

Key Terms
السلام (al-salam): Greeting salam (التحية) said to someone present, which invalidates prayer if intentional.
تحية (tahiyyah): The greeting intended for the person, not as part of the prayer ritual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid because it is intentional speech.
B) The prayer is valid because salam is a good deed.
C) The prayer is invalid only if the person responds.
D) The prayer remains valid if done forgetfully.

Key Takeaway
Intentional greeting salam during prayer invalidates it; forgetful salam does not but requires sajdah sahw.
