Counting Tasbih with Hand in Prayer: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on counting with hand in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on counting tasbih with the hand in prayer and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Counting tasbih with the hand in prayer is makruh tanzih per the mufta bihi, but the Sahibayn permitted it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is it permissible to count Qur'anic verses or tasbih (glorifications) using one's hand during prayer? The school's founding imam, Abu Hanifa, held it as disliked, while his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, saw no harm. The passage weighs their arguments and clarifies the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
The act is counting verses (āyāt) or tasbīḥ (subḥānallāh etc.) using the hand (fingers) during prayer, whether fard or nafl.
This does not include counting with the tongue (invalidates prayer) or with the heart (no issue).
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: makruh tanzih (disliked) in fard prayer, with some saying the dislike extends to all prayers. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn): lā ba'sa (no harm) in any prayer.
The text mentions a view that there is consensus on dislike in fard, but the stronger opinion (adhar) is that the dispute covers both fard and nafl.
3
Understand the scope of the dispute
Some scholars restrict the difference to fard prayers only, others include nafl. The passage declares the most apparent (adhar) that the difference applies to all prayers.
This affects practical fatwa: if the mufta bihi is dislike in all prayers, counting with hand is discouraged even in supererogatory prayers.
4
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that counting with the hand in prayer is makruh tanzih in both fard and nafl. Outside prayer, it is permissible and even beneficial.
This is the view favoured by later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani.
5
Analyze the evidentiary basis
The Sahibayn's view is supported by a hadith where the Prophet saw a woman counting on date pits and did not forbid her, but guided to an easier method. This indicates permissibility. Abu Hanifa's view considers the act as a distraction reducing khushūʿ.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its indication (dalāla) is also zanni, so the matter is open to ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعد الآي والتسبيح، لا قتل الحية والعقرب، أي تكون الصورة فوق رأسه أي في السقف مقتضاه عدم الكراهة إذا كانت تحت رجليه أو في محل جلوسه؛ لأنها مهانة، ولكن يكره كراهة جعل الصورة في البيت لخبر، لا تدخل الملائكة بيتاً فيه كلب ولا صورة وأشدها الكراهة أن تكون أمام مصلي ثم فوق رأسه ثم بحذائه ثم خلفه [تبيين الحقائق: ٤١٤/١] بين يديه بأن تكون معلقة أو موضوعة صغيرة: [ بحيث لا تبدو للناظر إلا بالتأمل؛ لأن الكراهة باعتبار العبادة والصغيرة لا تعبد عادة. (ع)] لما روي أن خاتم أبي هريرة كان عليه ذبابتان وخاتم دانيال كان عليه أسد ولبوة وبينهما رجل يلحسانه والمراد بالصغيرة أن تكون بحال لو كانت على الأرض والناظر واقف لا يرى تفاصيل أعضائها. (فتح) أو مقطوعة الرأس لأنها لا تعبد بدون الرأس. [رمز الحقائق: ٧٦/١] لغير ذي روح كالشجرة والثمرة والكواكب ونحوها ؛ لأنها لا تعبد. (ط) وعد الآي: الآي جمع آية، أي آيات القرآن وقالا : لا بأس باليد ثم قيل: لا خلاف في التطوع أنه لا يكره والخلاف في الفرض، وقيل: كره في الفرض إجماعاً، والخلاف في النوافل، والأظهر أن الخلاف في الكل، ولا يكره العد خارج الصلاة في الصحيح؛ لأنه أسكن للقلب وأجلب للنشاط؛ ولما روي أنه عليها دخل على امرأة وبين يديها نوى أو تسبح به، فقال: حصي " أخبرك بما . هو أيسر عليك من هذا وأفضل"، فلم ينهها عن ذلك، وإنما أرشدها إلى ما هو أيسر، ولو كان مكروهاً لبين ذلك، ثم هذا الحديث ونحوه مما يشهد باتخاذ المسبحة المعروفة لإحصاء عدد الأذكار؛ إذ لا تزيد المسبحة إلا بضم النوى ونحوه في خيط، ومثل ذلك لا يظهر تأثيره في المنع ، ولهذا نقل اتخاذها والعمل بها عن جماعة من الصوفية الأخيار وغيرهم اللهم إلا أن يترتب عليها رياء وسمعة. (فتح) والتسبيح باليد في الصلاة ولو نفلا أما باللسان فمفسد وبرؤوس الأصابع والقلب لا يكره كخارج الصلاة. (ع)
And counting verses and tasbih, not killing the snake and scorpion... (then after image discussion) And counting the verses: āy is plural of āyah, i.e., verses of the Qur'an. And they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: There is no harm with the hand. Then it was said: There is no dispute in supererogatory (nafl) that it is not disliked, and the dispute is in obligatory (fard). It was said: It is disliked in fard by consensus, and the dispute is in nawafil. The most apparent is that the dispute applies to all. And it is not disliked outside prayer in the correct view, because it calms the heart and attracts activity. And because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered upon a woman and before her were date pits or she was counting tasbih with them, and he said: "Shall I tell you of what is easier for you than this and better?" He did not forbid her from it, but only guided her to what is easier. Had it been disliked, he would have explained that. Then this hadith and similar ones attest to using the known misbaḥah (prayer beads) for counting dhikr, as the misbaḥah only adds pits and the like on a string, and such does not show any effect in prevention. Hence, its usage has been transmitted from a group of righteous Sufis and others, unless it leads to riyā' and sum'ah (showing off). (Fath) And tasbih with the hand in prayer, even in nafl, but with the tongue it invalidates, and with fingertips and heart it is not disliked, as outside prayer. (Ayn)
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on counting Qur'anic verses (āyāt) or tasbīḥ (glorifications) during prayer. The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) say there is no harm in counting with the hand (i.e., using fingers) during prayer. Abu Hanifa's view is that it is disliked in fard prayers, but some say the difference applies only to fard, while others extend it to nafl. The relied-upon position is that counting with the hand is disliked in both fard and nafl, but outside prayer it is not disliked. Evidence includes the hadith where the Prophet saw a woman counting on date pits and did not forbid her, only guided to something better. This indicates it is not haram or makruh, but merely that a better method exists. The use of prayer beads (misbaḥah) is thus permissible, though caution should be exercised against ostentation. Counting with the tongue out loud invalidates prayer; with fingertips or heart is not disliked.

Key Terms
عد الآي (ʿadd al-āyī): Counting the number of recited verses during prayer.
التسبيح باليد (al-tasbīḥ bi al-yad): Counting glorifications (subhanallah etc.) using fingers or prayer beads.
لا بأس (lā ba'sa): There is no harm – a term indicating permissibility (ibāḥah) or absence of prohibition.
مسبحة (misbaḥah): Prayer beads used for counting dhikr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi ruling on counting tasbih with the hand during a nafl prayer?
A) It is recommended (mandūb).
B) It is disliked (makruh tanzih).
C) It is prohibited (haram).
D) It is permissible without dislike.

Key Takeaway
Counting tasbih with the hand in prayer is disliked (makruh tanzih) according to the mufta bihi, but outside prayer it is permissible and even beneficial.

Killing snakes, scorpions, and praying behind a talking person
Ruling with evidence and conditional clarifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing dangerous animals during prayer and identify the condition that changes the ruling from permissible to disliked.

Core Idea
Killing a snake in prayer is permissible if you fear harm; otherwise it is disliked — the Prophet's command implies permissibility, but intention matters.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two practical concerns in prayer: dealing with dangerous animals like snakes and scorpions, and the etiquette of praying behind a seated person who is talking. The Hanafi school balances the authority of the Prophetic command with the need for concentration in prayer, making the ruling conditional on fear of harm. The passage also clarifies that killing with many actions does not invalidate prayer, and that jinn snakes may have a different ruling due to a covenant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is killing a snake or scorpion during prayer. What is the initial ruling? The text says 'not killing' (la qatl) and then explains the proof.
The Arabic begins with 'la qatl', which may be read as 'it is not prohibited to kill'.
2
Locate the dalil
The source is a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered killing the rabid dog, snake, and scorpion even in prayer. Identify the type of dalil (Sunnah ahad) and its epistemological weight (zanni al-thubut).
3
Analyze the dalil
The command (amr) indicates at minimum permissibility (ibahah) in Hanafi usul. The phrase 'even in prayer' shows that this act is allowed during worship, overriding the normal prohibition of unnecessary movement.
Compare with Shafi'i usul where amr indicates obligation unless diverted.
4
Apply the condition
The permissibility is conditioned on fear of harm. If the snake passes in front and the worshipper fears harm, it is mubah. If no fear, it becomes makruh tanzih because it disturbs concentration unnecessarily.
Also note the jinn snake debate: some say jinn snakes should not be killed due to a covenant, but others argue they break the covenant by appearing.
5
Extend to other cases
The passage extends the ruling to lice and fleas: permissible if harmful, otherwise taking them is disliked. Also, Sarakhsi states that killing with many actions does not invalidate prayer. Finally, the second part: praying behind a seated talking person — if the talk is quiet, it is not disliked; if loud enough to cause fear of error in prayer, it becomes disliked.
The text ends abruptly, but the ruling is clear from context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا قتل الحية والعقرب لما ورد أنه عليه السلام أمر بقتل الكلب العقور والحية والعقرب : الصلاة أيضاً، وأقل مراتب الأمر الإباحة، ولا يكره قتلهما مطلقاً، سواء كانت جنية أو غيرها؛ لأنه عليه السلام عاهد الجن أن لا يدخلوا بيوت أمته، وأن لا يظهروا أنفسهم، فإذا خالفوا فقد نقضوا عهدهم، فلا حرمة لهم، وقيل: لا يحل قتل الجنية؛ لقوله عليا: "اقتلوا ذا الطفيتين والأبتر، وإياكم والحية البيضاء، فإنها من الجن"، ولا باس بقتل القمل والبرغوث إذا تعرضت له بالأذى، فإن لم تتعرض كره له الأخذ وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي أنه إذا قتل الحية بعمل كثير لا تفسد صلاته، وقالوا: إنما يباح قتلها في الصلاة إذا مرت بين يديه وخاف الأذى منها، وإن لم يخف يكره. (فتح، مسكين) قاعد يتحدّث : أي سراً بحيث لا يخاف منه إغلاط في الصلاة، فلو رفع بالحديث بحيث يخاف المصلي أن يزل =
Not killing the snake and scorpion, because it has been reported that he (peace be upon him) ordered killing the rabid dog, snake, and scorpion even in prayer. The minimum rank of an order is permissibility, so killing them is not disliked absolutely, whether they are jinn or otherwise; because he (peace be upon him) made a covenant with the jinn not to enter the houses of his ummah and not to show themselves; so if they violate, they have broken their covenant, thus they have no sanctity. And it is said: It is not permissible to kill the jinn snake, due to his saying: "Kill the one with two streaks and the tailless, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn." And there is no harm in killing lice and fleas if they cause harm; if they do not, then taking them is disliked. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that if one kills a snake with many actions, his prayer is not invalidated. They said: Killing it is only permissible in prayer if it passes in front of him and he fears harm; if he does not fear, it is disliked. (Fath, Miskin) A person sitting and talking: i.e., quietly so that the worshipper does not fear making mistakes in prayer; if he raises his voice such that the worshipper fears slipping (into error), then...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: killing dangerous animals during prayer, and praying behind a seated talking person. Regarding snakes and scorpions, the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered killing them even during prayer. An order implies at least permissibility (ibahah), so it is not disliked to kill them. This includes snakes that are jinn (i.e., appearing as snakes), though some reports differentiate: snakes with two streaks or tailless are to be killed, but the white snake (a type of jinn) is to be avoided. The ruling is permissive when there is fear of harm; if no fear, it is disliked. Killing with many actions does not invalidate the prayer. As for praying towards the back of a seated person who is talking quietly, it is not disliked, as long as the worshipper does not fear making mistakes due to the talking. However, if the talk is loud and causes fear of error, it becomes disliked.

Key Terms
الحية (al-ḥayyah): Snake, includes both ordinary and jinn snakes.
العقرب (al-ʿaqrab): Scorpion.
الإباحة (al-ibāḥah): Permissibility; the minimum implication of a command in Hanafi usul.
جنية (jinniyyah): Jinn snake; a snake that is believed to be a jinn in form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always permissible regardless of fear.
B) Only if it is a jinn snake.
C) If it passes in front and the worshipper fears harm.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
Killing a snake or scorpion in prayer is mubah if there is fear of harm; otherwise it is makruh tanzih — the Prophet's command establishes permissibility, but the presence or absence of danger modifies the ruling.

Images in Salah: The Hanafi Exception Rule
The passage states the ruling and exceptions for images in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images during prayer and identify the three exceptions that remove the dislike.

Core Idea
Images in prayer are disliked unless small, headless, or inanimate — because only complete animate forms distract from worship.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with commentaries from al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir, explains the Hanafi ruling on images in the presence of a praying person. The core principle is that any image that might be worshipped as an idol is disliked, but exceptions apply when the image is not treated as an object of devotion. You will learn the specific conditions that remove the karahah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is having an image above, in front, or beside the praying person. The default ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked).
The ruling is based on a hadith about angels not entering houses with images.
2
Locate the three exceptions
The passage lists three exceptions: small images (where details are not clearly visible), headless images, and images of inanimate objects (e.g., trees, stars).
Each exception removes the dislike because the image is not considered an object of worship.
3
Understand the rationale
The dislike is tied to the possibility of the image being worshipped. Small images are not typically worshipped, headless images lack the complete form, and inanimate objects are never objects of worship.
This rationale is supported by the practice of the Prophet's companions, as seen in the rings of Abu Huraira and Daniel.
4
Apply the hierarchy of dislike
The strongest dislike is when the image is in front of the praying person, then above his head, then beside him, then behind him.
The position affects the degree of distraction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن يكون فوق رأسه أو بين يديه أو بحذائه صورة، إلا أن تكون صغيرةً أو مقطوعة الرأس أو لغير ذي روح. فوق رأسه أي في السقف مقتضاه عدم الكراهة إذا كانت تحت رجليه أو في محل جلوسه؛ لأنها مهانة، ولكن يكره كراهة جعل الصورة في البيت لخبر، لا تدخل الملائكة بيتاً فيه كلب ولا صورة وأشدها الكراهة أن تكون أمام مصلي ثم فوق رأسه ثم بحذائه ثم خلفه [تبيين الحقائق: ٤١٤/١] بين يديه بأن تكون معلقة أو موضوعة صغيرة: بحيث لا تبدو للناظر إلا بالتأمل؛ لأن الكراهة باعتبار العبادة والصغيرة لا تعبد عادة. (ع) لما روي أن خاتم أبي هريرة كان عليه ذبابتان وخاتم دانيال كان عليه أسد ولبوة وبينهما رجل يلحسانه والمراد بالصغيرة أن تكون بحال لو كانت على الأرض والناظر واقف لا يرى تفاصيل أعضائها. (فتح) أو مقطوعة الرأس لأنها لا تعبد بدون الرأس. [رمز الحقائق: ٧٦/١] لغير ذي روح كالشجرة والثمرة والكواكب ونحوها؛ لأنها لا تعبد. (ط)
And that there be an image above his head, or in front of him, or beside him, unless it is small, or headless, or of something without a soul. Above his head: meaning in the ceiling, its implication is that it is not disliked if it is under his feet or in his sitting place because it is degraded, but it is disliked as a degree of dislike to place an image in the house due to the report 'Angels do not enter a house that has a dog or an image,' and the strongest dislike is that it be in front of a praying person, then above his head, then beside him, then behind him. In front of him: meaning it is hung or placed, small: such that it does not appear to the viewer except upon reflection, because dislike is in consideration of worship, and small ones are not usually worshipped. It is narrated that the ring of Abu Huraira had two flies on it, and the ring of Daniel had a lion and lioness and between them a man licking them, and the meaning of 'small' is that if it were on the ground and the viewer was standing, he would not see the details of its limbs. Or headless because without a head it is not worshipped. For something without a soul, like a tree, fruit, stars, and the like; because they are not worshipped.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on images during prayer. The main text states it is disliked to have an image above, in front, or beside the praying person, with three exceptions: if the image is small (where details are not clearly visible), headless, or of a non-living thing. The commentator explains that the dislike is based on the hadith that angels do not enter houses with dogs or images. The strongest dislike is when the image is in front, then above, then beside, then behind. Small images that are not clearly detailed are not disliked because they are not typically worshipped. The examples of the rings of Abu Huraira and Daniel prove that small images were permitted. Headless images are also excluded as they cannot be worshipped. Images of trees, fruits, stars etc. are also not disliked. The ruling is derived from the principle that any image that distracts from worship or invites association with Allah is disliked, but exceptions apply when the image is not treated as an object of worship.

Key Terms
صورة (surah): An image or picture, especially of a living being.
كراهة (karahah): Dislike (tanzihi) — an act that is reprehensible but not sinful.
مقطوعة الرأس (maqtu'at al-ra's): An image that has its head cut off, which removes the ability to be worshipped.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a praying person has a small image in front of him that is not clearly detailed?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Permissible (la ba's)
D) Wajib to remove

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits small, headless, and inanimate images in prayer, basing this on the principle that only images prone to worship are disliked.

Counting Verses and Tasbih During Prayer
Rulings on counting verses and tasbih during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting verses and tasbih during prayer and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Counting verses with hand during obligatory prayer is disliked; the Sahibayn permit it, and the easier view is preferred.

This lesson addresses two related actions: counting the number of verses recited and performing tasbih (saying Subhanallah) during prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between doing so with the hand, tongue, or heart, and between obligatory and supererogatory prayers. A hadith of the Prophet with a woman counting on date pits provides the primary proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the section on 'counting of verses' (عد الآي). Note that Abu Hanifa considers it disliked (makruh) in obligatory prayer, while the Sahibayn see no harm.
2
Understand the dispute scope
The text mentions different opinions on whether the dispute applies to obligatory or supererogatory prayers. The preferred view is that it applies to both.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The Prophet did not forbid the woman from counting with pits; he only guided her to something easier. This indicates permissibility, not dislike.
The Hanafi response: if it were disliked, the Prophet would have made it clear.
4
Apply to tasbih and prayer beads
Tasbih with the hand in prayer is permissible; with the tongue it invalidates; with fingertips or heart it is not disliked. Outside prayer, counting and using prayer beads is recommended.
The text notes that prayer beads are permissible unless they lead to ostentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعد الآي: الآي جمع آية، أي آيات القرآن وقالا: لا بأس باليد ثم قيل: لا خلاف في التطوع أنه لا يكره والخلاف في الفرض، وقيل: كره في الفرض إجماعاً، والخلاف في النوافل، والأظهر أن الخلاف في الكل، ولا يكره العد خارج الصلاة في الصحيح؛ لأنه أسكن للقلب وأجلب للنشاط؛ ولما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام دخل على امرأة وبين يديها نوى أو تسبح به، فقال: 'حصى؟ أخبرك بما هو أيسر عليك من هذا وأفضل'، فلم ينهها عن ذلك، وإنما أرشدها إلى ما هو أيسر، ولو كان مكروهاً لبين ذلك، ثم هذا الحديث ونحوه مما يشهد باتخاذ المسبحة المعروفة لإحصاء عدد الأذكار؛ إذ لا تزيد المسبحة إلا بضم النوى ونحوه في خيط، ومثل ذلك لا يظهر تأثيره في المنع، ولهذا نقل اتخاذها والعمل بها عن جماعة من الصوفية الأخيار وغيرهم اللهم إلا أن يترتب عليها رياء وسمعة. (فتح) والتسبيح باليد في الصلاة ولو نفلا أما باللسان فمفسد وبرؤوس الأصابع والقلب لا يكره كخارج الصلاة. (ع) لا قتل الحية والعقرب لما ورد أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر بقتل الكلب العقور والحية والعقرب في الصلاة أيضاً، وأقل مراتب الأمر الإباحة، ولا يكره قتلهما مطلقاً، سواء كانت جنية أو غيرها؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام عاهد الجن أن لا يدخلوا بيوت أمته، وأن لا يظهروا أنفسهم، فإذا خالفوا فقد نقضوا عهدهم، فلا حرمة لهم، وقيل: لا يحل قتل الجنية؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'اقتلوا ذا الطفيتين والأبتر، وإياكم والحية البيضاء، فإنها من الجن'، ولا بأس بقتل القمل والبرغوث إذا تعرضت له بالأذى، فإن لم تتعرض كره له الأخذ وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي أنه إذا قتل الحية بعمل كثير لا تفسد صلاته، وقالوا: إنما يباح قتلها في الصلاة إذا مرت بين يديه وخاف الأذى منها، وإن لم يخف يكره. (فتح، مسكين) قاعد يتحدث: أي سراً بحيث لا يخاف منه إغلاط في الصلاة، فلو رفع بالحديث بحيث يخاف المصلي أن يزل في القراءة فحينئذ يكره، وقيد بالظهر؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان إذا أراد أن يصلي أمر عكرمة أن يجلس بين يديه ويصلي، وكذا لو كان بين يدي المصلي نائم، فإن كان بحيث لو ظهر منه صوت يضحك من هو في صلاته، أو يخجل النائم إذا انتبه يكره، وإن أمن من ذلك فلا بأس؛ لحديث عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها كانت نائمة بين يدي رسول الله وهو يصلي، ولو صلى إلى وجه إنسان وبينهما ثالث ظهره إلى وجه المصلي لا يكره، ومن المكروهات: أن يصلي مكشوف الرأس للتكاسل وعدم المبالاة لا للتذلل، ومنها: إتمام القراءة راكعاً، والقراءة في غير حالة القيام، وحمل صبي، وأما حمله عليه الصلاة والسلام لأمامة بنت زينب فقيل: منسوخ. (فتح) وإلى مصحف، أو سيف معلق أو شمع، أو سراج، أو على بساط فيه تصاوير أي ولا تكره أيضا إن لم يسجد عليها.
And the counting of verses: Al-ayi is the plural of ayah, meaning verses of the Quran, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: there is no harm with the hand. Then it was said: there is no dispute regarding supererogatory prayers that it is not disliked, and the dispute is regarding obligatory prayers. And it was said: it is disliked in obligatory prayers by consensus, and the dispute is in supererogatory prayers. The more apparent is that the dispute applies to all. And counting outside prayer is not disliked according to the sound view because it settles the heart and invites activity. And it is narrated that the Prophet entered upon a woman and in front of her were date pits or she was counting with them, so he said: 'Pebbles? Shall I inform you of what is easier for you and better?' and he did not forbid her from that, but only guided her to what is easier. If it were disliked, he would have clarified that. Then this hadith and similar ones testify to the use of the well-known prayer beads for counting dhikr, since the prayer beads are no more than joining pits or the like on a string, and such a thing does not appear to have an effect in prohibition. For this reason, its use and practice has been narrated from a group of righteous Sufis and others, unless it leads to ostentation and reputation. And tasbih with the hand in prayer, even in supererogatory, while with the tongue it nullifies, and with the fingertips and the heart it is not disliked, like outside prayer. The killing of the snake and scorpion: because it is narrated that the Prophet commanded the killing of the rabid dog, snake, and scorpion even during prayer, and the least level of a command is permission. It is not disliked to kill them absolutely, whether they are jinn or not, because the Prophet made a covenant with the jinn that they would not enter the houses of his nation nor show themselves. If they violate, they have broken their covenant, so they have no sanctity. It is said that it is not permissible to kill the female jinn due to his saying: 'Kill the two-horned and the tailless, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn.' There is no harm in killing lice and fleas if they cause harm; if they do not, it is disliked to take them. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that if one kills the snake with many actions, his prayer is not invalidated. They said: it is only permissible to kill it in prayer if it passes in front of him and he fears harm from it; if not, it is disliked. A seated person talking: meaning quietly such that one does not fear mistakes in prayer. If he raises his voice such that the praying person fears making an error in recitation, then it is disliked. It is restricted to the back because the Prophet used to command 'Ikrimah to sit in front of him and pray. Similarly, if there is a sleeping person in front of the praying person: if such that a sound from him would make the one in prayer laugh or embarrass the sleeper when he wakes, it is disliked. If safe from that, there is no harm due to the hadith of 'A'ishah that she was sleeping in front of the Messenger of Allah while he was praying. If one prays towards the face of a person with a third person between them whose back is to the praying person's face, it is not disliked. Among the disliked actions: praying with head uncovered out of laziness and carelessness, not out of humility; completing recitation while bowing; reciting in a non-standing position; carrying a child. As for his carrying Umamah bint Zayn, it is said to be abrogated. And towards a Mushaf, or a suspended sword, or a candle, or a lamp, or on a rug with images: meaning that it is also not disliked if he does not prostrate on it.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage compiles several rulings on actions that may be disliked or permissible during prayer. The first issue is counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) see no harm in using the hand for counting, while Abu Hanifa considers it disliked. The commentator notes that the dispute applies to obligatory prayers, but for supererogatory prayers there is less concern. Outside of prayer, counting is not disliked and is even beneficial for concentration. The hadith of the woman counting with pits shows that the Prophet did not forbid it, indicating permissibility. The use of prayer beads is thus allowed as long as it does not lead to ostentation. Tasbih with the hand during prayer is permissible; doing so with the tongue invalidates the prayer, while using fingertips or the heart is not disliked. Second, killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is allowed, especially if the creature poses a threat. The Prophet commanded killing them even in prayer, and the command indicates permission. Some differentiate between jinn and non-jinn snakes, but the preferred view is that all such dangerous creatures can be killed. Killing lice or fleas is only permissible if they cause harm. Third, having a seated person talking behind the praying person is disliked if the talk is loud enough to distract or cause mistakes. However, if the person is quiet or sleeping, it is not necessarily disliked. The hadith of 'A'ishah and the example of 'Ikrimah show that having a person in front is not inherently disliked. Additional disliked actions include praying with head uncovered out of laziness, completing recitation while bowing, reciting while not standing, and carrying a child. Finally, praying towards a Mushaf, a suspended sword, a candle, a lamp, or a rug with images is not disliked as long as one does not prostrate on the images, since prostrating on them would be showing reverence.

Key Terms
عد الآي (addu al-ayi): Counting the number of verses recited during prayer, typically with the hand or fingers.
تسبيح (tasbih): Saying 'Subhanallah' or the like during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on tasbih with the tongue during prayer?
A) Permissible
B) Disliked
C) It nullifies the prayer
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Counting verses with the hand during prayer is not inherently prohibited; the Hanafi school permits it, preferring ease over strictness.

Killing Snakes and Scorpions During Prayer
Ruling on killing dangerous creatures during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing dangerous creatures during prayer and apply the condition of fear of harm.

Core Idea
Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is permissible if one fears harm; otherwise it is disliked.

What if a dangerous creature appears while you are praying? The Hanafi school derives the ruling from the Prophet's command to kill snakes and scorpions even during prayer. This lesson examines the conditions and exceptions, including the difference between harmful and harmless creatures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the creatures covered
The text specifically mentions the snake (حية), scorpion (عقرب), and rabid dog (كلب عقور). Also discusses lice and fleas.
2
Determine the general ruling
The Prophet's command to kill these creatures even in prayer indicates permission. The lowest level of a command (أمر) is ibaha (permissibility).
3
Apply the condition of fear
The permissibility is conditional on fear of harm. If the snake passes in front and one fears its harm, killing is permissible. Without fear, it becomes disliked.
4
Address the jinn snake issue
Some narrations distinguish between ordinary snakes and those that are jinn. The Hanafi view is that all dangerous snakes can be killed, as jinn who break the covenant have no sanctity.
There is a counter-narration warning about the white snake from jinn, but the dominant view permits killing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعد الآي: الآي جمع آية، أي آيات القرآن وقالا: لا بأس باليد ثم قيل: لا خلاف في التطوع أنه لا يكره والخلاف في الفرض، وقيل: كره في الفرض إجماعاً، والخلاف في النوافل، والأظهر أن الخلاف في الكل، ولا يكره العد خارج الصلاة في الصحيح؛ لأنه أسكن للقلب وأجلب للنشاط؛ ولما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام دخل على امرأة وبين يديها نوى أو تسبح به، فقال: 'حصى؟ أخبرك بما هو أيسر عليك من هذا وأفضل'، فلم ينهها عن ذلك، وإنما أرشدها إلى ما هو أيسر، ولو كان مكروهاً لبين ذلك، ثم هذا الحديث ونحوه مما يشهد باتخاذ المسبحة المعروفة لإحصاء عدد الأذكار؛ إذ لا تزيد المسبحة إلا بضم النوى ونحوه في خيط، ومثل ذلك لا يظهر تأثيره في المنع، ولهذا نقل اتخاذها والعمل بها عن جماعة من الصوفية الأخيار وغيرهم اللهم إلا أن يترتب عليها رياء وسمعة. (فتح) والتسبيح باليد في الصلاة ولو نفلا أما باللسان فمفسد وبرؤوس الأصابع والقلب لا يكره كخارج الصلاة. (ع) لا قتل الحية والعقرب لما ورد أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر بقتل الكلب العقور والحية والعقرب في الصلاة أيضاً، وأقل مراتب الأمر الإباحة، ولا يكره قتلهما مطلقاً، سواء كانت جنية أو غيرها؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام عاهد الجن أن لا يدخلوا بيوت أمته، وأن لا يظهروا أنفسهم، فإذا خالفوا فقد نقضوا عهدهم، فلا حرمة لهم، وقيل: لا يحل قتل الجنية؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'اقتلوا ذا الطفيتين والأبتر، وإياكم والحية البيضاء، فإنها من الجن'، ولا بأس بقتل القمل والبرغوث إذا تعرضت له بالأذى، فإن لم تتعرض كره له الأخذ وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي أنه إذا قتل الحية بعمل كثير لا تفسد صلاته، وقالوا: إنما يباح قتلها في الصلاة إذا مرت بين يديه وخاف الأذى منها، وإن لم يخف يكره. (فتح، مسكين) قاعد يتحدث: أي سراً بحيث لا يخاف منه إغلاط في الصلاة، فلو رفع بالحديث بحيث يخاف المصلي أن يزل في القراءة فحينئذ يكره، وقيد بالظهر؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان إذا أراد أن يصلي أمر عكرمة أن يجلس بين يديه ويصلي، وكذا لو كان بين يدي المصلي نائم، فإن كان بحيث لو ظهر منه صوت يضحك من هو في صلاته، أو يخجل النائم إذا انتبه يكره، وإن أمن من ذلك فلا بأس؛ لحديث عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها كانت نائمة بين يدي رسول الله وهو يصلي، ولو صلى إلى وجه إنسان وبينهما ثالث ظهره إلى وجه المصلي لا يكره، ومن المكروهات: أن يصلي مكشوف الرأس للتكاسل وعدم المبالاة لا للتذلل، ومنها: إتمام القراءة راكعاً، والقراءة في غير حالة القيام، وحمل صبي، وأما حمله عليه الصلاة والسلام لأمامة بنت زينب فقيل: منسوخ. (فتح) وإلى مصحف، أو سيف معلق أو شمع، أو سراج، أو على بساط فيه تصاوير أي ولا تكره أيضا إن لم يسجد عليها.
And the counting of verses: Al-ayi is the plural of ayah, meaning verses of the Quran, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: there is no harm with the hand. Then it was said: there is no dispute regarding supererogatory prayers that it is not disliked, and the dispute is regarding obligatory prayers. And it was said: it is disliked in obligatory prayers by consensus, and the dispute is in supererogatory prayers. The more apparent is that the dispute applies to all. And counting outside prayer is not disliked according to the sound view because it settles the heart and invites activity. And it is narrated that the Prophet entered upon a woman and in front of her were date pits or she was counting with them, so he said: 'Pebbles? Shall I inform you of what is easier for you and better?' and he did not forbid her from that, but only guided her to what is easier. If it were disliked, he would have clarified that. Then this hadith and similar ones testify to the use of the well-known prayer beads for counting dhikr, since the prayer beads are no more than joining pits or the like on a string, and such a thing does not appear to have an effect in prohibition. For this reason, its use and practice has been narrated from a group of righteous Sufis and others, unless it leads to ostentation and reputation. And tasbih with the hand in prayer, even in supererogatory, while with the tongue it nullifies, and with the fingertips and the heart it is not disliked, like outside prayer. The killing of the snake and scorpion: because it is narrated that the Prophet commanded the killing of the rabid dog, snake, and scorpion even during prayer, and the least level of a command is permission. It is not disliked to kill them absolutely, whether they are jinn or not, because the Prophet made a covenant with the jinn that they would not enter the houses of his nation nor show themselves. If they violate, they have broken their covenant, so they have no sanctity. It is said that it is not permissible to kill the female jinn due to his saying: 'Kill the two-horned and the tailless, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn.' There is no harm in killing lice and fleas if they cause harm; if they do not, it is disliked to take them. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that if one kills the snake with many actions, his prayer is not invalidated. They said: it is only permissible to kill it in prayer if it passes in front of him and he fears harm from it; if not, it is disliked. A seated person talking: meaning quietly such that one does not fear mistakes in prayer. If he raises his voice such that the praying person fears making an error in recitation, then it is disliked. It is restricted to the back because the Prophet used to command 'Ikrimah to sit in front of him and pray. Similarly, if there is a sleeping person in front of the praying person: if such that a sound from him would make the one in prayer laugh or embarrass the sleeper when he wakes, it is disliked. If safe from that, there is no harm due to the hadith of 'A'ishah that she was sleeping in front of the Messenger of Allah while he was praying. If one prays towards the face of a person with a third person between them whose back is to the praying person's face, it is not disliked. Among the disliked actions: praying with head uncovered out of laziness and carelessness, not out of humility; completing recitation while bowing; reciting in a non-standing position; carrying a child. As for his carrying Umamah bint Zayn, it is said to be abrogated. And towards a Mushaf, or a suspended sword, or a candle, or a lamp, or on a rug with images: meaning that it is also not disliked if he does not prostrate on it.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage compiles several rulings on actions that may be disliked or permissible during prayer. The first issue is counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) see no harm in using the hand for counting, while Abu Hanifa considers it disliked. The commentator notes that the dispute applies to obligatory prayers, but for supererogatory prayers there is less concern. Outside of prayer, counting is not disliked and is even beneficial for concentration. The hadith of the woman counting with pits shows that the Prophet did not forbid it, indicating permissibility. The use of prayer beads is thus allowed as long as it does not lead to ostentation. Tasbih with the hand during prayer is permissible; doing so with the tongue invalidates the prayer, while using fingertips or the heart is not disliked. Second, killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is allowed, especially if the creature poses a threat. The Prophet commanded killing them even in prayer, and the command indicates permission. Some differentiate between jinn and non-jinn snakes, but the preferred view is that all such dangerous creatures can be killed. Killing lice or fleas is only permissible if they cause harm. Third, having a seated person talking behind the praying person is disliked if the talk is loud enough to distract or cause mistakes. However, if the person is quiet or sleeping, it is not necessarily disliked. The hadith of 'A'ishah and the example of 'Ikrimah show that having a person in front is not inherently disliked. Additional disliked actions include praying with head uncovered out of laziness, completing recitation while bowing, reciting while not standing, and carrying a child. Finally, praying towards a Mushaf, a suspended sword, a candle, a lamp, or a rug with images is not disliked as long as one does not prostrate on the images, since prostrating on them would be showing reverence.

Key Terms
قتل الحية والعقرب (qatl al-hayyah wa al-aqrab): Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer.
الكلب العقور (al-kalb al-aquur): A rabid dog that attacks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a snake appears during prayer and the worshipper does not fear harm from it?
A) Killing is permissible
B) Killing is disliked
C) Killing is prohibited
D) Prayer becomes invalid if he kills it

Key Takeaway
Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is permitted if one fears harm, and the prayer remains valid.

Prayer Direction and Other Disliked Acts
Rulings on prayer direction and miscellaneous disliked acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which having a seated or sleeping person in front of the praying person is disliked, and list other disliked actions during prayer.

Core Idea
Having a person talking or sleeping in front of you during prayer is not disliked unless it causes distraction and potential error.

This lesson covers several scenarios related to the space in front of the worshipper and other minor disliked acts. The key principle is that what does not distract or cause error is permissible, while anything that leads to potential mistake or disrespect is discouraged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of a seated person
The text discusses a person sitting in front of the praying person and talking. If the talk is quiet and does not cause fear of error in recitation, it is not disliked. If loud enough to cause fear, it becomes disliked.
2
Consider a sleeping person
Similarly, a sleeping person in front is not disliked if no sound or movement causes distraction or embarrassment. The hadith of 'A'ishah is cited as proof.
3
Evaluate other disliked acts
Listed: praying with head uncovered out of laziness, completing recitation while bowing, reciting in non-standing position, carrying a child. Each has specific evidence or reasoning.
4
Praying towards images or objects
Praying towards a Mushaf, sword, candle, lamp, or a rug with images is not disliked as long as one does not prostrate on the images.
Prostrating on images would show reverence to them, which is not allowed.

Closing the Mosque Door: When Dislike Becomes Permissible
Ruling on closing mosque doors with fatwa differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi ruling on closing the mosque door, explain why it is disliked, and identify the circumstances under which the fatwa permits it.

Core Idea
Closing the mosque door is originally disliked, but permissible when thieves threaten—fatwa follows necessity.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a common practical issue: may the mosque door be closed during non-prayer times? The matn states it is disliked because it resembles preventing people from prayer. However, the commentator expands on this, noting that due to widespread theft, the fatwa (operative ruling) has shifted to permissibility. You will learn how the Hanafi School balances original rulings against changing circumstances and security needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling and its reason
Read the first part: 'وغلق باب المسجد ... يكره'. The original position is that closing the door is makruh (disliked). The reason given is that it resembles preventing people from entering for prayer (يُشبه المنع من الصلوات).
The matn groups this with other disliked acts like treading on the roof.
2
Note the change due to time and necessity
The commentator then says 'وفي هذا الزمان لا يكره؛ لكثرة اللصوص'. In this era, it is not disliked because of many thieves. This is a clear example of fatwa adapting to circumstances.
The phrase 'عليه الفتوى' indicates the relied-upon position.
3
Distinguish between different opinions
Several opinions are cited: (1) It is permissible if there is fear for the mosque's belongings outside prayer times. (2) It is not closed when prayer times are close (e.g., Asr to Maghrib), but may be closed from Isha to Fajr and from sunrise to zawal.
These are intra-Hanafi differences; the fatwa may vary by context.
4
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text states 'وعليه الفتوى' after the permissibility view due to thieves. This is the fatwa given for practice.
The later authorities (mutakhkhirin) favour permissibility with conditions.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a mosque in a high-crime area. The imam wants to lock the door between Isha and Fajr to prevent theft. Using this ruling, it is permissible (not even disliked) because of necessity. However, during overlapping prayer times (e.g., just before Jumu'ah), the door should remain open.
The ruling hinges on the presence of genuine fear and the time period.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغلق باب المسجد والوطء فوقه والبول والتخلي لا فوق بيتٍ فيه مسجد، أي كن، كذا يكره. وغلق باب المسجد الأنه يشبه المنع من الصلوات وفي هذا الزمان لا يكره؛ لكثرة اللصوص، وعليه الفتوى. (ع) وقيل: لا بأس به إذا خيف على متاع المسجد في غير أوان الصلاة، وعليه الفتوى، وقيل: إذا تقارب الوقتان كالعصر والمغرب والعشاء لا يغلق، وبعد العشاء إلى الفجر، ومن طلوع الشمس إلى الزوال يغلق. (فتح)
And closing the door of the mosque and treading on top of it and urination and relieving oneself not above a house in which there is a mosque, i.e., whatever, thus it is disliked. And closing the door of the mosque because it resembles prevention from prayers, and in this time it is not disliked due to the abundance of thieves, and upon it is the fatwa. (ع) And it was said: There is no harm in it if the mosque's belongings are feared upon outside the time of prayer, and upon it is the fatwa. And it was said: When the two times are close, like Asr and Maghrib and Isha, it is not closed, and after Isha until Fajr, and from sunrise until zawal it is closed. (فتح)
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on closing the mosque door. The matn states that closing the door of the mosque, along with other acts like treading on top, urination, and defecation, is disliked if done above a house that contains a mosque. The commentator then focuses on the specific issue of closing the door. Originally, it is makruh (disliked) because it resembles preventing people from entering for prayer. However, in this era due to the risk of theft, the fatwa is that it is not makruh. Another opinion says it is permissible (no harm) if there is fear for the mosque's property outside prayer times. A third opinion distinguishes between times: if the prayer times are close together (e.g., Asr, Maghrib, Isha), the door should not be closed; between Isha and Fajr and from sunrise to midday, it may be closed. The relied-upon fatwa varies according to circumstances, with the majority preferring the permissibility due to security concerns.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): Disliked act (makruh tanzih or tahrimi) in Hanafi fiqh, meaning something whose prohibition is not established with certainty.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The operative ruling given for practice, which may differ from the original legal position due to changing circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage say that in this time (the commentator's era) closing the mosque door is not disliked?
A) Because the mosque door is no longer needed
B) Because of the abundance of thieves, necessitating protection
C) Because people pray at home now
D) Because the ruling is abrogated

Key Takeaway
The Hamafi School's ruling on closing the mosque door shifts from disliked to permissible when necessity (such as theft) overrides the original reason for dislike.

beginner

Treading and Urination in the Mosque
Rulings on treading and urination in the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on treading on top of a mosque and on urination inside it, and identify the recommended action regarding footwear.

Core Idea
Treading on a mosque roof is disliked; urination is disliked even in a vessel.

This lesson addresses two specific acts that may occur in or on a mosque: treading on the roof or floor, and urination. The text establishes that both are disliked (makruh), with treading on top being less severe than inside. Additionally, it reminds us of the importance of checking one's footwear for impurity before entering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the phrase 'والوطء فوقه ففي داخله بالأولى'. This tells us that treading on top of the mosque is disliked, and even more so inside the mosque.
The comparative 'بالأولى' indicates a gradation: if outside is disliked, inside is more so.
2
Examine the urination ruling
Find 'وكره البول ولو في إناء'. This states that urination is disliked (makruh), even if done into a vessel.
The phrase 'ولو في إناء' emphasizes that even indirect urination is disliked, showing the sanctity of the mosque.
3
Note the recommended action
Read 'وينبغي لداخل المسجد أن يتعاهد نعله وخفه عن النجاسة'. This recommends (yambaghi) that those entering the mosque should check their sandals and leather socks for impurity.
This is a sunnah, not wajib, but it shows care for the mosque's purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوطء فوقه ففي داخله بالأولى، وكره البول ولو في إناء، وينبغي لداخل المسجد أن يتعاهد نعله وخفه عن النجاسة، واختلف في كراهة إخراج الريح فيه والمراد من التخلي التغوط، وقيل: الخلوة بالمرأة، ولم يذكر المصنف كراهة البول والمجامعة في مصلى الجنازة، قال بعض أصحابنا يكره كما في المساجد التي على القوارع عند الحياض، والأصح أنه ليس له حرمة المسجد كمصلى العيد، والمختار للفتوى في مصلى الجنازة والعيد أنه مسجد في حق جواز الاقتداء، وفي ماعدا ذلك ليس له حكم المسجد. (فتح) فوقه أي فوق المسجد؛ لأن سطحه مسجد ولهذا يصح الاقتداء منه بمن فيه. (ع) لا فوق بيت إلخ: التقييد بـ"فوق" اتفاقي؛ لجواز المجامعة ودخول الجنب والحائض في مسجد البيت من غير كراهة، بخلاف سقف المسجد، فإنه لا يحل لهما الوقوف عليه وكذا مباشرة النساء في المسجد حرام ودخول الصبيان والمجانين حيث يغلب تنجيسهم، وإلا فيكره، وقيل: دخول المسجد متنعلاً من سوء أدب. (فتح) مسجد أي للصلاة، وهو ليس بمسجد حقيقة حتى يجوز بيعه فلم يكن له حرمة المساجد. (ع)
And treading on top of it, so in its interior it is even more [disliked]. And he disliked urination even in a vessel. And it is recommended for the one entering the mosque to check his sandal and leather socks for impurity. And there is disagreement on the dislike of passing wind in it. And the meaning of 'takhalli' is defecation. And it was said: privacy with a woman. And the author did not mention the dislike of urination and intercourse in the janazah musalla. Some of our companions said it is disliked as in the mosques that are on the main roads near the tanks. And the correct view is that it does not have the sanctity of the mosque like the 'Id musalla. And the chosen for fatwa regarding the janazah and 'id musalla is that it is a mosque regarding the validity of following (iqtida'), and regarding other than that it does not have the ruling of a mosque. (Fath) Above it, i.e., above the mosque, because its roof is a mosque, and for this reason following from it to those inside is valid. ('Ayni) 'Not above a house...': The restriction to 'above' is coincidental; because it is permissible to have intercourse and for a junub or menstruating woman to enter a mosque that is part of a house without dislike, unlike the roof of a mosque, for it is not permissible for them to stand upon it. Similarly, direct contact with women in the mosque is forbidden. And the entry of children and insane people who often make impurity is disliked, otherwise it is disliked. And it was said: entering the mosque with shoes is bad manners. (Fath) A mosque, i.e., for prayer, and it is not a mosque in reality such that its sale is permissible, so it does not have the sanctity of mosques. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of disliked acts (makruhat) related to mosques. It covers several rulings: First, treading on top of the mosque is disliked, and even more so inside. Second, urination is disliked even if done in a vessel. Third, one entering the mosque should check his footwear for impurity. Fourth, passing wind in the mosque is subject to disagreement; the text does not settle it. Fifth, 'takhalli' (relieving oneself) is defined as defecation. Sixth, the author did not address the dislikeness of urination and intercourse in the janazah musalla (prayer area for funeral). Some Hanafi scholars say it is disliked just like in regular mosques, but the correct view is that the janazah musalla does not have the full sanctity (hurmah) of a mosque, similar to the 'id musalla. However, for the sake of following the imam (iqtida'), it is considered a mosque. The roof of a mosque is considered part of the mosque, so following the imam from the roof is valid. A house that contains a mosque within it: acts like intercourse and entering by a junub or menstruating woman are not disliked in the house area, but the actual mosque area (even the roof) has sanctity. Direct contact with women in the mosque is forbidden. Children and insane people whose impurity is dominant should not enter; otherwise it is disliked. Entering with shoes is bad manners. Finally, a mosque that is a prayer room (not a full masjid appointed for all prayers) is not considered a complete mosque with full sanctity, so its sale is permissible, and it does not have the same hurmah as a dedicated mosque.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-wat'): Treading, stepping, or walking upon something.
البول (al-bawl): Urination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on treading on the top of a mosque?
A) Permissible
B) Disliked
C) Forbidden
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Treading on a mosque roof and urination (even in a vessel) are disliked, while checking footwear for impurity is recommended.
